The Four Categories of Ignorance in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining ignorance and classifying its four types with legal effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of ignorance in Hanafi fiqh, apply the rule that ignorance in a place of doubt excuses, and distinguish false ignorance from excusable ignorance.

Core Idea
Ignorance excuses only when accompanied by genuine doubt or valid ijtihad, not when stemming from disbelief or negligence.

Ignorance is not a one-size-fits-all excuse in Hanafi law. This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir classifies ignorance into four types, ranging from false ignorance that never excuses to ignorance in matters of doubt that does. Understanding these categories is crucial for a mufti when assessing whether a party's ignorance affects validity, liability, or punishment. We will dissect the definition, types, and key applications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Definition
Start by parsing the definition of ignorance (jahl) as the absence of knowledge about something knowable. Distinguish simple (absence of knowledge) from compound (believing the opposite). This sets the foundation for the categories.
Compound ignorance is more severe because it includes a positive misbelief.
2
Identify the Four Categories
List the four types from the text: (1) false ignorance (jahl batil) – no excuse; (2) ignorance in a place of ijtihad/shubha – is an excuse; (3) ignorance in Dar al-Harb for a non-migrant Muslim – excuse; (4) attached ignorances – e.g., pre-emptor, slave woman, virgin, agent. Note what makes each category distinct.
The fourth category is considered an annex to the third.
3
Apply the Principle 'Ignorance Repels Invalidity'
The passage states at the end: 'ignorance is considered with us to repel invalidity' (الجهل معتبر عندنا لدفع الفساد). Take each furu' (example) – oath on dead person, slave woman's option, sale of hidden property, khul' claim, etc. – and confirm how ignorance changes the ruling.
This principle is not absolute; it applies only where the ignorance is genuine and not due to negligence.
4
Recognize Exceptions
The passage ends with a critical exception: uttering a word of kufr ignorantly – the majority rule that it is not excused. This shows that ignorance of foundational beliefs does not save one from apostasy. Also, false ignorance (type one) never excuses.
The exception for kufr is based on the principle that matters of belief require certainty.
5
Evaluate the Legal Effect
For each category, determine the legal consequence: exemption from liability, prevention of hadd, validity of contract, etc. For example, ignorance in a place of ijtihad prevents the hadd penalty for zina if there is a strong shubha.
The mufta bihi position in each furu' is mentioned; note which are relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجهل فحقيقته عدم العلم عما شأنه من العلم؛ فإن قارن اعتقاد النقيض فهو مركب، وهو المراد بالشعور بالشيء على خلاف ما هو به وإلا فبسيط، وهو المراد بعدم الشعور وأقسامه على ما ذكره الأصليون كما في المنار أربعة.
•
الأول : جهل باطل لا يصلح عذرًا في الآخرة كجهل الكافر بصفات الله تعالى وأحكام الآخرة، وجهل صاحب الهوى، وجهل الباغي حتى يضمن مال العدل إذا أتلفه، وجهل من خالف في اجتهاده الكتاب أو السُّنَّة المشهورة والإجماع كالفتوى ببيع أُمهات الأولاد. والثاني : الجهل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح أو في موضع الشبهة وأنه يصلح عذرًا وشبهة كالمحتجم إذا أفطر على ظن أنها فطرته وكمَن زنى بجارية والده أو زوجته على ظن أنها تحلّ له.
والثالث : الجهل في دار الحرب من مسلم لم يهاجر وأنه يكون عذرًا. ويلحق به الرابع : وهو جهل الشفيع، وجهل الأمة بالإعتاق وجهل البكر بنكاح الولي، وجهل الوكيل والمأذون بالإطلاق وضده. (انتهى).
ومما فرَّقوا فيه بين العلم والجهل ؛ لو قال إن لم أقتل فلانا فكذا وهو ميت إن علم به حنث وإلا لا ؛ كذا في الكنز، وقالوا لو لم تعلم الأمة بأن لها خيار العتق لا يبطل بسكوتها، ولو لم تعلم الصغيرة خيار البلوغ بطل، وقالوا لو استام(۱) جارية متنقبة أو ثوبا ملفوفًا فظهر أنه ملكه بعد الكشف ؛ قيل يعذر إذا دعاه للجهل في موضع الخفاء وقيل لا والمعتمد الأول، وقالوا يعذر الوارث والوصي والمتولي بالتناقض للجهل، وقالوا إذا قبلت الخلع ثم ادعت الثلاث قبله تسمع، فإذا برهنت استردت البدل للجهل في محله ولو قبل الكتابة وادَّعى البدل ثم ادعى الإعتاق قبله تسمع ويسترد البدل إذا برهن وقالوا إذا باع الوصي أو الأب ثم ادعى أنه وقع بغبن فاحش وقال لم أعلم يقبل. وقالوا في باب الرضاع؛ ولا يضر التناقض في الحرية والنسب والطلاق كما أوضحناه في البحر من باب المتفرقات أن الجهل معتبر عندنا لدفع الفساد، فلا ضمان على الكبيرة لو جهلت أن الإرضاع مفسد كما في الهدايا وفي الخلاصة إذا تكلم بكلمة الكفر جاهلاً . قال بعضهم لا كفر. وعامتهم على أنه يكفر ولا يعذر. (انتهى).
(۱) استام طلب بيعها .
As for ignorance, its reality is the absence of knowledge regarding that which is proper to be known. If it is accompanied by belief in the opposite, it is compound ignorance; that is meant by perceiving a thing contrary to what it is. Otherwise, it is simple ignorance; that is meant by lack of perception. Its divisions, as mentioned by the usul scholars in al-Manar, are four: First: false ignorance that is no excuse in the Hereafter, like the ignorance of the disbeliever regarding Allah's attributes and the rulings of the Hereafter, the ignorance of the follower of desire (sahib al-hawa), the ignorance of the transgressor (baghi) such that he guarantees the property of the just person if he destroys it, and the ignorance of one who in his ijtihad contradicts the Qur'an, well-known Sunnah, or consensus, like the fatwa permitting the sale of ummahat al-awlad (mothers of children). Second: ignorance in a place of valid ijtihad or in a place of doubt (shubha), and it is an excuse and a doubt, like the cupper who breaks his fast thinking it is his breakfast, and like one who commits zina with his father's slave-girl or his wife's slave-girl thinking she is permissible to him. Third: ignorance in the Abode of War for a Muslim who has not migrated, and it is an excuse. Attached to it: the fourth: the ignorance of the pre-emptor (shafi'), the ignorance of the slave woman regarding manumission (itq), the ignorance of the virgin regarding marriage by a guardian, and the ignorance of the agent (wakil) and the authorized slave (ma'dhun) regarding unrestricted or restricted authorization. (End). And among the matters in which they distinguished between knowledge and ignorance: if someone says 'If I do not kill so-and-so, then such-and-such' and he is dead, if he knew of his death he breaks his oath, otherwise not. Thus in al-Kanz. They said: if the slave woman does not know that she has the option of manumission (khiyar al-itq), it is not invalidated by her silence; but if a minor girl does not know the option of puberty, it is invalidated. They said: if one negotiates the price of a veiled slave-girl or a wrapped garment, and after uncovering it appears it is his own property, it is said he is excused if he claims ignorance in a hidden matter, and it is said he is not; the relied-upon is the first. They said: the heir, executor, and administrator are excused for contradiction due to ignorance. They said: if a woman accepts khul' and then claims that three divorces occurred before it, she is heard; if she proves it, she takes back the compensation due to ignorance in its place. And similarly, if after writing (kitabah) she claims the compensation and then claims manumission before it, she is heard and takes back the compensation if she proves it. They said: if the executor or father sells and then claims that it involved gross undervaluation, and says 'I did not know', it is accepted. They said in the chapter of rada'ah: contradiction regarding freedom, lineage, and divorce does not harm, as we clarified in al-Bahr from the chapter of miscellaneous rulings, that ignorance is considered with us to repel invalidity. So no liability on the older woman if she did not know that breastfeeding is invalidating, as in al-Hidayah. And in al-Khulasa: if one speaks a word of kufr ignorantly, some said he does not become a disbeliever; but the majority hold that he becomes a disbeliever and is not excused. (End). (1) Istama: he sought to buy it.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir defines ignorance (jahl) and provides a fourfold classification from the usul work al-Manar. The definition distinguishes between simple ignorance (lack of knowledge) and compound ignorance (believing something contrary to its reality). The four types are: (1) False ignorance — not an excuse in the hereafter; includes disbelief, following desires, transgression, or ijtihad contradicting clear texts; such ignorance does not excuse from liability. (2) Ignorance in matters of valid ijtihad or doubt (shubha) — this is an excuse and creates doubt that may prevent penalty; examples given: a cupper who breaks his fast thinking it is breakfast, or someone who commits zina with his father's slave-girl thinking she is permissible (i.e., a strong doubt). (3) Ignorance in Dar al-Harb for a Muslim who hasn't migrated — considered an excuse for actions done without knowledge of Islamic rulings. (4) Attached to the third: specific ignorances of certain legal positions, like the pre-emptor not knowing his right, a slave woman not knowing about manumission option, a virgin not knowing about guardian marriage, or an agent not knowing the scope of authorization. The passage then gives several furuq (distinctions) between knowledge and ignorance in various legal issues: oaths, options of slaves, sales with hidden defects, contracts of khul' and kitabah, sales by executors, contradictions in claims of rada'ah, etc. The guiding principle (as stated in al-Bahr) is that ignorance is considered to ward off invalidity (fasād). However, the passage ends with an important exception: speaking a word of kufr ignorantly — the majority rule that it is not excused and leads to disbelief, though some disagreed. This nuanced treatment shows that ignorance is not always a blanket excuse; it depends on the context and the possibility of knowing.

Key Terms
الجهل الباطل (al-jahl al-bāṭil): False ignorance: ignorance that is no excuse because it stems from disbelief, desire, or opposition to clear evidence.
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): Compound ignorance: believing something contrary to its true nature.
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt: a situation where the legal status is uncertain, often arising from ignorance in a place of ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a Muslim in Dar al-Harb who commits an act without knowing its Islamic ruling?
A) He is not excused because he should have known.
B) He is excused because ignorance in Dar al-Harb is an excuse.
C) It depends on whether he had access to scholars.
D) He is considered a disbeliever.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance in Hanafi fiqh is classified into four types; only genuine doubt or valid ijtihad excuses, while false ignorance from disbelief or rebellion does not.

The Legal Maxim: Ignorance Prevents Corruption – Applications and Scope
Defining ignorance and applying the maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-jahl mu'tabar li-daf' al-fasad' to determine when ignorance excuses a party and derive the correct ruling in the provided furu' cases.

Core Idea
Ignorance excused in ambiguous matters, not in matters known by necessity from religion.

The Hanafi school recognises that ignorance can be a valid excuse in many legal contexts, but its application is nuanced. This lesson introduces the foundational maxim 'ignorance is considered to prevent corruption' and walks through its numerous furu' applications to build your ability to distinguish when ignorance is accepted and when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Classify types of ignorance
From the passage, identify the four types of ignorance and note which excused and which do not.
Focus on the first two types: invalid ignorance (batil) and ignorance in valid ijtihad/shubha.
2
Extract the qa'ida
Locate the explicit statement: 'al-jahl mu'tabar indana li-daf' al-fasad' and understand its scope: ignorance is considered to prevent corruption.
This is the core maxim governing the cases.
3
Apply the qa'ida to furu' cases
Work through each case (oaths, options, sales, agency, etc.) and explain how ignorance or knowledge changes the ruling.
Note the consistency: ignorance leads to leniency (no liability, option preserved, etc.), knowledge leads to liability/invalidity.
4
Identify istithna'at (exceptions)
Find cases where ignorance does NOT excuse, such as uttering kufr or acknowledging a debt after the fact.
These exceptions hinge on the matter being ma'lum min al-din bi'l-darura or a fixed right.
5
Apply as a mufti
Given a modern scenario, determine whether a party can plead ignorance and what the mufta bihi ruling is per the Hanafi school.
Use the maxim alongside the exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجهل فحقيقته عدم العلم عما شأنه من العلم؛ فإن قارن اعتقاد النقيض فهو مركب، وهو المراد بالشعور بالشيء على خلاف ما هو به وإلا فبسيط، وهو المراد بعدم الشعور وأقسامه على ما ذكره الأصليون كما في المنار أربعة.
•
الأول : جهل باطل لا يصلح عذرًا في الآخرة كجهل الكافر بصفات الله تعالى وأحكام الآخرة، وجهل صاحب الهوى، وجهل الباغي حتى يضمن مال العدل إذا أتلفه، وجهل من خالف في اجتهاده الكتاب أو السُّنَّة المشهورة والإجماع كالفتوى ببيع أُمهات الأولاد. والثاني : الجهل في موضع الاجتهاد الصحيح أو في موضع الشبهة وأنه يصلح عذرًا وشبهة كالمحتجم إذا أفطر على ظن أنها فطرته وكمَن زنى بجارية والده أو زوجته على ظن أنها تحلّ له .
به
والثالث : الجهل في دار الحرب من مسلم لم يهاجر وأنه يكون عذرًا. ويلحق
الرابع : وهو جهل الشفيع، وجهل الأمة بالإعتاق وجهل البكر بنكاح الولي، وجهل الوكيل والمأذون بالإطلاق وضده. (انتهى).
ومما فرَّقوا فيه بين العلم والجهل ؛ لو قال إن لم أقتل فلانا فكذا وهو ميت إن علم به حنث وإلا لا ؛ كذا في الكنز، وقالوا لو لم تعلم الأمة بأن لها خيار العتق لا يبطل بسكوتها، ولو لم تعلم الصغيرة خيار البلوغ بطل، وقالوا لو استام جارية متنقبة أو ثوبا ملفوفًا فظهر أنه ملكه بعد الكشف ؛ قيل يعذر إذا دعاه للجهل في موضع الخفاء وقيل لا والمعتمد الأول، وقالوا يعذر الوارث والوصي والمتولي بالتناقض للجهل، وقالوا إذا قبلت الخلع ثم ادعت الثلاث قبله تسمع، فإذا برهنت استردت البدل للجهل في محله ولو قبل الكتابة وادَّعى البدل ثم ادعى الإعتاق قبله تسمع ويسترد البدل إذا برهن وقالوا إذا باع الوصي أو الأب ثم ادعى أنه وقع بغبن فاحش وقال لم أعلم يقبل. وقالوا في باب الرضاع؛ ولا يضر التناقض في الحرية والنسب والطلاق كما أوضحناه في البحر من باب المتفرقات أن الجهل معتبر عندنا لدفع الفساد، فلا ضمان على الكبيرة لو جهلت أن الإرضاع مفسد كما في الهدايا وفي الخلاصة إذا تكلم بكلمة الكفر جاهلاً . قال بعضهم لا كفر. وعامتهم على أنه يكفر ولا يعذر. (انتهى).
وفي آخر اليتيمة ظن لجهله أن ما فعله من المحظورات حلال له، فإن كان مما يعلم من دين النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ضرورة كفر وإلا فلا. وقالوا في باب خيار الرؤية لو اشترى ما كان رآه ولم يتغيَّر فلا خيار له إلا إذا كان لا يعلم أنه مرئيه لعدم الرضاء كذا في الهداية. وقالوا في كتاب الغصب إن الجهل بكونه مال الغير يدفع الإثم لا الضمان وفي إقرار اليتيمة سُئِلَ علي بن أحمد عن رجل أقر أن عليه لفلان حنطة من سلم عقداه بينهما . ثم إنه بعد ذلك قال سألت الفقهاء عن العقد فقالوا هو فاسد؛ فلا يجب على شيء، والمقرّ معروف بالجهل هل يؤاخذ بإقراره؟ فقال لا يسقط عنه الحق بدعوى الجهل (انتهى). وقال قبله : إذا أقرَّ بالطلاق الثلاث على ظن صدق المفتي بالوقوع ثم تبيَّن خطؤه فإفتاء الأهل لم يقع ديانة ولا يصدق في الحكم، ولو باع الوكيل قبل العلم بالوكالة لم يجز البيع ولو باع الوصي قبل العلم بالإيصاء جاز، ولو باع ملك أبيه ولم يعلم بموته ثم علم جاز، وكذا لو باع الجد مال ابنه ولم يعلم بموته نفذ على الصغير ومقتضى بيع الوارث أنه لو زوّج أمة ابنه ثم بان ميتا نفذ. ولو باعه على أنه أبق فبان راجعا ينبغي أن ينفذ.
ومما فرَّقوا فيه بين العلم والجهل ما في وكالة الخانية الوكيل بقضاء الدين إذا دفعه إلى الطالب بعد ما وهب الدين من المديون قالوا إن علم الوكيل بالهبة ضمن وإلا فلا، ولو دفع إلى الطالب بعد ردّته، قالوا إن علم الوكيل بطريق الفقه أن الدفع إلى الطالب بعد ردته لا يجوز ضمن ما دفعه وإلا فلا ولو دفع بعد ما دفع الموكل ؛ فعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله الفرق بين العلم والجهل والمذهب الضمان مطلقا، كالمتفاوضين إذا أذن كل منهما لصاحبه بأداء الزكاة فأدى أحدهما عن صاحبه ثم أدى الثاني عن نفسه وعن صاحبه فإنه يضمن مطلقا . والمأمور بقضاء الدين إذا أدى الأمر بنفسه ثم قضى المأمور فإنه لا يضمن إذا لم يعلم بقضاء الموكل، قالوا هذا على قولهما، أما على قوله فيضمن على كل حال . (انتهى). ولو أجاز الورثة الوصية، ولم يعلموا ما أوصى به لم تصح إجازتهم كذا في وصايا الخانية. وفي وكالة المنية : أمر رجلاً ببيع غلامه بمائة دينار فباعه بألف درهم ولم يعلم الموكل بما باعه، فقال المأمور بعت الغلام فقال أجزت جاز البيع، وكذا في النكاح. وإن قال قد أجزت ما أمرتك به لم يجز. (انتهى).
وفي وكالة الولوالجية : إذا عفا بعض الورثة عن القاتل عمدًا ثم قتله الباقي؛ إن علم أن عفو البعض يسقط القصاص اقتص منه وإلا ،فلا لأن هذا مما يشكل على الناس. (انتهى).
As for ignorance, its reality is the absence of knowledge about something that is normally known. If it is accompanied by belief in the opposite, it is compound ignorance, which is meant by perceiving a thing contrary to its reality. Otherwise, it is simple ignorance, which is meant by lack of perception. Its divisions according to the legal scholars as mentioned in al-Manar are four. First: invalid ignorance that does not serve as an excuse in the afterlife, such as the disbeliever's ignorance of Allah's attributes and the rulings of the afterlife, the ignorance of the person swayed by desire, the ignorance of the rebel such that he guarantees the property of the just person if he destroys it, and the ignorance of the one who contradicts in his ijtihad the Book, the well-known Sunnah, or consensus, like giving a fatwa to sell slave-mothers of children. Second: ignorance in a place of valid ijtihad or in a place of doubt, and it serves as an excuse and a doubt, such as a cupper who breaks fast thinking it is his breaking, and someone who commits fornication with his father's slave-girl or his wife thinking she is lawful for him. Third: ignorance in the land of war by a Muslim who has not emigrated, and it is an excuse. Fourth: the ignorance of the pre-emptor, the ignorance of the slave-girl about emancipation, the ignorance of the virgin about the guardian's marriage, and the ignorance of the agent and the authorized person about the scope of authority and its opposite. (End). Among the distinctions they made between knowledge and ignorance: if someone says, 'If I do not kill so-and-so, then such-and-such [is upon me],' and the person is dead, if he knew [of the death] he breaks his oath, otherwise not. As in al-Kanz. And they said: If the slave-girl did not know that she has the option upon emancipation, it is not voided by her silence; but if the minor did not know the option of puberty, it is voided. And they said: If one negotiates the price of a veiled slave-girl or a wrapped cloth, and then it appears that it was his own property after unveiling, it is said he is excused if he was led by ignorance in a hidden matter, and it is said not; the relied-upon is the first. And they said: The heir, executor, and trustee are excused for contradiction due to ignorance. And they said: If a woman accepts khul' and then claims triple divorce before it, she is heard; then if she provides proof, she recovers the compensation due to ignorance in its place. Similarly, if she accepts kitaba and then claims a compensation, then claims emancipation before it, she is heard and recovers the compensation if she proves it. And they said: If the executor or father sells and then claims that it occurred with gross fraud and says, 'I did not know,' he is accepted. And they said in the chapter of suckling: Contradiction regarding freedom, lineage, and divorce does not harm, as we clarified in al-Bahr from the chapter of miscellaneous topics: that ignorance is considered in our school to prevent corruption. So there is no liability upon an older woman if she was ignorant that suckling invalidates [the marriage], as in al-Hidaya. And in al-Khulasa: If one utters a word of disbelief while ignorant—some said it is not disbelief, but the majority hold that he commits disbelief and is not excused. (End). And at the end of al-Yatima: If one thinks due to his ignorance that what he did from prohibited things is lawful for him, then if it is something known by necessity from the religion of the Prophet (peace be upon him), he disbelieves; otherwise not. And they said in the chapter of option of sight: If one buys something he had seen and it has not changed, he has no option unless he did not know that it was the one he saw, due to lack of consent. As in al-Hidaya. And they said in the book of usurpation: Ignorance that it is the property of another removes sin but not liability. And in the acknowledgment of the orphan: Ali ibn Ahmad was asked about a man who acknowledged that he owed wheat to someone from a salam contract between them. Then afterwards he said: I asked the jurists about the contract and they said it is invalid, so nothing is due. And the acknowledging person is known for ignorance; is he held to his acknowledgment? He said: The right is not dropped from him by the claim of ignorance. (End). And before that: If one acknowledges triple divorce based on the assumption that the mufti's fatwa is correct that it occurred, then his error becomes clear, the fatwa of the family does not occur religiously, and he is not believed judicially. And if the agent sells before knowing of the agency, the sale is not valid. If the executor sells before knowing of the will, it is valid. If one sells his father's property not knowing of his death, then learns, it is valid. Similarly, if the grandfather sells his son's property not knowing of his death, it is effective upon the minor. And the implication of the heir's sale: If he marries off his son's slave-girl then it becomes clear he is dead, it is effective. And if he sells it as an absconder and then it becomes clear he has returned, it should be effective. Among the distinctions they made between knowledge and ignorance is what is in the Agency chapter of al-Khaniyya: The agent for paying a debt—if he pays the claimant after the debtor had gifted the debt, they said: If the agent knew of the gift, he is liable; otherwise not. And if he paid after the debtor's apostasy, they said: If the agent knew by the way of fiqh that payment after apostasy is not valid, he is liable for what he paid; otherwise not. And if he paid after the principal had paid, there is from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) a distinction between knowledge and ignorance, but the school position is absolute liability, like two partners in speculative partnership when each authorizes the other to pay zakat: if one pays for his partner, then the second pays for himself and his partner, he is absolutely liable. And the one ordered to pay a debt—if the principal pays himself and then the agent pays, he is not liable if he did not know of the principal's payment, they said this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), but according to Abu Hanifa he is liable in any case. (End). And if the heirs validate the will without knowing what was bequeathed, their validation is not valid, as in Wasiyya of al-Khaniyya. And in the Agency of al-Muniya: A man ordered another to sell his slave for 100 dinars, and he sold him for 1000 dirhams without the principal knowing. The agent said, 'I sold the slave,' and the principal said, 'I ratify it,' the sale is valid. Similarly in marriage. But if he said, 'I ratify what you commanded me,' it is not valid. (End). And in the Agency of al-Walwaljiyya: If some of the heirs forgive the intentional killer, then the remaining [heirs] kill him: if they knew that the forgiveness of some nullifies retaliation, they are retaliated against; otherwise not, because this is confusing to people. (End).
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir' addresses the legal concept of ignorance (jahl) and its different types, followed by numerous applications that distinguish between knowledge and ignorance. The author begins by defining ignorance as the absence of knowledge about something normally known. He distinguishes compound ignorance (accompanied by a false belief) and simple ignorance (mere lack of awareness). He then cites the fourfold classification from the Hanafi usul work 'al-Manar': 1) Invalid ignorance that does not excuse in the afterlife, covering matters known by necessity (e.g., disbelief, rebellion, opposing clear texts); 2) Ignorance in matters of valid ijtihad or shubha, which excuses and creates doubt (e.g., a cupper thinking he broke his fast, or one who fornicates with his father's slave-girl thinking it permissible); 3) Ignorance in dar al-harb for a Muslim who has not emigrated; 4) Ignorance of specific parties like the pre-emptor (shafi'), slave-girl regarding emancipation, virgin regarding guardian's marriage, and agent regarding the scope of authority. After this classification, the author presents a long series of furu' (subsidiary cases) where the distinction between knowledge and ignorance determines the ruling. The underlying principle is stated: 'ignorance is considered in our school to prevent corruption' (al-jahl mu'tabar 'indana li-daf' al-fasad). This maxim governs many cases: in oaths, options (khiyar), sales by agents, contradicting statements, khul', divorce acknowledgments, usurpation, agency for debt payment, will validation, and retaliation. In each case, if the person acted without knowledge, the ruling is lenient (e.g., no liability, oath not broken, excuse for contradiction). Conversely, knowledge triggers liability or invalidity. The passage also notes internal Hanafi disagreements, such as whether uttering a word of disbelief while ignorant constitutes kufr (majority say yes, some no), or whether an agent who pays after the principal has paid is liable (Abu Hanifa says absolutely, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad distinguish). The overall purpose is to guide the mufti in determining when ignorance can be pleaded as a valid excuse, emphasizing that it depends on the nature of the matter: well-known (ma'lum min al-din bi'l-darura) vs. ambiguous.

Key Terms
الجهل (al-jahl): Absence of knowledge about something that is normally known, either simple (without false belief) or compound (with false belief).
الجهل المركب (al-jahl al-murakkab): Ignorance accompanied by a belief contrary to reality, i.e., thinking one knows when one does not.
الجهل البسيط (al-jahl al-basit): Ignorance without any belief, i.e., simply not knowing.
الشفيع (al-shafi'): The pre-emptor (one who has the right of shuf'a) whose ignorance of the sale is considered an excuse.
معتبر لدفع الفساد (mu'tabar li-daf' al-fasad): Considered to prevent corruption – the legal principle that ignorance is taken into account to avoid invalidating actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of invalid ignorance (jahil batil) that does NOT serve as an excuse?
A) A cupper who breaks his fast thinking it is allowed.
B) A Muslim in dar al-harb who did not know he should emigrate.
C) A person who gives a fatwa to sell ummahat al-awlad (slave-mothers) out of ignorance that it contradicts ijtihad on clear texts.
D) A woman who accepts khul' and later claims triple divorce occurred before.

Key Takeaway
Ignorance is a valid legal excuse in the Hanafi school only for ambiguous matters; it does not excuse violations of rulings known by necessity of religion.

Faith and Financial Obligations of Minors
Rasm rule with exceptions for minors' obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the obligation of iman for a sane minor and apply the relied-upon view on sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah.

Core Idea
A sane minor must believe in Allah, and his wealth bears sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah.

The general principle is that minors are not subject to taklif. However, the Hanafi school carves out exceptions for the core of faith and certain financial duties. This passage from Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir examines the obligation of iman for a sane child and the dispute over sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah. The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that both are obligatory on the child's wealth, with the guardian responsible for fulfillment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
Recall that children are not legally obligated (la taklif) until puberty. This is the baseline.
2
Exceptional case: iman
Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi excepted faith from the rule. A sane child is obligated to believe due to the evidence of the created world, but not to perform acts. His conversion is valid and stands upon adulthood.
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani disagreed, but the preferred view is the first.
3
Financial obligations: sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah
Scholars differed. The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that both are obligatory on the child's wealth. The guardian must pay sadaqat al-fitr and slaughter the udhiyah, following specific rules about the meat.
4
Apply the guardian's role
The guardian performs the duty using the child's wealth, ensuring no charity from the udhiyah meat but feeding the child and preserving value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإيمان بالله تعالى؛ ففي التحرير واستثنى فخر الإسلام من العبادات الإيمان فأثبت أصل وجوبه في الصبي العاقل بسببية حدوث العالم لا الأداء، فإذا أسلم وقع فرضا فلا يجب تجديده بالغًا كتعجيل الزكاة بعد السبب. ونفاه شمس الأئمة لعدم حكمه ولو أدَّاه وقع فرضًا لأن عدم الوجوب كان لعدم حكمه فإذا وجد وجد، والأول أوجه . (انتهى). واختلفوا في وجوب صدقة الفطر في ماله والأضحية. والمعتمد الوجوب فيؤديها الوليّ ويذبحها ولا يتصدق بشيء من لحمها فيطعمه منه ويبتاع له بالباقي ما تبقى عينه. واتفقوا على وجوب العشر والخراج في أرضه وعلى وجوب نفقة زوجته وعياله وقرابته كالبالغ وعلى بطلان عبادته بفعل ما يفسدها من نحو كلام في الصلاة، وأكل وشرب في الصوم وجماع في الحج قبل الوقوف بعرفة، لكن لا دم عليه في فعل محظور إحرامه ولا تنتقص طهارته بالقهقهة في صلاته وإن أبطلت الصلاة. وتصح عباداته وإن لم تجب عليه . واختلفوا في ثوابها والمعتمد أنه له وللمعلم ثواب التعليم، وكذا جميع حسناته. ولا تصح إمامته واختلفوا في صحتها في التراويح. والمعتمد عدمها . وتجب سجدة التلاوة على سامعها من صبي، وقيل لا بد من عقله، وتحصل فضيلة الجماعة بصلاته مع واحد إلا في الجمعة فلا تصح بثلاثة هو منهم.
As for faith in Allah Almighty: In al-Tahrir, Fakhr al-Islam excepted faith from acts of worship and affirmed its obligation in its origin for the sane child due to the contingency of the world's creation, not performance. So if he becomes Muslim, it counts as obligatory, and he does not have to renew it as an adult, like hastening zakat after the cause. Shams al-A'imma rejected this due to lack of legal effect; but if he performs it, it counts as obligatory because the lack of obligation was due to lack of effect, so when it occurs, it occurs. The first is more appropriate. (End). And they differed on the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr from his wealth and udhiyah. The relied-upon is obligation, so the guardian pays and slaughters, and does not give any of its meat in charity; he feeds him from it and buys for him with the remainder what preserves its value. And they agreed on the obligation of 'ushr and kharaj on his land, and on the obligation of maintenance of his wife, dependents, and relatives like an adult, and on the invalidation of his worship by doing what spoils it, such as speaking in prayer, eating and drinking in fast, and intercourse in Hajj before standing at Arafah, but there is no blood penalty on him for doing a prohibited act of ihram, and his purity is not nullified by loud laughter in his prayer even though it invalidates the prayer. And his acts of worship are valid even if not obligatory upon him. And they differed on their reward; the relied-upon is that he has it, and the teacher has the reward of teaching, and likewise all his good deeds. And his leading prayer is not valid, though they differed on its validity in tarawih; the relied-upon is its invalidity. And the prostration of recitation is obligatory on one who hears it from a child; it is said his intellect is necessary. And the virtue of congregation is attained by his praying with one person, except in Friday prayer, which is not valid with three including him.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage details exceptions and expansions on the principle of no taklif. First, regarding faith (iman): according to Fakhr al-Islam, a sane child is obligated to believe due to the evidence of the created world, though not to perform acts. Thus his conversion is valid and does not need renewal at puberty. Shams al-A'imma disagreed, but the preferred view is the former. Second, financial obligations: sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah are obligatory on his wealth; the guardian must fulfill them. Zakat on land ('ushr, kharaj) and maintenance obligations apply. Third, his acts of worship (prayer, fasting, hajj) are valid if performed, even though not obligatory. If he invalidates them, the usual effects (like qada) apply, but some penalties (dam) are waived. Fourth, his imamah (leading prayer) is generally invalid except possibly in tarawih, but the relied-upon view is invalidity. Fifth, sajdat al-tilawah is obligatory on the hearer of a child's recitation. Sixth, he can attain congregational reward by praying with one other person, except for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Charity given at the end of Ramadan, obligatory on the child's wealth according to the relied-upon view
الأضحية (udhiyah): Sacrificial animal for Eid al-Adha, obligatory on the child's wealth per the mu'tamad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view, is sadaqat al-fitr obligatory on the wealth of a minor?
A) Yes, and the guardian must pay
B) No, children are not obligated
C) Only if the child is insane
D) Only for orphans

Key Takeaway
Minors are exempt from most duties, but faith and financial obligations like sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah are exceptions; the guardian must fulfill them.

Validity of Worship and Special Rulings for Minors
Rasm rule on validity and special rules for minors' worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the validity of a minor's worship and apply the rulings on invalidation, imamah, sajdat al-tilawah, and congregational reward.

Core Idea
A minor's worship is valid though not obligatory, but invalidations lead to qada without certain penalties.

While minors are generally not obligated, their acts of worship, if performed, are valid and rewarded. This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir details how invalidation affects a child's prayer, fasting, and hajj, and also covers special rules for imamah, sajdat al-tilawah, and congregational reward. Understanding these nuances helps a mufti issue accurate fatwas regarding children's worship.

Guided Path
1
Establish the default: validity of acts
A minor's worship (prayer, fasting, hajj) is valid even though not obligatory. This is agreed upon.
2
Identify invalidators and consequences
Speaking in prayer, eating/drinking in fast, intercourse in hajj invalidate the act. For invalidation, the child must make up (qada) the act. However, some penalties like dam are waived, and laughter does not break wudu.
3
Determine imamah and congregational rules
A child's leading prayer (imamah) is generally invalid. There is a dispute about tarawih, but the relied-upon view is invalidity. The child can earn congregational reward by praying with one other person, except for Jumu'ah (not valid with three including him).
4
Apply sajdat al-tilawah and reward
Hearing a child's recitation of a sajda verse makes sajdat al-tilawah obligatory on the hearer. The child also earns reward for his good deeds, and the teacher gets reward for teaching.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So if he becomes Muslim, it counts as obligatory, and he does not have to renew it as an adult, like hastening zakat after the cause. Commentary
This passage details exceptions and expansions on the principle of no taklif. Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation, obligatory upon hearing a verse of sajda even from a child.
إمامة الصبي (imamat al-sabi): A minor leading prayer; generally invalid in Hanafi school except possibly tarawih, but mu'tamad is invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effect of loud laughter in prayer for a minor?
A) Invalidates prayer but not wudu
B) Invalidates both prayer and wudu
C) Invalidates only wudu
D) Neither is invalidated

Key Takeaway
A minor's worship is valid and rewarded; but invalidations may have reduced penalties, and the child cannot lead prayer or form a Jumu'ah congregation.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
beginner
6 min
Minor's Purely Harmful Statements Are Suspended
States the qawida and gives three furuat with an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا' to determine the validity of a minor's contracts and identify the exception for a permitted minor.

Core Idea
A minor's purely harmful statements are suspended; permission to trade lifts the interdiction.

This lesson presents a key sub-maxim from the Hanafi school regarding the legal capacity of minors. Not every act of a minor is invalid; only those that are purely harmful are suspended. Through clear examples, the text illustrates when a minor's lending, borrowing, and suretyship are valid or invalid. Understanding this principle is essential for muftis when assessing contracts involving minors.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the qawida
Commit the Arabic text to memory: 'يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا'. This is the core rule.
The rule is a dabt (sub-maxim) that governs the minor's statements.
2
Identify the two categories of minors
Distinguish between the 'محجور' (interdicted) and the 'مأذون' (permitted). The rule applies only to the former.
The permission (إذن) must be explicitly given by the guardian.
3
Match the furuat to the qawida
For each furu' (lending, borrowing, surety), determine whether the act is purely harmful (ضرر محض) or not. If it is, the statement is suspended.
Surety for a minor is purely harmful, but acting as principal or beneficiary is not.
4
Apply the exception for the permitted minor
When the minor is ma'dhun, the same acts (lending, borrowing) become valid because the permission lifts the interdiction.
The exception is built into the first two furuat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا ومنه إقراضه واستقراضه لو كان محجورًا، لا لو كان مأذونا وكفالته باطلة ولو عن أبيه، وصحت له وعنه مطلقا . وقد جمع العمادي في فصوله أحكام الصبيان فمن أراد الاطلاع على كثرة فروعنا وحُسْن تقريرنا واستيعابنا وعلى نِعَم الله تعالى علينا فيما نقصده من جمع المتفرق فلينظر ما ذكره العمادي، وقد ذكر العمادي ما يكون به بالغا، وما يتعلق به تركناه قصدًا لتصريحهم به في كتاب الحجر، وكتابنا هذا إن شاء الله تعالى كتاب المفردات الملتقطات .
Things that are suspended from his statements are those that are purely harmful, and from these are his lending and borrowing if he is interdicted, not if he is permitted, and his surety is invalid even from his father, and it is valid for him and from him absolutely. And al-Imadi has collected in his chapters the rulings of minors, so whoever wants to see the abundance of our branches, the excellence of our exposition, and our comprehensiveness, and the blessings of Allah upon us in our aim of collecting scattered matters, let him look at what al-Imadi mentioned. And al-Imadi has mentioned what makes one an adult, and what relates to that we have left out intentionally because they have explicitly stated it in the chapter of interdiction, and this book of ours, Allah willing, is a book of selected individual rulings.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage opens with a key qawida: A minor's statements that are purely harmful (متمحض ضرر) are suspended (يتوقف), meaning they do not take effect unless they bring benefit. The author gives three furuat: (1) A minor under interdiction (محجور) who lends or borrows—the transaction is invalid. (2) If he is permitted to trade (مأذون), the same transactions are valid. (3) His surety (كفالة) is invalid even if for his father, but it is valid in his favor and on his behalf absolutely. The passage then references al-Imadi's comprehensive work on minors, and the author explains that he omitted the discussion of puberty (بلوغ) because it is covered in the book of interdiction (كتاب الحجر). This methodological note shows that the present work intends to collect scattered rulings without repetition.

Key Terms
تمحض ضررًا (tamahhada dararan): A statement that is purely harmful to the minor with no potential benefit
محجور (mahjur): A minor under legal interdiction due to lack of maturity or insanity
مأذون (ma'dhun): A minor who has been granted permission by his guardian to engage in trade

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid, because it is for a family member
B) Invalid, as stated in the text
C) Valid only if the father is unable to pay
D) Valid if the minor is above the age of discernment

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا' is a cornerstone for evaluating minors' contracts; always check if the minor is interdicted or permitted.

The Minor's Liability for Usurpation and Related Torts
List of rulings on minor's tort liability and guardian duties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'la yadmanu al-sabi bi al-ghasb' to various tort scenarios, identify exceptions, and explain the Hanafi position on parental liability for a minor's accidental death.

Core Idea
A minor is not liable for usurpation, but liability shifts when the act involves direct harm or negligence.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a series of rulings revolving around a key legal maxim: the minor is not liable for usurpation. However, the text expands this with numerous exceptions and applications, particularly in cases of harm caused by or to minors. The goal is to understand how this dabt (sub-maxim) operates in different fiqh chapters and how to apply it in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Qawida and Scope
Read the first few lines to find the qawida 'لا يضمن الصبي بالغصب'. Note that it applies to usurpation (ghasb) by force, not to all interactions with minors.
The qawida is a dabt (restrictive principle) within the larger maxim on damages.
2
Distinguish Force from Deception
Compare the rulings: taking a minor by force (ghasb) leads to imprisonment until the minor is returned; taking by deception (khid'a) without force is not ghasb and does not trigger liability.
The key condition for ghasb is forceful taking.
3
Analyze Cases of Harm to the Minor
Review cases where a third party causes harm through the minor (handing a knife, ordering to fall from a tree, sending on a dangerous errand). Note that liability falls on the person who initiated the dangerous act.
These are extensions of the qawida via the principle of direct causation (tawallud).
4
Evaluate the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Parental Liability
Study the case of a nine-year-old falling from a roof. Identify the two views: some say kaffara on parents due to negligence; the correct view (الصحيح) says only istighfar unless the child fell from the parent's hands.
The tarjih depends on the child's ability to guard himself at age nine.
5
Apply the Qawida to Fatwa Practice
Consider how a mufti would use these rulings in a real fatwa. Identify the mufta bihi positions and the authority level of the sources (al-Khaniyya, al-Multaqat).
Later fatwa collections often adopt the lenient view for parental liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصبية التي لا تُشتَهَى يجوز السفر بها بغير محرم ولا يضمن الصبي بالغصب فلو غصب صبيا فمات عنده لم يضمنه إلا إذا نقله إلى أرض مسبعة (۱) أو مكان الوباء أو الحمى، وقد سُئِلتُ عمَّن أخذ ابن إنسان صغيرًا وأخرجه من البلد هل يلزمه إحضاره إلى أبيه ؟ فأجبت بما في الخانية : رجل غصب صبيا حرًا فغاب الصبي عن يده فإن الغاصب يُحبَس حتى يجيء بالصبي أو يعلم أنه مات (انتهى). ولو خدعه حتى أخذه برضاه لم يضمن كما في الخانية، لأنه ما غصبه لأنه الأخذ قهرًا وفي الملتقط من النكاح وعن محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيمن خدع بنت رجل أو امرأته وأخرجها من منزله. قال أحبسه أبدًا حتى يأتي بها أو يعلم موتها. (انتهى). ولو قطع طرف صبي لم تعلم صحته ففيه حكومة عدل لا دية ولو دفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل نفسه لم يضمن الدافع، وإن قتل غيره فالدية على عاقلة الصبي، ويرجعون بها على الدافع. وكذا لو أمر صبيا بقتل إنسان فقتله، ولو أمر صبيا بالوقوع من شجرة فوقع ضمن ديته، ولو أرسله في حاجة فعطب ضمنه وكذا لو أمره بصعود شجرة لنقض ثمارها فوقع، وكذا لو أمره بكسر الحطب كذا في الخانية، وفيها أيضًا : صبي ابن تسع سنين سقط من سطح أو غرق في ماء ؛ قال بعضهم لا شيء على الوالدين لأنه ممن يحفظ نفسه، وإن كان لا يعقل أو كان أصغر سنًا ؛ قالوا يكون على الوالدين أو على من كان الصبي في حجره الكفارة لترك الحفظ، وقال بعضهم ليس على الوالدين شيء إلا الاستغفار وهو الصحيح، إلا أن يسقط من يده فعليه الكفَّارة، ولو حمل صبيا على دابة وقال أمسكها لي وهي واقفة فسقط ومات كان على عاقلة الذي حمله الدية مطلقا، وإن سير الصبي الدابة فوطأت إنسانًا فقتلته فالدّية على عاقلة الصبي، إلا أن يكون الصبي لا يستمسك عليها فهدر، ولو كان الرجل راكبًا فجعل صبيا معه فقتلت الدابة إنسانًا ؛ فإن كان الصبي لا يستمسك فالدية على عاقلة الرجل فقط، وإلا فعلى عاقلتهما. (انتهى). ولو ملأ صبي كوزا من حوض ثم صبه فيه لم يحلّ لأحد أن يشرب منه، ولا يجوز للولي إلباسه الحرير والذهب ولا أن يسقيه الخمر ولا أن يجلسه للبول والغائط مستقبلاً أو مستدبرًا، ولا أن يخضب يده أو رجله بالحناء، وفي الملتقط : زوج ابنته من رجل وذهبت ولا تدري لا يجبر زوجها على الطلب (انتهى).
A young girl who is not desired may travel without a mahram. The minor is not liable for usurpation: if someone usurps a minor and the minor dies in his possession, he is not liable unless he moved him to a land of many wild beasts or a place of plague or fever. I was asked about someone who took another's small child and took him out of the city: is he obliged to bring him back to his father? I answered according to al-Khaniyya: If a man usurps a free minor and the minor disappears from his hand, the usurper is imprisoned until he brings the minor or knows that he died. If he deceived him until he took him with his consent, he is not liable, as in al-Khaniyya, because he did not usurp him since usurpation is taking by force. In al-Multaqat from al-Nikah, on the authority of Muhammad (rahimahullah) about someone who deceived a man's daughter or wife and took her out of his house, he said: I would imprison him forever until he brings her or knows of her death. If someone cuts off a limb of a minor whose health is unknown, there is an equitable compensation (hukumat 'adl), not diya. If someone hands a knife to a minor and he kills himself, the giver is not liable. If he kills another, the diya is on the minor's aqila, and they recover from the giver. Similarly, if he orders a minor to kill someone and he does so. If he orders a minor to fall from a tree and he falls, he is liable for his diya. If he sends him on an errand and he is injured, he is liable. Similarly, if he orders him to climb a tree to pick fruit and he falls. Similarly, if he orders him to split wood, as in al-Khaniyya. And therein also: A minor of nine years falls from a roof or drowns in water; some said there is nothing on the parents because he is one who can guard himself; if he is not intelligent or is younger, they said there is kaffara on the parents or on the one in whose lap the minor was for neglecting supervision. And some said there is nothing on the parents except seeking forgiveness, and that is the correct view, unless he falls from his hand, then he is liable for kaffara. If someone places a minor on an animal and says 'hold it for me' while it is standing still, and he falls and dies, then the diya is on the aqila of the one who placed him absolutely. If the minor causes the animal to move and it tramples and kills a person, the diya is on the minor's aqila, unless the minor cannot hold on, then it is null. If a man is riding and places a minor with him and the animal kills a person, then if the minor cannot hold on, the diya is only on the man's aqila; otherwise, on both their aqilas. If a minor fills a cup from a tank and then pours it back in, it is not permissible for anyone to drink from it. It is not permissible for the guardian to dress him in silk and gold, nor to give him wine to drink, nor to seat him for urination or defecation facing or turning away from the qibla, nor to dye his hand or foot with henna. In al-Multaqat: If he marries off his daughter to a man and she disappears and does not know, her husband is not compelled to search.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive collection of rulings concerning a minor's liability in torts and the guardian's duties. It begins with a rule about a young girl traveling without a mahram. Then the core qawida: 'لا يضمن الصبي بالغصب' (the minor is not liable for usurpation). However, exceptions are detailed: if the usurper moves the minor to a dangerous place (land of beasts, plague, fever), he becomes liable. The ruling on imprisonment of the usurper until the minor is produced is quoted from al-Khaniyya. Deception without force does not constitute ghasp, so no liability. Then follow various cases: cutting a limb (governed by equitable assessment, not fixed diya), handing a knife to a minor causing death (giver not liable if the minor kills himself; if kills another, diya on minor's aqila who then recover from giver), ordering a minor to do dangerous acts (liability falls on the orderer). The case of a nine-year-old child falling from a roof illustrates a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: some impose kaffara on the parents for negligence, while others only require istighfar, with the latter being preferred unless the child fell from the parent's hands. Rulings on riding animals and liability for death follow. Finally, guardianship duties are listed: not dressing in silk/gold, not giving wine, not seating for excretion facing the qibla, not dyeing with henna. The last ruling concerns a wife who disappears after marriage; the husband is not forced to search.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: taking someone else's property or person by force without right
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Equitable compensation determined by a fair assessment, not a fixed diya

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone usurps a free minor and the minor disappears?
A) The usurper is simply fined
B) The usurper is imprisoned until he brings the minor or knows he died
C) The usurper is not liable because the minor is free
D) The usurper must pay the minor's value

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'la yadmanu al-sabi bi al-ghasb' is not absolute; liability arises when the act involves direct harm (e.g., moving to dangerous place) or when a third party orders dangerous acts.

The Legal Status of the Intoxicated Person: Key Principles and Exceptions
Defines legal capacity and exceptions for the intoxicated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida on the intoxicated person, distinguish between prohibited and permissible intoxication, and apply the exceptions to legal responsibility.

Core Idea
The intoxicated from a prohibited source is like the sane—responsible for his acts, with limited exceptions.

This passage establishes the foundational Hanafi rule: the intoxicated person (السكران) is legally responsible (مكلف) if his intoxication stems from a prohibited substance. The proof is divine address in Quran 4:43. However, exceptions exist for specific acts, and the ruling differs if the intoxicant is permissible (e.g., under compulsion) or if it is a narcotic like banj. Understanding this distinction is crucial for fatwa on divorce, manumission, and other legal acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of legal responsibility
The text cites Quran 4:43 to prove that the intoxicated person is addressed by Allah and thus is mukallaf. This is the foundational dalil naqli.
The verse prohibits approaching prayer while intoxicated, indicating the person is responsible even in that state.
2
Distinguish the cause of intoxication
The key distinction: if intoxication is from a prohibited substance (حرام), the person is treated like a sane person; if from a permissible cause (مباح), he is like an unconscious person and his divorce does not occur.
Permissible causes include forced drinking (مكره) or necessity, though there is ikhtilaf on some details.
3
Learn the general rule and its exceptions
The prohibited-intoxicated is like the conscious person except in specific matters. The original three exceptions: apostasy, confession of pure hudud, and testifying against oneself. The author adds four more from al-Imadi regarding marriage of minors, agency for divorce, agency for sale, and usurpation.
These exceptions show that even the prohibited-intoxicated is not fully accountable in every matter.
4
Understand the ruling on types of intoxicants
For drinks from grains/honey, the fatwa is that if the substance is prohibited, divorce and manumission occur. For banj, it depends on whether the person knew it was banj.
This addresses contemporary substances like cannabis and opium.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
Apply the rule to ibadat: adhan is disliked and should be repeated; fasting is valid if intention is made after sobering; i'tikaf is not invalidated; standing at Arafat is valid without intention.
These furuat confirm that intoxication does not automatically nullify acts of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام السكران
مكلف هو لقوله تعالى: ﴿ لاَ تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلاةَ وَأَنْتُم سُكَارَى [النساء : ٤٣] خاطبهم تعالى ونهاههم حال سكرهم. فإن كان السكر من محرم فالسكران منه هو المكلف، وإن كان من مباح فلا، فهو كالمغمى عليه لا يقع طلاقه. واختلف التصحيح فيما إذا سكر مكرها أو مضطرًا فطلق. وقدمنا في الفوائد أنه من محرم كالضاحي إلا في ثلاث: الرَّدَّة والإقرار بالحدود الخالصة، والإشهاد على شهادة نفسه وزدت على الثلاث مسائل :
الأولى : تزويج الصغير والصغيرة بأقل من مهر المثل أو بأكثر فإنه لا ينفذ.
الثانية الوكيل بالطلاق صاحيًا، إذا سكر فطلق لم يقع.
الثالثة : الوكيل بالبيع لو سكر فباع لم ينفذ على موكله .
الرابعة : غصب من صاح ورده عليه وهو سكران وهي في فصول العمادي، فهو كالصاحي إلا في سبع فيؤاخذ بأقواله وأفعاله.
واختلف التصحيح فيما إذا سكر من الأشربة المتَّخذة من الحبوب أو العسل. والفتوى على أنه إن سكر من محرم فيقع طلاقه وعتاقه ولو زال عقله بالبنج لم يقع، وعن الإمام أنه إن كان يعلم أنه بنج حين شربه يقع وإلا فلا. وصرحوا بكراهة أذان السكران واستحباب إعادته وينبغي ألأ يصح أذانه كالمجنون. وأما صومه في رمضان فلا إشكال أنه إن صحا قبل خروج وقت النيَّة أنه يصح منه إذا نوى لأنا لا نشترط التبييت فيها، وإذا خرج وقتها قبل صحوه أتمَّ وقضى ولا يبطل الاعتكاف بسكره. ويصح وقوفه بعرفات كالمغمى عليه لعدم اشتراط النية فيه.
Rulings on the intoxicated person. He is legally responsible (mukallaf) due to the verse: 'Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated' (4:43); Allah addressed them and prohibited them while in their intoxication. So if the intoxication is from a prohibited substance, then the intoxicated person from it is the legally responsible one; and if from a permissible one, then not; he is like the unconscious person, his divorce does not occur. There is difference in verification (tas-hih) regarding when he becomes intoxicated under compulsion or necessity and then divorces. We previously stated in the benefits (al-Fawa'id) that he is like the conscious person except in three matters: apostasy, confession of pure hudud, and witnessing against himself. And I added three more issues: First: Marrying a minor boy or girl for less or more than the proper mahr – it is not executed. Second: An agent for divorce when sober, if he becomes intoxicated and divorces, it does not occur. Third: An agent for sale, if he becomes intoxicated and sells, it is not binding on his principal. Fourth: [Actually fourth is from al-Imadi's chapters:] Usurpation from a conscious person and returning it while intoxicated – he is like the conscious person except in seven matters; he is held accountable for his statements and actions. There is a difference in verification regarding intoxication from drinks made from grains or honey. The fatwa is that if he becomes intoxicated from a prohibited substance, his divorce and manumission occur; if his mind is removed by banj (a narcotic), it does not occur. From Imam Abu Hanifa: if he knew he was drinking banj when he drank it, it occurs; otherwise not. They explicitly stated the dislike (karaha) of the adhan of an intoxicated person and the recommendation to repeat it; it is not valid like that of a madman. As for his fasting in Ramadan, there is no issue: if he becomes sober before the time of intention exits, it is valid if he intends, because we do not require the intention to be made at night. If the time exits before he sobers, he completes and makes up the day. His i'tikaf is not invalidated by his intoxication. His standing at Arafat is valid like the unconscious person because intention is not required for it.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This section defines the legal status of the intoxicated person (السكران). It begins with a dalil naqli: Quran 4:43 addresses the intoxicated, proving they are mukallaf (legally responsible). The key distinction is the cause of intoxication: if from a prohibited substance (حرام), the person is treated like a sane person in most matters; if from a permissible cause (مباح, e.g., forced or necessary), he is like one unconscious – his divorce does not occur. There is an internal Hanafi difference (اختلف التصحيح) regarding intoxication under compulsion or necessity. The author then quotes from al-Fawa'id that the prohibited intoxicated person (like one who intentionally drinks) is like the conscious person except in three matters: apostasy (ردة), confession to pure hudud penalties, and testifying against oneself. The author adds four more exceptions from al-Imadi: (1) marrying a minor at less or more than proper mahr is not binding; (2) a sober agent for divorce who divorces while drunk – not effective; (3) an agent for sale who sells while drunk – not binding on principal; (4) usurping from a conscious person and returning it while intoxicated – he is like the conscious except in seven matters. Then the text discusses drinks from grains/honey: the fatwa is that if the substance is prohibited, divorce and manumission occur even if drunk; if the mind is removed by banj (a narcotic), it does not occur unless the person knew it was banj when drinking. Practical rulings follow: adhan of an intoxicated person is disliked and should be repeated; fasting is valid if intention is made after sobering; i'tikaf is not invalidated; standing at Arafat is valid without intention.

Key Terms
سكران (sakran): A person in a state of intoxication, legally defined as one whose mind is clouded from consumption
بنج (banj): A narcotic substance that removes the mind, like cannabis or opium
مكره (mukrah): One who is forced or compelled to drink

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It does not occur because he is not in his senses
B) It occurs, because he is considered legally responsible
C) It occurs only if the drink was from grapes
D) It does not occur unless he was a habitual drinker

Key Takeaway
The intoxicated from a prohibited source is legally responsible like the sane person; his divorce and manumission are valid, with limited exceptions.

Liability of Rider and Child Passenger
Ruling on liability when a rider's horse kills someone with a child passenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim on joint liability to the case of a rider and a child passenger when the animal kills someone.

Core Idea
Liability follows capacity to control; if the child cannot hold on, the rider bears full responsibility.

This lesson examines a specific furu' case from the Hanafi tradition that applies a broader qa'ida (legal maxim) about liability for harm caused by animals. The ruling hinges on a factual determination: whether the child passenger is capable of holding onto the animal. Understanding this distinction helps muftis apply the correct maxim in similar cases of shared control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core factual distinction
The ruling turns on whether the child 'cannot hold on' (la yastamsik) or can hold on. This is a factual inquiry into the child's age, strength, and ability to control the animal.
The legal consequence changes only at this factual pivot.
2
Apply the maxim of causation
If the child cannot hold on, he is not a cause of the death; only the rider is. If he can hold on, both are causes. Liability follows direct causation.
The underlying maxim: الضمان يتبع السببية (Liability follows causation).
3
Determine who is liable
When only the rider is the cause, his 'aqila alone pays diya. When both are causes, the 'aqila of each are liable for half.
The text says 'on the 'aqila of both of them', implying equal sharing.
4
Connect to broader qa'ida
This case is a furu' of the maxim: إذا اجتمع سببان انقسم الضمان (When two causes combine, liability is divided). Recognise it as a memorisation anchor for that maxim.
Ibn Nujaym in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir lists this case under that maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان الرجل راكبًا فجعل صبيا معه فقتلت الدابة إنسانًا ؛ فإن كان الصبي لا يستمسك فالدية على عاقلة الرجل فقط، وإلا فعلى عاقلتهما.
And if a man was riding and placed a child with him, and the animal killed a person: then if the child cannot hold on, the blood money is only on the 'aqila (male paternal relatives) of the man; otherwise, it is on the 'aqila of both of them.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding liability when a rider places a child behind him on an animal, and the animal kills someone. The key distinction is whether the child is capable of holding on independently. If the child is too young or weak to hold on (لا يستمسك), then the rider alone is responsible for controlling the animal, so the blood money is on his 'aqila. If the child is capable of holding on, then both the rider and the child share responsibility, and the 'aqila of both are liable. This is a specific application of the general principle that liability follows causation and capacity.

Key Terms
عاقلة ('aqila): The male paternal relatives (asaba) who are liable to pay blood money (diya) on behalf of a killer in cases of accidental homicide.
لا يستمسك (la yastamsik): The child is unable to hold onto the animal or the rider due to immaturity or weakness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if the child cannot hold on, the diya is on whose 'aqila?
A) The child's 'aqila only
B) The rider's 'aqila only
C) Both 'aqilas
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Liability for harm caused by an animal is shared among those who have effective control; capacity to hold on determines whether a child passenger is a co-cause.

Guardian's Prohibitions Regarding a Child
List of prohibited guardian actions with a related impurity case and a missing-daughter ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal maxim governing a guardian's prohibited actions towards a child and apply it to similar cases from the furuat provided.

Core Idea
A guardian must avoid any action leading to sin or impurity for the child, even if the child is not yet accountable.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a series of rulings on what a guardian cannot do with a child. These are not random prohibitions but applications of a broader principle: the guardian is entrusted with the child's religious and physical well-being and must not expose the child to harm or sin. The passage also includes a case about water impurity caused by a child's action, showing that the child's actions can have legal consequences. Understanding these rulings helps a mufti advise guardians on their responsibilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying qawida
Recognize that all prohibitions stem from the guardian's duty to avoid causing sin or impurity for the child. The maxim is: 'The guardian must protect the child from prohibitions and impurities and may not do anything with the child that violates the shari'ah.'
This is a sughra (minor) qawida governing guardianship.
2
List the furuat (specific cases)
Enumerate each specific prohibition mentioned: dressing in silk/gold, giving wine, seating for elimination facing/away from qibla, dyeing with henna. Also note the water impurity case and the missing daughter case.
Each furu' is an application of the qawida.
3
Extract the legal basis for each furu'
For each prohibition, determine why it is prohibited: silk/gold is haram for males, wine is haram, facing qibla during elimination is makruh tahriman, henna may be considered beautification inappropriate for a child, etc.
The water case shows the child's action can cause impurity; the missing daughter case shows the guardian is not liable for unforeseeable consequences.
4
Apply to similar cases
Using the qawida, deduce rulings on analogous situations, e.g., guardian giving the child a musical instrument, cutting the child's hair in a non-sunnah style, or allowing the child to watch haram content.
The qawida prevents any action that leads to sin or harm.
5
Note the exception from al-Multaqit
The case of a missing daughter shows that obligations are not imposed beyond one's capacity. The husband is not compelled to search; this aligns with the principle of 'لا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها'.
This is not a prohibition but a statement of what is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ملأ صبي كوزا من حوض ثم صبه فيه لم يحلّ لأحد أن يشرب منه، ولا يجوز للولي إلباسه الحرير والذهب ولا أن يسقيه الخمر ولا أن يجلسه للبول والغائط مستقبلاً أو مستدبرًا، ولا أن يخضب يده أو رجله بالحناء، وفي الملتقط : زوج ابنته من رجل وذهبت ولا تدري لا يجبر زوجها على الطلب.
And if a child fills a jug from a tank and then pours it back into it, it is not permissible for anyone to drink from it. And it is not permissible for the guardian to clothe him (the child) in silk or gold, nor to give him wine to drink, nor to seat him for urination or defecation facing or turning away from the qibla, nor to dye his hand or foot with henna. And in al-Multaqit: (if a man) married his daughter to a man and she went away and he does not know (where she is), her husband is not compelled to search for her.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage provides a series of rulings concerning the guardian's (wali) conduct towards a child under his care. It begins with a case where a child contaminates water by filling a jug from a tank and pouring it back, rendering the water impure, so no one may drink it. Then it lists prohibitions on the guardian: dressing the child in silk or gold (forbidden for males in Islam), giving wine, seating the child facing or with back to the qibla during elimination (which is disliked or prohibited), and dyeing the child's limbs with henna (which is considered a form of beautification that should be avoided for children? Actually, henna is permissible but may be disliked for young children?). The last ruling from al-Multaqit states that if a father marries off his daughter and she goes missing, the husband is not compelled to search for her. These are all specific applications of the guardian's responsibility to raise the child in accordance with shari'ah and to avoid causing sin or impurity.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian (usually father or grandfather) who has legal authority over the child's affairs.
الملتقط (al-Multaqit): A Hanafi legal text (al-Multaqit fi al-Fatawa) by al-Hasan al-Multaqit, a collection of rulings.
مستقبلاً (mustaqbilan): Facing the qibla.
مستدبرًا (mustadbaran): Turning one's back to the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a child pours water from a jug back into the tank?
A) The water becomes impure and cannot be drunk.
B) The child must be punished.
C) The guardian may drink it after purification.
D) It is permissible to drink if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The guardian must avoid all actions that would be sinful for an adult, even when done to a child.

Rulings on the Intoxicated Person (Ahkam al-Sakran)
Comprehensive list of rulings on the intoxicated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi rulings on the intoxicated person based on the source of intoxication and apply the exceptions where the intoxicated is treated differently from the conscious person.

Core Idea
Intoxication from a forbidden substance does not remove legal responsibility; from a permissible source, it does.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a detailed set of rulings (ahkam) concerning the intoxicated person (sakran) in Hanafi fiqh. The central principle is that the intoxicated person remains legally responsible (mukallaf) if the intoxication resulted from a forbidden substance, but if from a permissible substance, he is treated like an unconscious person. The passage then lists exceptions and delves into the madhhab dispute on the legal definition of intoxication. Understanding these rulings is crucial for a mufti when issuing fatwas on matters such as divorce, sales, oaths, and acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Primary Ruling
Recognize that the intoxicated person is mukallaf (legally responsible) when the intoxication is from a forbidden substance, based on Quran 4:43 which addresses them while intoxicated. If from a permissible source, he is like an unconscious person (maghmi 'alayh).
This distinction governs all subsequent rulings.
2
Distinguish the Source of Intoxication
Determine whether the intoxicant is forbidden (khamr, etc.) or permissible (e.g., accidental). The ruling on the validity of actions depends on this. Forbidden source: divorce and emancipation are valid; permissible source: they are not.
Also consider cases of duress (ikrah) which have ikhtilaf.
3
List the Exceptions
Note that the intoxicated from a forbidden substance is like the conscious person except in a specific set of cases. The text lists seven: apostasy, confession of hadd, testimony on himself, and four added by the author (marriage of minors with improper dower, agent's divorce, agent's sale, and seizure of property).
These exceptions are where the intoxicated is not held accountable despite being from a forbidden substance.
4
Analyze the Madhhab Dispute on the Definition
Understand the two definitions of intoxication: Abu Hanifa's (loss of basic discrimination) and the Sahibayn's (confused speech). The fatwa follows the Sahibayn in matters of impurity and oaths as a precaution (ihtiyat).
This affects rulings on wudu invalidation and oath fulfillment.
5
Apply to Furu' (Subsidiary Cases)
Apply the principles to specific scenarios: validity of adhan, fasting, i'tikaf, standing at 'Arafat, and the obligation to make up missed worship.
The text explicitly addresses these cases, providing a comprehensive picture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام السكران. مكلف هو لقوله تعالى: ﴿ لاَ تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلاةَ وَأَنْتُم سُكَارَى ﴾ خاطبهم تعالى ونهاهم حال سكرهم. فإن كان السكر من محرم فالسكران منه هو المكلف، وإن كان من مباح فلا، فهو كالمغمى عليه لا يقع طلاقه. واختلف التصحيح فيما إذا سكر مكرها أو مضطرا فطلق. وقدمنا في الفوائد أنه من محرم كالضاحي إلا في ثلاث: الرَّدَّة والإقرار بالحدود الخالصة، والإشهاد على شهادة نفسه وزدت على الثلاث مسائل : الأولى : تزويج الصغير والصغيرة بأقل من مهر المثل أو بأكثر فإنه لا ينفذ. الثانية الوكيل بالطلاق صاحيًا، إذا سكر فطلق لم يقع. الثالثة : الوكيل بالبيع لو سكر فباع لم ينفذ على موكله . الرابعة : غصب من صاح ورده عليه وهو سكران وهي في فصول العمادي، فهو كالصاحي إلا في سبع فيؤاخذ بأقواله وأفعاله. واختلف التصحيح فيما إذا سكر من الأشربة المتَّخذة من الحبوب أو العسل. والفتوى على أنه إن سكر من محرم فيقع طلاقه وعتاقه ولو زال عقله بالبنج لم يقع، وعن الإمام أنه إن كان يعلم أنه بنج حين شربه يقع وإلا فلا. وصرحوا بكراهة أذان السكران واستحباب إعادته وينبغي ألا يصح أذانه كالمجنون. وأما صومه في رمضان فلا إشكال أنه إن صحا قبل خروج وقت النيَّة أنه يصح منه إذا نوى لأنا لا نشترط التبييت فيها، وإذا خرج وقتها قبل صحوه أتمَّ وقضى ولا يبطل الاعتكاف بسكره. ويصح وقوفه بعرفات كالمغمى عليه لعدم اشتراط النية فيه. واختلف في حدّ السكران فقيل : مَن لا يعرف الأرض من السماء والرجل من المرأة. وبه قال الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله . وقيل : مَن في كلامه اختلاط وهذيان، وهو قولهما وبه أخذ كثير من المشايخ والمعتبر في القدح المُسكِر في حق الحرمة ما قالاه احتياطا في المحرَّمات والخلاف في الحدّ والفتوى على قولهما في انتقاض الطهارة به وفي يمينه ألا يُسكر كما بيناه في شرح الكنز. تنبيه : قولهم إن السكر من مباح كالإغماء، يُستثنى منه سقوط القضاء فإنه لا يسقط عنه وإن كان أكثر من يوم وليلة لأنه بصنعه؛ كذا في المحيط.
Rulings of the Intoxicated. He is morally responsible because of the Almighty's saying: 'Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated' – He addressed them and forbade them while they were in a state of intoxication. So if the intoxication was from a forbidden (substance), then the intoxicated person from it is morally responsible; but if it was from a permissible (substance), then he is not, and he is like an unconscious person – his divorce does not take effect. There is a difference in verification regarding when he becomes intoxicated under duress or necessity and then divorces. We have previously stated in the benefits that he is like the conscious (al-dahiya) except in three: apostasy, confession of pure hadd punishments, and giving testimony regarding his own statement. And I added four more issues to the three: First: marrying a minor girl or boy for less or more than the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) – it is not effective. Second: an agent for divorce while sober, if he becomes intoxicated and divorces, it does not occur. Third: an agent for sale, if he becomes intoxicated and sells, it is not binding on his principal. Fourth: (if) someone who is conscious seizes (property) and returns it to him while he is intoxicated – this is in Fusul al-Imadi; he is like the conscious except in seven (cases); he is held accountable for his words and actions. And there is a difference in verification regarding when he becomes intoxicated from drinks made from grains or honey. The fatwa is: if he becomes intoxicated from a forbidden (substance), his divorce and emancipation take effect; even if his mind is gone due to banj (a narcotic), it does not take effect. And from Imam (Abu Hanifa) that if he knew it was banj when he drank it, it takes effect; otherwise not. And they explicitly stated the dislike of the adhan of an intoxicated person and the recommendation to repeat it; it should not be valid like the insane. As for his fasting in Ramadan, there is no issue: if he becomes sober before the time of intention exits, it is valid from him if he intends because we do not require the intention at night; and if the time exits before his sobriety, he completes and makes up (the fast). And his i'tikaf is not invalidated by his intoxication. And his standing at 'Arafat is valid like an unconscious person because intention is not required there. And there is a difference regarding the legal definition of the intoxicated: it is said: one who does not distinguish between heaven and earth, or between a man and a woman – this is the view of Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa). And it is said: one whose speech is confused and delirious – this is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and many scholars adopt it; and the reliable view regarding the intoxicating drink concerning prohibition is what the two said as a precaution regarding forbidden things. The disagreement is about the legal definition, and the fatwa is according to the two regarding the invalidation of wudu by it and regarding his oath not to get intoxicated, as we explained in Sharh al-Kanz. A note: Their statement that intoxication from a permissible source is like unconsciousness – an exception is made from it for the lapse of making up (qada') – for it (the obligation to make up) does not fall from him even if it is more than a day and night because it is by his own action. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This extensive passage from Imam Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a comprehensive treatment of rulings related to the intoxicated person (sakran) in Hanafi fiqh. The passage type is a compilation of rulings under the heading 'Ahkam al-Sakran'. The opening establishes the principle that the intoxicated person is held morally accountable (mukallaf) if the intoxication resulted from a forbidden substance, citing Quran 4:43 as evidence that Allah addressed them while intoxicated. Key distinctions: (1) If intoxication is from a permissible substance (e.g., accidentally), he is like unconscious (maghmi 'alayh) – his divorce does not occur; (2) If from a forbidden substance, his divorce and emancipation are valid; (3) If under duress, there is ikhtilaf; (4) He is like a conscious person except in three matters (apostasy, confession of hadd, testifying on himself) – but the author adds four more: (a) marrying minors with improper dower, (b) agent for divorce divorce, (c) agent for sale, (d) seizure of property while conscious. Then it discusses the legal definition of intoxication: Abu Hanifa's view (loss of basic discrimination) vs. the two Sahibayn (confused speech). The fatwa follows the Sahibayn's definition in matters of impurity and oaths. A concluding note clarifies that if intoxication is from a permissible source, the obligation to make up missed acts of worship does not fall off because it was by his own action.

Key Terms
مكلف (mukallaf): One who is legally responsible (has taklif) and whose actions are subject to reward and punishment.
مغمى عليه (maghmi 'alayh): Unconscious person; his acts (e.g., divorce) are invalid because he lacks intention.
الضاحي (al-dahiya): The conscious person; used as a benchmark for rulings on the intoxicated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the divorce of a person intoxicated from a forbidden substance?
A) It does not take effect.
B) It takes effect.
C) It is suspended until he becomes sober.
D) It depends on the amount consumed.

Key Takeaway
The intoxicated from a forbidden substance is legally responsible and his actions are generally valid, with specific exceptions, while the definition of intoxication follows the Sahibayn for practical rulings.
