The Slave's Legal Incapacity in Hanafi Fiqh
Comprehensive enumeration of slave-specific rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi rulings on slaves across acts of worship, family law, criminal liability, and public authority, using the principle of diminished legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Core Idea
A slave's legal capacity is diminished; many obligations shift to the master and certain acts are invalid without permission.

This dense passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair compiles the specific rulings (ahkam) pertaining to slaves in the Hanafi school. Unlike free persons, slaves have limited rights and obligations, reflecting their status as property. Understanding these rulings requires grasping the underlying principle that the slave lacks full ahliyyah (legal capacity). We will explore the branches (furu') across various chapters of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recognize that all the rulings stem from the slave's diminished legal capacity due to ownership.
The maxim is: 'al-'abd laysa lahu ahliyyah kamilah' (the slave does not have full capacity).
2
Categorize the rulings
Group the rulings into 'ibadat, family law, criminal liability, public authority, and property/transactions.
This helps organize the many furu'.
3
Note deviations from free persons
For each category, compare the slave's ruling with that of a free person. For example, no Friday prayer, half diya, no hadd for slander, etc.
Focus on the practical difference (thamarah).
4
Identify exceptions and conditions
Some rulings have specific conditions (e.g., executor only under Abu Hanifa's conditions) or exceptions (e.g., confession of wealth by ma'dhun).
These are istithna'at from the general prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام العبيد. لا جمعة عليه ولا عيد ولا تشريق ولا أذان ولا إقامة ولا حج ولا عمرة، وصورتها كالرجل ويُزاد البطن والظهر، ويحرم نظر غير المحرم إلى عورتها فقط وما عداها إن اشتهى. ولا يجوز كونه شاهدًا ولا مزكّيًا علانية، ولا عاشرًا ولا قاسما ولا مقوما ولا كاتب حكم ولا أمينا لحاكم ولا إمامًا أعظم ولا قاضيا ولا وليا في نكاح أو قود ولا يلي أمرًا عامًا إلا نيابة عن الإمام الأعظم فله نصب القاضي نيابة عن السلطان، ولو حكم بنفسه لم يصح، ولو أذِنَ لعبده بالقضاء فقضى بعد عتقه جاز بلا تجديد إذن، ولا وصيًّا إلا إذا كان عبد الموصي والورثة صغار، عند الإمام الأعظم، ولا يملك إن ملكه سيده ولا زكاة عليه ولا فطرة وإنما هي على مولاه إن كان للخدمة، ولا أُضحية ولا هدي عليه ولا يكفر إلا بالصوم، ولا يصوم غير فرض إلا بإذن السيد ولا فرضًا وجب إيجابه، وكذا الاعتكاف والحج والعمرة، ولا ينفذ إقراره بمال مأذونا كان أو مكاتبًا إلا بإذن مولاه إلا إذا أقر المأذون بما في يده ولو بعد حجره، وكذا إقراره بجناية موجبة للدفع أو الفداء غير صحيح بخلافه بحد أو قود، ولا ينفرد بتزويج نفسه ويجبر عليه ويجعل صداقًا ويكون نذرًا ورهنا، ولا يرث ولا يورث، ولا تصح كفالته حالة إلا بإذن سيده ولا دية في قتله، وقيمته قائمة مقامها كلاً وبعضا ولا تبلغها ولا عاقلة له ولا هو منهم وحده النصف، ولا إحصان له، وجنايته متعلقة برقبته كديته، ولا سهم له من الغنيمة بل يرضخ له إن قاتل، ويباع في ديته ويدفع في جنايته إن لم يفده سيده وينكح اثنتين ولا تسري له مطلقا، وطلاقها ثنتان وعدتها حيضتان ونصف المقدّر ، ولا لعان بقذفها ولا تنكح على حرَّة، ويصح عتقه عن الكفارات، ولا يحدّ قاذفه وإنما يعزر وقسمها على النصف من قسم الحرة.
Rulings of Slaves. There is no Friday prayer for him, nor Eid, nor Tashriq, nor adhan, nor iqama, nor Hajj, nor Umrah. And her (female slave's) 'awrah is like that of a man, with the addition of the belly and back. And it is forbidden for a non-mahram to look at her 'awrah only; whatever is beyond that is permissible if desire is not present. And it is not permissible for him to be a witness, nor a source of tazkiyah publicly, nor a tenth-collector, nor a land-divider, nor a valuator, nor a court scribe, nor a trustee for a judge, nor a supreme imam, nor a judge, nor a guardian in marriage or qisas, nor does he assume any general authority except as a deputy for the supreme imam, so he may appoint a judge deputizing for the sultan. And if he judges himself, it is not valid. And if (the master) authorized his slave to judge and then the slave judges after being emancipated, it is permissible without renewal of permission. And he is not an executor (of a will) unless it is the slave of the testator and the heirs are minors, according to Imam al-A'zam. And he does not own property if his master owns him, nor does zakat or fitra obligate him; rather it is on his master if he is for service. And there is no udhiyah (sacrifice) or hady (sacrificial animal) on him; and he does not expiate (for sins) except by fasting. And he may not fast any non-obligatory fast without the master's permission, nor any obligatory fast that has become due? (ambiguous). Similarly, i'tikaf, Hajj, and Umrah. And his confession regarding wealth, whether he is a ma'dhun (permitted slave) or mukatab (contracting to buy freedom), is not effective except with the master's permission, unless the ma'dhun confesses regarding what is in his hand, even after being interdicted. Similarly, his confession regarding a crime that requires payment or ransom is not valid, unlike a confession of hadd or qisas. And he does not independently marry himself; he is compelled (by master) and the mahr is made (by master) and becomes a vow and a pledge. And he does not inherit nor is he inherited. And his surety (kafala) is not valid in absolute terms except with the master's permission. And there is no diya for killing him; his value stands in its place wholly or partially, but does not reach it (i.e., diya). And there is no 'aqila for him, nor is he from them; his diya is half. And there is no ihsan (pelvic protection) for him. And his crime is tied to his neck (i.e., he may be sold to pay) like his diya. And there is no share of the spoils for him; rather he is given a reward (radhkh) if he fights. And he is sold for his diya and handed over for his crime if his master does not ransom him. And he may marry two (slave women), but concubinage is absolutely not permissible for him. And his divorce (of a slave woman) counts as two, and her 'idda is two menstrual periods and half of the fixed amount (for free women). And there is no li'an (mutual curse) upon accusing her, and she may not marry a free man. And his emancipation is valid as expiation for sins. And one who slanders him is not flogged with hadd but is given ta'zir. And her portion (of time with husband) is half that of a free woman.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive listing of the legal incapacities and special rulings applying to slaves in Hanafi fiqh. It covers acts of worship (no Friday/Eid prayer, no adhan, no Hajj etc.), criminal liability (diya is half, his crime is tied to his value), family law (can marry two, divorce counts as two, etc.), and public authority (cannot be judge except as deputy). The rulings are based on the principle that the slave lacks full legal capacity (ahliyyah) due to his status as property, and his master bears many obligations on his behalf. Notable points: the slave's 'awrah is more extensive than a man but less than a free woman; his confession in certain matters requires master's permission; he can be emancipated for expiation; slander of a slave carries only ta'zir not hadd. Many of these rulings are derived from the foundational texts of the Hanafi school and are part of the surviving legal framework within classical fiqh.

Key Terms
عبد ('abd): A male slave owned by another person; lacks full legal capacity.
رضخ (radhkh): A grant or reward given to a slave from the spoils of war, less than a full share.
إحصان (ihsan): Legal protection from hadd for adultery due to being married and free. Slaves are not muhsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the diya (blood money) for killing a slave according to this passage?
A) The full diya of a free person.
B) Half the diya of a free person.
C) His value, but not exceeding half of diya.
D) No diya, only the value.

Key Takeaway
The slave's rulings are coherently derived from the principle of diminished legal capacity; a mufti must apply these specific rules when encountering slave-related cases, recognising that the mufta bihi may differ from raw narrations.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Isqat: The General Principle and Distinction Between Ownership and Rights
Introduction to the maxim with key examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ownership (milk) and rights (huquq) and apply the general rule that non-binding rights can drop by isqat while ownership cannot.

Core Idea
Ownership is not extinguished by abandonment, but non-binding rights can be dropped.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi maxim regarding which rights can be dropped (isqat) and which cannot. The author begins by distinguishing between ownership (milk) and rights (huquq) and illustrates the principle with several cases from inheritance, booty, mortgage, watercourse, usufruct, and bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Read the opening sentence: 'If the heir says I have left my right, his right is not invalidated; because ownership is not invalidated by abandonment, but rights are invalidated by it.' Recognize that ownership (milk) is stronger than a mere right (haqq).
This is the foundational principle for all that follows.
2
Analyze the examples of rights that drop
Examine the cases of booty participant, mortgagee, water channel owner (without ownership), usufruct legatee, and bequest settlement. Note that in each, the right is non-binding (ghayr muta'akkid) and therefore susceptible to isqat.
The water channel case shows the key condition: does the right include ownership of the corpus (raqabah)?
3
Identify the Khawaharzadah principle
Read the comment by Khawaharzadah that the right of the legatee and heir before division is 'non-binding' (ghayr muta'akkid) and 'susceptible to dropping by isqat.' This explains why these rights can drop.
The term 'muta'akkid' (binding) recurs as a criterion for whether a right can drop.
4
Summarize the general rule
Synthesize: any right that is not binding (ghayr muta'akkid) or does not involve ownership of the corpus can be dropped by isqat. Ownership itself cannot be dropped by mere saying.
This rule has exceptions to be covered in later lessons.

ما يقبل الإسقاط من الحقوق وما لا يقبله وبيان أن الساقط لا يعود : لو قال الوارث تركت حقي لم يبطل حقه ؛ إذ الملك لا يبطل بالترك والحق يبطل به حتى لو أن أحدًا من الغانمين قال قبل القسمة تركت حقي بطل حقه، وكذا لو قال المرتهن تركت حقي في حبس الرهن بطل كذا في جامع الفصولين وفصول العمادي، وظاهره أن كل حق يسقط بالإسقاط، وهو أيضًا ظاهر ما في الخانية من الشرب ولفظها : رجل له مسيل ماء في دار غيره فباع صاحب الدار داره مع المسيل ورضي به صاحب المسيل كان لصاحب المسيل أن يضرب بذلك في الثمن، وإن كان له حق إجراء الماء دون الرقبة لا شيء له من الثمن ولا سبيل له على المسيل بعد ذلك، كرجل أوصى لرجل بسكنى داره فمات الوصي وباع الوارث الدار ورضي به الموصى له جاز البيع وبطل سكناه، ولو لم يبغ صاحب الدار داره، ولكن قال صاحب المسيل أبطلت حقي في المسيل، فإن كان له حق إجراء الماء دون الرقبة بطل حقه قياسًا على حق السكنى وإن كان له رقبة المسيل لا يبطل ذلك الإبطال . وذكر في الكتاب : إذا أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله ومات الموصي فصالح الوارث الموصى له من الثلث على السدس جاز الصلح وذكر الشيخ الإمام المعروف بخواهر زاده أن حق الموصى له وحق الوارث قبل القسمة غير متأكد يحتمل السقوط بالإسقاط. (انتهى).

فقد علم أن حق الغنائم قبل القسمة وحق حبس الرهن وحق المسيل المجرد وحق الموصى له بالسكنى وحق الموصى له بالثلث قبل القسمة وحق الوارث قبل القسمة على قول خواهر زاده يسقط بالإسقاط ، وصرَّحوا أن حق الشفعة يسقط بالإسقاط، وقالوا حق الرجوع في الهبة لا يسقط، كما في هبة البزازية .
وأما الحق في الوقف؛ فقال قاضيخان في فتاواه من الشهادات في الشهادة بوقف المدرسة : إن مَن كان فقيرًا من أصحاب المدرسة يكون مستحقا للوقف استحقاقا لا يبطل بالإبطال، فإنه لو قال أبطلت حقي كان له أن يطلب ويأخذ بعد ذلك (انتهى). وقد كتبنا في شرح الكنز من الشادات ما فهمه الطرسوسي من عارة قاضيخان وما ردَّه عليه ابن وهبان وما حرَّرناه فيها. وقد بقي حقوق منها خيار الشرط؛ قالوا يسقط به، ومنها خيار الرؤية ؛ قالوا لو أبطله قبل الرؤية بالقول لم يبطل وبالفعل يبطل وبعدها يبطل بهما، ومنها خيار العيب يبطل ،به ومنه الدين يسقط بالإبراء، ومنها حق القصاص يسقط بالعفو، ومنها حق القسم للزوجة يسقط بإسقاطها وإن كان لها الرجوع في المستقبل .

يسقط إلا بالإقالة .
الأ
وقد وقع الاشتباه في مسائل وكثر السؤال عنها ولم أرَ فيها صريحًا بعد التفتيش؛ منها أن بعض الذرية المشروط لهم الربع إذا أسقط حقه لغيره من استحقاقه. ومنها المشروط له النظر إذا أسقط لغيره بأن فرَّغ له عنه إلا أن في اليتيمة وغيرها أن المشروط له النظر إذا فوَّضه لغيره، فإن كان التفويض له على وجه العموم صح تفويضه، وإلا فإن كان في صحته لم يجز، وإن كان عند موته جاز بناء على أن أن يوصي إلى غيره. (انتهى).
للوصي
وفي القنية : إذا عزل الناظر المشروط له النظر عن نفسه لا ينعزل إلا أن يخرجه الواقف أو القاضي. (انتهى).
ومنها أن الواقف إذا شرط لنفسه شرطًا في أصل الوقف كشرط الإدخال والإخراج والزيادة والنقصان والاستبدال فأسقط حقه من هذا الشرط. وينبغي أن يقال بالسقوط في الكل لأنه الأصل في من أسقط حقه من شيء. كما علم سابقا من كلام جامع الفصولين إلا إذا أسقط المشروط له الريع حقه لا لأحد فلا يسقط كما فهمه الطرسوسي، بخلاف ما إذا أسقط حقه لغيره وفيما إذا أسقط الواقف حقه مما شرطه لنفسه أو لغيره. فإن قلت إذا أقرّ المشروط له الريع أو بعضه أنه لا حق له فيه وأنه يستحق فلان فهل يسقط حقه؟ قلت نعم ولو كان مكتوب الوقف بخلافه لما ذكره الخصاف في باب مستقل.
وأما حق المطالبة برفع جذوع الغير الموضوعة على حائطه تعديًا فلا يسقط بالإبراء ولا بالصلح ولا بالعفو ولا بالبيع ولا بالإجارة. كما ذكره البزازي من فصل الاستحقاق فاغتنم هذا التحرير فإن من مفردات هذا التأليف إن شاء الله تعالى ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم.

۲۷۳
And its completion is in Fusul al-'Imadi, and we wrote in Buyu' al-Sharh the flowing of dirhams in the place of dinars in eight. And in Wakalat al-Nihayah: Know that the non-determination of dirhams and dinars is only with respect to entitlement, for they become determined by type, quantity, and description through spending, and that is stated by Imam al-'Attabi in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir.

What rights accept dropping and what do not accept it, and the clarification that what has fallen does not return: If the heir says "I have left my right," his right is not invalidated; because ownership is not invalidated by abandonment, but rights are invalidated by it. So much so that if one of the recipients of booty says before division "I have left my right," his right is invalidated. Similarly, if the mortgagee says "I have left my right in detaining the pawn," it is invalidated. This is in Jami' al-Fusulayn and Fusul al-'Imadi. And its apparent meaning is that every right falls by dropping. It is also apparent from what is in al-Khaniyah concerning watercourse, with its wording: A man has a water channel in someone else's house; then the owner of the house sells his house along with the water channel, and the owner of the water channel consents to it; the owner of the water channel may take a share of the price accordingly. But if he only has the right to run water without ownership (raqabah), he has nothing from the price and no way to the water channel thereafter. This is like a man who bequeaths the usufruct of his house to someone; then the executor dies and the heir sells the house, and the legatee consents; the sale is valid and the usufruct is nullified. And if the owner of the house does not sell his house, but the owner of the water channel says "I have invalidated my right in the water channel," then if he has the right to run water without ownership, his right is invalidated by analogy to the right of usufruct; but if he owns the water channel itself, that invalidation does not take effect. And it is mentioned in the book: If a person bequeaths one-third of his property to someone and the testator dies, and the heir settles with the legatee for one-sixth instead of the one-third, the settlement is valid. And the Shaykh Imam known as Khawaharzadah mentioned that the right of the legatee and the right of the heir before division are non-binding (ghayr muta'akkid) and susceptible to dropping by isqat. (End).

So it is known that the right to booty before division, the right to detain the pawn, the right of the water channel alone (without ownership), the right of the legatee to usufruct, the right of the legatee to one-third before division, and the right of the heir before division according to the statement of Khawaharzadah, all drop by isqat. And they explicitly stated that the right of pre-emption drops by isqat. And they said the right to revoke a gift does not drop, as in Hibat al-Bazzaziyyah.

As for the right in a waqf; Qadikhan said in his Fatawa (in the chapter of testimony regarding testimony of waqf of a school): One who is poor among the people of the school has an entitlement to the waqf that cannot be invalidated by annulment, for if he says "I have invalidated my right," he may still request and take afterward. (End). And we have written in Sharh al-Kanz from al-Shadat what al-Tarsusi understood from the expression of Qadikhan, and what Ibn Wuhban responded to him, and what we verified in that. And there remain rights: including khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation); they said it drops by isqat. Among them is khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection); they said if he invalidates it before seeing by word, it does not drop; by action, it drops; and after seeing, it drops by both. Among them is khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect); it drops by isqat. Among them is debt; it drops by discharge. Among them is the right of qisas; it drops by pardon. Among them is the right of division for the wife; it drops by her dropping it, even though she may return to it in the future.

As for the rights of Allah, they do not accept isqat from the servant. They said if the slandered person pardons and then returns and demands (hadd), it is established? But it is not implemented after his pardon due to the absence of demand. As for contracts that are not binding, they are not described by isqat, such as agency, loan, and acceptance of deposit. As for the right of rental, it should drop only by cancellation (iqalah).

And there have been confusions in some issues, and questions have been frequent, and I have not found an explicit text after investigation. Among them: Some of the descendants for whom a quarter (rub') is stipulated: if they drop their right to another from their entitlement. And among them: the one for whom supervisory authority (nazar) is stipulated: if he drops it for another by assigning it to him, except that in al-Yatimah and others, the one for whom nazar is stipulated, if he delegates it to another, then if the delegation is general in scope, his delegation is valid; otherwise, if it is during his health, it is not permissible, and if at the time of his death, it is permissible based on the fact that he may appoint an executor to another. (End). For the executor?

And in al-Qunyah: If the supervisor (nazir) who is stipulated to have supervisory authority removes himself, he is not removed unless the waqif or the judge removes him. (End).

Among them is the waqif's stipulation of a condition for himself in the original waqf, such as the condition of inclusion and exclusion, increase and decrease, and substitution; then he drops his right from this condition. It should be said that it drops in all cases, because that is the principle for one who drops his right from something, as previously known from the speech of Jami' al-Fusulayn, except if the one for whom the right is stipulated drops his right (the usufruct?) not for anyone, then it does not drop, as understood by al-Tarsusi, contrary to if he drops his right for another, and in case the waqif drops his right from what he stipulated for himself or for another. If you say: If the one for whom the usufruct is stipulated acknowledges that he has no right in it and that so-and-so is entitled to it, does his right drop? I say: Yes, even if the waqf document states otherwise, based on what al-Khassaf mentioned in an independent chapter.

As for the right to demand the removal of another's beams placed on his wall wrongfully, it does not drop by discharge, settlement, pardon, sale, or rental. As al-Bazzazi mentioned in the chapter on entitlement. So seize this editing, for it is among the unique points of this composition, Allah willing. There is no power and no strength except by Allah the Exalted, the Mighty.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi legal maxim regarding which rights can be dropped (isqat) and which cannot, along with numerous applications. The author begins by distinguishing between ownership (milk) and rights (huquq). Ownership is not invalidated by mere abandonment (tark), but certain rights are. For example, if an heir says 'I have left my right,' it does not invalidate his ownership. However, a participant in war booty before division can drop his right. This extends to the mortgagee's right to detain the pawn, the right to a water channel (without ownership), the right to usufruct, and the right to a third of the estate before division according to Khawaharzadah. The right of pre-emption (shuf'a) also drops, but the right to revoke a gift (ruju' fi al-hiba) does not. Importantly, the right in a waqf (endowment) is inalienable: even if a beneficiary says 'I invalidate my right,' he retains the right to claim later. This is based on Qadikhan's fatwa. The author then lists options: khiyar al-shart drops; khiyar al-ru'ya only drops by action before seeing but drops by either word or action after seeing; khiyar al-'ayb drops by isqat; debt drops by discharge; qisas drops by pardon; the wife's right to division drops by her dropping it, but she may reclaim it later. Rights of Allah (hudud) are not subject to isqat by the servant; if the slandered person pardons, the hadd is not enforced because demand is lost. Non-binding contracts like agency, loan, and deposit are not described by isqat. The right of rental only drops by formal cancellation (iqalah). The passage then addresses several problematic cases: descendants' rights in waqf, supervisory authority (nazar), and the waqif's conditional rights. The author concludes with a unique ruling that the right to demand removal of encroaching beams on one's wall does not drop by any means. The overall principle is that rights that are non-binding (ghayr muta'akkid) or purely personal may drop, but rights that are binding or involve ownership (raqabah) or are established by waqf do not. This commentary follows the author's order, explaining each category and its exceptions.

Key Terms
إسقاط (isqat): The act of a right-holder verbally or by action declaring the abandonment of a right, which legally extinguishes it if the right is subject to dropping.
حق (haqq): A legal claim or entitlement that may be financial or non-financial, sometimes subject to isqat, sometimes not.
ساقط لا يعود (saqit la ya'ud): A principle that once a right has been dropped (validly), it cannot be reclaimed.
رقبة (raqabah): Ownership of the substance/corpus of property as opposed to mere usufruct (manfa'a).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following rights does NOT drop by isqat?
A) Right of pre-emption (shuf'a)
B) Right of the mortgagee to detain the pawn
C) Right of a beneficiary in a waqf to receive income
D) Right of a legatee to one-third before division

Key Takeaway
Ownership cannot be abandoned by mere saying, but many non-binding rights can be dropped by isqat.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
Rules of Dropping Rights (Isqat) in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumeration of rights that can and cannot be dropped

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify which rights can be dropped (isqat) and which cannot, and apply the principle of isqat to new cases, including conditions in binding contracts.

Core Idea
Rights of individuals can be dropped; rights of Allah cannot — but even individual rights become binding if embedded in a binding contract.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir lays out the Hanafi rules for dropping rights (isqat). The author enumerates various rights from options, debts, retaliation, and marital division, then contrasts them with rights of Allah that cannot be dropped. He also addresses nuanced cases where dropping is ineffective because the right is tied to a binding obligation. As a mufti, you will often encounter questions about whether a person can relinquish a stipulation in a waqf or contract; this lesson provides the principles to answer such questions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between haqq Allah and haqq al-ibad
Identify which rights belong to Allah (e.g., hudud punishments, acts of worship) and which belong to individuals (e.g., debts, options). The text states that huquq Allah 'do not accept dropping by the servant.'
Rights of Allah are established for public benefit and cannot be waived by an individual.
2
List rights that can be dropped and their method
For each right mentioned (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, khiyar al-'ayb, debt, retaliation, wife's right to division), note whether dropping occurs by statement, action, or both. For example, khiyar al-shart is dropped by the same action that exercises it.
Some rights require explicit words; others can be dropped by conduct.
3
Identify rights that cannot be dropped
Besides huquq Allah, also note that non-binding contracts (agency, loan, trust) are 'not characterized by dropping' because they are not owned rights. Hire contracts are dropped only by dissolution (iqala).
Non-binding contracts can be terminated but not 'dropped' as a right.
4
Understand the bindingness (luzum) exception
The passage teaches that if a right is embedded in a binding contract (e.g., a condition in a waqf, or delivery location in salam), it cannot be dropped unilaterally. The stipulation becomes binding like the contract itself.
This is a key nuance: even a personal right can become irrevocable when part of a binding agreement.
5
Apply the principle to the waqf fatwa
The author gives a fatwa: a waqif who stipulated conditions for himself and a judge ruled on the endowment cannot later drop those conditions. The ruling made the conditions binding.
The lesson: once a right is affirmed by a judge's ruling, it becomes enforceable and cannot be dropped by the right-holder alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه ابن وهبان وما حرَّرناه فيها. وقد بقي حقوق منها خيار الشرط؛ قالوا يسقط به، ومنها خيار الرؤية ؛ قالوا لو أبطله قبل الرؤية بالقول لم يبطل وبالفعل يبطل وبعدها يبطل بهما، ومنها خيار العيب يبطل ،به ومنه الدين يسقط بالإبراء، ومنها حق القصاص يسقط بالعفو، ومنها حق القسم للزوجة يسقط بإسقاطها وإن كان لها الرجوع في المستقبل . · وأما حقوق الله تعالى فلا تقبل الإسقاط من العبد قالوا لو عفا المقذوف ثم عاد وطلب حُدَّ ، لكن لا يُقام بعد عفوه لفقد الطلب، وأما ما ليس بلازم من العقود فلا يتّصف بالإسقاط كالوكالة والعارية وقبول الوديعة وأما حق الإجارة فينبغي يسقط إلا بالإقالة . وقد وقع الاشتباه في مسائل وكثر السؤال عنها ولم أرَ فيها صريحًا بعد التفتيش؛ منها أن بعض الذرية المشروط لهم الربع إذا أسقط حقه لغيره من استحقاقه. ومنها المشروط له النظر إذا أسقط لغيره بأن فرَّغ له عنه إلا أن في اليتيمة وغيرها أن المشروط له النظر إذا فوَّضه لغيره، فإن كان التفويض له على وجه العموم صح تفويضه، وإلا فإن كان في صحته لم يجز، وإن كان عند موته جاز بناء على أن أن يوصي إلى غيره. (انتهى). للوصي وفي القنية : إذا عزل الناظر المشروط له النظر عن نفسه لا ينعزل إلا أن يخرجه الواقف أو القاضي. (انتهى). ومنها أن الواقف إذا شرط لنفسه شرطًا في أصل الوقف كشرط الإدخال والإخراج والزيادة والنقصان والاستبدال فأسقط حقه من هذا الشرط. وينبغي أن يقال بالسقوط في الكل لأنه الأصل في من أسقط حقه من شيء. كما علم سابقا من كلام جامع الفصولين إلا إذا أسقط المشروط له الريع حقه لا لأحد فلا يسقط كما فهمه الطرسوسي، بخلاف ما إذا أسقط حقه لغيره وفيما إذا أسقط الواقف حقه مما شرطه لنفسه أو لغيره. فإن قلت إذا أقرّ المشروط له الريع أو بعضه أنه لا حق له فيه وأنه يستحق فلان فهل يسقط حقه؟ قلت نعم ولو كان مكتوب الوقف بخلافه لما ذكره الخصاف في باب مستقل. وأما حق المطالبة برفع جذوع الغير الموضوعة على حائطه تعديًا فلا يسقط بالإبراء ولا بالصلح ولا بالعفو ولا بالبيع ولا بالإجارة. كما ذكره البزازي من فصل الاستحقاق فاغتنم هذا التحرير فإن من مفردات هذا التأليف إن شاء الله تعالى ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم. وفي إيضاح الكرماني من السلم : لو قال ربّ السلم أسقطت حقي في التسليم في ذلك المكان أو البلد لم يسقط . (انتهى). وقد وقعت حادثة سُئِلتُ عنها : شرط الواقف له شروطا من إدخال وإخراج وغيرهما وحكم بالوقف متضمنا للشروط حاكم حنفي ثم رجع الواقف عما شرطه لنفسه من الشروط . فأجبت بعدم صحة لأن رجوعه الوقف بعد الحكم ،لازم كما صرَّحوا به بسبب الحكم وهو شامل للشروط فلزمت كلزومه كما صرح به الطرسوسي فيمن أسقط حقه فيما شرط له من الريع لا لأحد، فإنه قال بعدم السقوط. وعلته أن الاشتراط له صار لازمًا كلزوم الوقف كما أن المشروط لا يملك إسقاط ما شرطه له فكذا الشارط ويدلّ عليه أيضًا ما نقلناه عن إيضاح الكرماني من إسقاط ربّ السلم حقه مما شرط له من تسليم المسلم فيه في مكان معين، فإنه يدل على أن الشرط إذا كان في ضمن لازم فإنه يلزم ولا يقبل الإسقاط .
Upon it [the text] Ibn Wahban and what we have recorded in it. And there remain rights from among them: the option of stipulation; they said it is dropped by it. And among them: the option of sight; they said if he invalidates it before sight by statement, it is not invalidated, but by action it is invalidated, and after sight it is invalidated by both. And among them: the option of defect; it is dropped by it. And from it: debt is dropped by discharge. And among them: the right of retaliation is dropped by pardon. And among them: the right of division for the wife is dropped by her dropping it, though she may return in the future. As for the rights of Allah Most High, they do not accept dropping by the servant. They said: if the slandered one pardons, then returns and demands the prescribed punishment, it is not imposed after his pardon due to lack of demand. As for what is not binding from contracts, it is not characterized by dropping, such as agency, loan of an object, and acceptance of a trust. As for the right of hire, it should be dropped only by dissolution. Confusion has occurred in some issues and questions have multiplied, and I have not seen explicitly after investigation: among them is that some descendants who are stipulated a quarter, if he drops his right to someone else from his entitlement. And among them is the one stipulated supervision, if he drops it to someone else by vacating it for him, except that in al-Yatima and others, the one stipulated supervision if he delegates it to someone else, then if the delegation is general, his delegation is valid; otherwise, if it is during his health, it is not permissible; if at his death, it is permissible based on that he may will to another. (End). For the executor: and in al-Quniyya: if the supervisor stipulated supervision removes himself, he is not removed unless the waqif or judge removes him. (End). And among them: if the waqif stipulates for himself a condition in the original endowment, such as a condition of entry, exit, increase, decrease, or substitution, then drops his right from this condition, it should be said that it is dropped in all because that is the principle for one who drops his right from something, as previously known from the statement of Jami' al-Fusulayn, except if the one stipulated the usufruct drops his right not to anyone, then it is not dropped as understood by al-Tarsusi, contrary to if he drops his right to someone else, and in the case where the waqif drops his right from what he stipulated for himself or for another. If you say: if the one stipulated the usufruct acknowledges that he has no right in it and that so-and-so is entitled, does his right drop? I say: yes, even if the endowment document states otherwise, due to what al-Khassaf mentioned in a separate chapter. As for the right to demand removal of another's beams placed on his wall wrongfully, it is not dropped by discharge, nor by compromise, nor by pardon, nor by sale, nor by hire, as mentioned by al-Bazzazi from the chapter of entitlement. So seize this recording, for it is among the unique points of this composition, God willing, and there is no power except with Allah the Exalted. In Idah al-Kirmani from salam: if the principal of salam says 'I have dropped my right regarding delivery in that place or town', it is not dropped. (End). And an incident occurred about which I was asked: a waqif stipulated conditions for himself of entry and exit etc., and a Hanafi judge ruled on the endowment including the conditions, then the waqif retracted from the conditions he stipulated for himself. So I answered that it is not valid, because his retraction after the ruling is binding, as they explicitly stated due to the ruling including the conditions, so they become binding as it is binding, as stated by al-Tarsusi regarding one who drops his right from the usufruct stipulated for him not to anyone, that he said it is not dropped. Its reason is that the stipulation for him became binding like the binding of the endowment, just as the one for whom something is stipulated does not own dropping what is stipulated for him, likewise the stipulator. And it is also indicated by what we transmitted from Idah al-Kirmani about the principal of salam dropping his right from what is stipulated for him regarding delivery of the salam commodity in a specific place, for it indicates that when a condition is within a binding [contract], it becomes binding and does not accept dropping.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rules (rasm) regarding which rights can be dropped (isqat) and which cannot. The author lists several rights from the chapter of options and other areas. The key principle is that rights of individuals (huquq al-'ibad) can generally be dropped by the possessor, while rights of Allah (huquq Allah) cannot be dropped by a servant. The author then delves into nuanced cases: options like khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, khiyar al-'ayb are dropped by explicit action or statement under certain conditions. Debt drops by discharge, retaliation by pardon, and the wife's right to division by her dropping it, though she may reclaim in future. Rights of Allah, such as hadd for slander, are not dropped by the victim's pardon; once pardoned, the punishment is not imposed because the demand is lost. Non-binding contracts like agency, loan, and acceptance of a trust are not subject to dropping. Hire contracts are only dropped by dissolution (iqala). The author then addresses problematic cases (mushtabahat) that he could not find explicit rulings for after research: descendants entitled to a quarter, supervisors dropping their right, and waqf conditions. He cites various sources like al-Yatima, al-Quniyya, Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Tarsusi, al-Bazzazi, and al-Khassaf. The overall thrust is that the principle is that a right can be dropped unless it is a right of Allah or is embedded in a binding contract such that dropping it would undermine the contract's binding nature. The passage ends with a fatwa on a waqf case: if a waqif stipulates conditions for himself and a judge rules on the endowment, the conditions become binding and the waqif cannot later drop them unilaterally.

Key Terms
إسقاط (isqat): The act of dropping or relinquishing a right voluntarily
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right belonging to Allah, such as prescribed punishments and acts of worship
لازم (lazim): Binding or obligatory; a contract or stipulation that cannot be unilaterally rescinded

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following statements is true regarding the right to demand removal of another's beams placed wrongfully on one's wall?
A) It is dropped by discharge (ibra') alone.
B) It is dropped by compromise (sulh) alone.
C) It is not dropped by any of the mentioned means (ibra', sulh, pardon, sale, hire).
D) It is dropped by pardon when the offender apologizes.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, rights of individuals can generally be dropped, but rights of Allah cannot, and any right that has become binding (lazim) through contract or court ruling also cannot be unilaterally dropped.

The Maxim: The Dropped Does Not Return (الساقط لا يعود) and Its Applications
Explanation of a qawida with furuat and fatwa incidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'الساقط لا يعود' by distinguishing genuine dropping (sāqiṭ) from temporary prevention (māni‘) and derive rulings for diverse furuat.

Core Idea
A genuinely dropped right never returns; only removal of a preventer revives it.

This lesson introduces the foundational legal maxim 'الساقط لا يعود' (the dropped does not return). The source passage presents a detailed explanation of this principle, illustrating it with numerous practical examples from ibadat, muamalat, and qada. Crucially, it distinguishes between genuine extinguishment (sāqiṭ) and temporary prevention (māni‘), which is the key to correct application. By mastering this maxim, you will be able to resolve cases where a right or effect appears to have been lost but may or may not be revivable.

Guided Path
1
Understand the maxim and its scope
State the maxim clearly: 'الساقط لا يعود' means that a right or legal effect that has truly fallen away cannot be revived. It applies across all fiqh chapters. Identify the key term 'sāqiṭ' as a genuine extinguishment.
The maxim is a wusta-rank kullyah.
2
Distinguish between sāqiṭ and māni‘
Learn the criterion given in the passage: if the effective cause (muqtadi) for the ruling still exists but the ruling is absent, it is a preventer (māni‘). If the cause itself is absent, it is a true drop (sāqiṭ). Only removal of a preventer can restore the ruling.
Forgetfulness is a preventer; dropping due to few missed prayers is a true drop.
3
Apply the maxim to the furuat
For each application in the passage, determine whether the case involves a sāqiṭ or a māni‘. For example, in salam, dropping the right to delivery is a genuine drop (right was binding, cannot be unilaterally dropped). For maintenance after nushuz, it is a preventer (cause exists, so returns).
Work through the list: waqf conditions, najasah, rescission of rescission, etc.
4
Identify the exception and the complementary maxim
Recognize that when dropping is due to a preventer (e.g., forgetfulness), the complementary maxim 'زوال المانع يعيد' applies. This is not a true exception but a clarification: only removal of a preventer restores the effect.
The exception is only apparent; it reaffirms the original maxim.
5
Synthesize using the fatwa cases
Analyze the fatwa incidents: the discharge-then-acknowledgment case and the contradictory confession case. Apply the distinction to determine that the debts have genuinely dropped and do not return. Also consider the khiyar dispute among mashayikh.
The khiyar dispute illustrates how disagreement arises when the classification (sāqiṭ vs. māni‘) is ambiguous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي إيضاح الكرماني من السلم: لو قال ربّ السلم أسقطت حقي في التسليم في ذلك المكان أو البلد لم يسقط. (انتهى). وقد وقعت حادثة سُئِلتُ عنها: شرط الواقف له شروطا من إدخال وإخراج وغيرهما وحكم بالوقف متضمنا للشروط حاكم حنفي ثم رجع الواقف عما شرطه لنفسه من الشروط. فأجبت بعدم صحة لأن رجوعه الوقف بعد الحكم لازم كما صرَّحوا به بسبب الحكم وهو شامل للشروط فلزمت كلزومه كما صرح به الطرسوسي فيمن أسقط حقه فيما شرط له من الريع لا لأحد، فإنه قال بعدم السقوط. وعلته أن الاشتراط له صار لازمًا كلزوم الوقف كما أن المشروط لا يملك إسقاط ما شرطه له فكذا الشارط ويدلّ عليه أيضًا ما نقلناه عن إيضاح الكرماني من إسقاط ربّ السلم حقه مما شرط له من تسليم المسلم فيه في مكان معين، فإنه يدل على أن الشرط إذا كان في ضمن لازم فإنه يلزم ولا يقبل الإسقاط . بيان أن الساقط لا يعود : فلا يعود الترتيب بعد سقوطه بقلة الفوائت بخلاف ما إذا سقط بالنسيان فإنه يعود بالتذكّر لأن النسيان كان مانعا لا مُسقِطًا فهو من باب زوال المانع. ولا تعود النجاسة بعد الحكم بزوالها؛ فلو دبغ الجلد بالتشميس ونحوه، وفرك الثوب من المني وجفت الأرض بالشمس ثم أصابها ماء لا تعود النجاسة في الأصح، وكذا البئر إذا غار ماؤها ثم عاد ومنه عدم صحة الإقالة للإقالة في السلم لأنه دين سقط فلا يعود، وأما النفقة بعد سقوطها بالنشوز بالرجوع فهو من باب زوال المانع لا من باب عود الساقط. وعلى هذا اختلف المشايخ في بعض مسائل في الخيارات من البيوع، فمنهم من قال يعود الخيار نظرًا إلى أنه مانع زال فعمل المقتضي ومنهم من قال لا يعود نظرًا إلى أنه ساقط لا يعود، وقد ذكرناه في الشرح والأصل أن المقتضي للحكم إن كان موجودًا والحكم معدوم فهو من باب المانع وإن عدم المقتضي فهو من باب الساقط، وقد وقعت حادثة الفتوى: أبرأه عامًا ثم أقرَّ بعده بالمال المبرأ منه عاما فهل يعود بعد سقوط كله؟ فأجبت بأنه لا يعود لما في جامع الفصولين: برهن أنه أبرأني من هذه الدعوى ثم ادعى المدعي ثانيا أنه أقر لي بالمال بعد إبرائي؛ فلو قال المدعى عليه أبرأني وقبلت الإبراء أو قال صدقت لا يصح هذا الدفع، يعني دعوى الإقرار ولو لم يقبله يصح الدفع لاحتمال الرّد فالإبراء يرتد بالرد فبقي المال عليه. (انتهى). وفي التاتارخانية من كتاب الإقرار: لو قال لا حق لي عليك فاشهد لي عليك درهم ، فقال نعم لا حق لك عليَّ ثم أشهد أن له عليه ألف والشهود يسمعون ذلك كله. فهذا باطل ولا يلزمه شيء ولا يسع الشهود أن يشهدوا عليه (انتهى). وفرَّعت على قولهم الساقط لا يعود قولهم إذا حكم القاضي برد شهادة الشاهد مع وجود الأهلية لفسق أو لتهمة فإنه لا يقبل بعد ذلك في تلك الحادثة.
In Idah al-Kirmani on salam: If the buyer of salam says 'I have dropped my right to delivery in that place or town,' it is not dropped. (End). And an incident occurred that I was asked about: The waqif stipulated conditions for himself concerning inclusion, exclusion, etc., and a Hanafi judge ruled on the waqf including the conditions, then the waqif retracted from the conditions he stipulated for himself. I answered that it is not valid because his retraction after the ruling is binding, as they explicitly stated due to the ruling including the conditions, so they became binding just like the waqf becomes binding, as al-Tarsusi stated concerning one who dropped his right to what was stipulated for him of the proceeds not for anyone, for he said it is not dropped. The reason is that the stipulation for him became binding like the binding of the waqf, just as the one for whom the stipulation is made does not own dropping what was stipulated for him, likewise the stipulator. And this is also supported by what we narrated from Idah al-Kirmani about the salam buyer dropping his right to delivery of the salam object in a specific place, for it indicates that if a condition is within something binding, it becomes binding and does not accept dropping. Statement that the dropped does not return: So the order (tartib) does not return after dropping due to few missed prayers, unlike if it dropped due to forgetfulness, then it returns with remembrance because forgetfulness was a preventer, not a dropper, so it is from the chapter of removal of preventer. And najasah does not return after the ruling of its removal; so if one tans skin by sunning and such, and rubs a garment from semen, and the earth dries by the sun, then water hits them, najasah does not return in the sound view, and likewise the well if its water recedes then returns. And from this is the invalidity of rescission of rescission in salam because it is a debt that dropped and does not return. As for maintenance after dropping due to nushuz by returning, it is from the chapter of removal of preventer, not from the chapter of return of the dropped. And upon this the mashayikh differed in some issues concerning options in sales: some said the option returns, considering it a preventer that ceased so the effective cause operates; and some said it does not return, considering it dropped and does not return. We mentioned it in the commentary and the principle is that if the effective cause (muqtadi) for the ruling exists and the ruling is non-existent, it is from the chapter of preventer; and if the effective cause is absent, it is from the chapter of the dropped. And a fatwa incident occurred: He gave a general discharge (ibra) for a year, then afterwards he acknowledged the wealth from which he was discharged for a year. Does it return after its entire dropping? I answered that it does not return, because in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If he proves that he discharged me from this claim, then the plaintiff claims again that he acknowledged the wealth for me after my discharge; if the defendant says 'He discharged me and I accepted the discharge' or says 'I affirm,' this defense is invalid, meaning the claim of acknowledgment, and if he did not accept it the defense is valid due to possibility of rejection, so the discharge is rejected by rejection and the wealth remains upon him. (End). And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from the book of Iqrrar: If someone says 'No right of mine is upon you, so bear witness for me that you owe me a dirham,' and he says 'Yes, no right of yours is upon me,' then he makes witnesses that he owes him a thousand while the witnesses hear all of that. This is invalid and nothing is binding upon him, and it is not permissible for the witnesses to testify against him. (End). And I derived from their statement 'the dropped does not return' their statement: 'If the judge rules to reject the testimony of a witness while he possesses eligibility, due to fisk or accusation, then he is not accepted thereafter in that incident.'
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the legal maxim 'the dropped does not return' (الساقط لا يعود). The author begins by citing examples from salam and waqf to illustrate that once a right has been established as binding (e.g., a stipulation in a contract or a ruling), the party who holds that right cannot unilaterally drop it. The core principle is that if a legal effect has genuinely fallen away (like a debt that is discharged or a right that is extinguished), it cannot be revived. However, if the absence of the effect was due to a preventer (مانع) rather than true dropping, then removal of the preventer brings the effect back. The author provides several applications: the order of prayers (ترتيب) lost due to few missed prayers does not return, while if lost due to forgetfulness, it returns (because forgetfulness is a preventer). Similarly, najasah removed by drying or tanning does not return upon moisture; a well's water that recedes and returns does not bring back najasah. In salam, rescission of a rescission is invalid because the debt from salam has dropped. Maintenance dropped due to nushuz returns upon the wife's return, because that is removal of preventer. The author notes a difference among mashayikh concerning khiyar (option) in sales: some analogize it to a preventer so it returns when the preventer is gone; others say it is genuinely dropped so it does not return. The author clarifies the criterion: if the effective cause (muqtadi) still exists but the ruling is absent, it is a preventer; if the cause itself is absent, it is a drop. Two fatwa cases follow: one about discharging a debt and then acknowledging it (does not revive), and another about contradictory confessions (invalid). Finally, a derivation: if a judge rejects a witness due to fisq or accusation, that witness cannot be accepted later for that same incident, because his testimony has dropped.

Key Terms
ساقط (sāqiṭ): A right or legal effect that has been genuinely extinguished and cannot be revived.
مانع (māni‘): A preventer that temporarily blocks the effect of a legal cause; removing it restores the effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the order (tartib) of prayers not return after being lost due to a few missed prayers, but does return after forgetfulness?
A) Because forgetfulness is a preventer, not a dropper
B) Because the effective cause is absent in forgetfulness
C) Because order is not a legal right
D) Because the prayers themselves drop

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'الساقط لا يعود' is a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh; it differentiates between genuine extinguishment and mere prevention, and its correct application requires careful analysis of whether the cause (muqtadi) still exists.

The Sleeping Person is Like the Awake in Eleven Cases
Listing cases where the sleeping person is legally treated as awake

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-nā'im ka al-mustayqiẓ' to eleven specific cases and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
A sleeping person is legally like an awake person in specific cases where his body directly causes a legal effect.

Does unconsciousness absolve one from liability? In Hanafi law, a sleeping person is not entirely off the hook. This lesson explores a set of cases collected by the later Hanafi jurist al-Walwaliji where the sleeping person is treated as awake – from fasting and ihram to property damage and inheritance. By working through these furū‘, you will see how the school applies the sub-maxim (ḍābiṭ) 'al-nā'im ka al-mustayqiẓ' with precision.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the Arabic text of the maxim: النائم كالمستيقظ. Note that it is a restrictive sub-maxim (ḍābiṭ) governing specific fiqh chapters: ibadāt (fasting, hajj), mu‘āmalāt (damages), and jināyāt (inheritance/homicide).
This maxim does not apply universally; it is limited to the cases enumerated by al-Walwaliji.
2
Work through the first three cases (fasting)
Analyse cases 1–3: rain drop entering mouth, intercourse with sleeping spouse, and intercourse while in ihram. Notice that the maxim makes the sleeping person responsible for effects entering his body or arising from his marital relationship.
In case 3, the sleeping muhrima still owes kaffārah because the act of intercourse is attributed to her as a cause.
3
Work through cases 4–7 (ihram and hunting)
Cases 4–6 involve a muhrim who is asleep: shaving his head, rolling onto game, and sleeping on a camel entering ‘Arafāt. The maxim attributes the acts (done by others or by his own body) to him. Case 7 treats game that dies near a sleeping person as carrion because he is unable to slaughter.
Sleeping on the camel suffices for wuqūf because intention is not required for standing at ‘Arafāt.
4
Work through cases 8–10 (property and homicide)
Case 8: rolling onto goods – liability for compensation because his body caused damage. Case 9: father sleeping under wall, son falls on him – father barred from inheritance as he indirectly caused death. Case 10: someone places sleeping person under wall – placer not liable because the sleeping person is not an agent.
The distinction between cases 9 and 10 hinges on whether the sleeping person played a causal role.
5
Work through case 11 (marriage) and synthesise
Case 11: khulwah (seclusion) is invalid if a sleeping stranger is present, because presence (even asleep) prevents true seclusion. Synthesise the common thread: the maxim applies when the sleeping person’s body, personal status (like ihram), or relationship (like marriage) is the direct cause of the legal effect.
Other cases beyond these eleven exist (al-Walwaliji mentions twenty-five in total).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن النائم كالمستيقظ في بعض المسائل: قال الولوالجي في آخر فتاواه : النائم كالمستيقظ في خمس وعشرين مسألة : الأولى : إذا نام الصائم على قفاه وفوه مفتوح فقطر قطرة من ماء المطر في فيه فسد صومه، وكذا وقطر أحد قطرة من الماء في فيه وبلغ ذلك جوفه. الثانية : إذا جامعها زوجها وهي نائمة يفسد صومها. الثالثة : لو كانت محرمة فجامعها زوجها وهي نائمة فعليها الكفارة. الرابعة : المحرم إذا نام فجاء رجل فحلق رأسه وجب الجزاء عليه. الخامسة : المحرم إذا نام فانقلب على صيد فقتله وجب عليه الجزاء. السادسة : إذا نام المحرم على بعير ودخل في عرفات فقد أدرك الحج. السابعة : الصيد المرمى إليه بالسهم إذا وقع عند نائم من تلك الرمية فمات يكون حرامًا كما إذا وقع عند يقظان وهو قادر على ذكاته. الثامنة : إذا انقلب النائم على متاع وكسره وجب الضمان. التاسعة : الأب إذا نام تحت جدار فوقع الابن عليه من سطح وهو نائم فمات الابن يحرم عن الميراث على قول البعض، وهو الصحيح. العاشرة : مَن رفع النائم ووضعه تحت جدار فسقط عليه الجدار ومات لا يلزمه الضمان . الحادية عشرة : رجل خلا بمرأته وثمة أجنبي نائم لا تصح الخلوة.
Statement that the sleeping person is like the awake in some issues: al-Walwaliji said at the end of his Fatawa: 'The sleeping person is like the awake in twenty-five issues: First: If a fasting person sleeps on his back with his mouth open and a drop of rain falls into his mouth, his fast is broken; likewise if someone drops a drop of water into his mouth and it reaches his stomach. Second: If her husband has intercourse with her while she is sleeping, her fast is broken. Third: If she was in ihram and her husband had intercourse with her while she was sleeping, she owes kaffarah. Fourth: If a muhrim sleeps and a man comes and shaves his head, the muhrim owes fidyah. Fifth: If a muhrim sleeps and rolls onto game and kills it, he owes fidyah. Sixth: If a muhrim sleeps on a camel and enters Arafat, he has performed the hajj. Seventh: Game shot with an arrow that falls near a sleeping person and dies is haram, just as if it falls near an awake person who is able to slaughter it. Eighth: If a sleeping person rolls onto goods and breaks them, he is liable for compensation. Ninth: If a father sleeps under a wall and the son falls on him from a roof while he is sleeping and the son dies, the father is barred from inheritance according to some; this is the correct view. Tenth: Someone who lifts a sleeping person and places him under a wall, then the wall falls on him and he dies, the lifter is not liable for compensation. Eleventh: A man who is alone with his wife while there is a sleeping stranger present, the seclusion is not valid (i.e., it is not true khulwah).'
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage presents a set of cases collected by al-Walwaliji illustrating the principle that a sleeping person is legally treated as awake in certain situations. The principle is that a sleeping person can still be the cause of legal effects, especially when those effects arise from his own body or from actions that occur to him. The cases cover fasting, ihram, hunting, property damage, inheritance, and marriage. For example, in fasting, if water enters the mouth of a sleeping person and reaches the stomach, the fast breaks because the mouth is a direct entry point (fuqaha consider it like eating/drinking). Similarly, intercourse with a sleeping spouse breaks her fast and may require kaffarah if she is in ihram. In ihram, if someone shaves the head of a sleeping muhrim, the muhrim still owes fidyah because he is the one in ihram; the action is attributed to him for purposes of compensation. Rolling onto game and killing it also imposes fidyah because it is direct causing of death. Sleeping on a camel entering Arafat suffices for hajj because intention is not required for standing. Game that falls near a sleeping person is considered carrion (not halal) because he is unable to slaughter it. For property damage, if a sleeping person rolls and breaks goods, he is liable because his body caused the damage (like an awake person). In inheritance, if a sleeping father is under a wall and his son falls on him, the father is barred from inheriting because he caused the son's death (though unintentionally). However, if someone else places a sleeping person under a wall and it collapses, the placer is not liable because the sleeping person is not an agent. Finally, seclusion (khulwah) is invalid if there is a sleeping stranger present, because the presence of a third party (even asleep) prevents true seclusion.

Key Terms
النائم (al-nā‘im): A person who is asleep; in these cases, his legal responsibility is similar to an awake person's in specific circumstances.
المستيقظ (al-mustayqiẓ): The awake person; the standard of legal responsibility against which the sleeping person is measured in these cases.
الفدية (al-fidyah): Compensation (often a sacrifice or charity) required for violations committed while in ihram, e.g., shaving head or killing game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a sleeping person rolls onto someone's merchandise and breaks it, what is the ruling?
A) The sleeping person is not liable because he was unconscious
B) The owner of the merchandise is liable for leaving it in the way
C) The sleeping person is liable for compensation
D) No liability because property damage requires intent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sub-maxim 'al-nā'im ka al-mustayqiẓ' establishes that a sleeping person bears legal responsibility in specific cases where his body directly causes a legal effect, covering ibadāt, mu‘āmalāt, and jināyāt.

The Maxim 'The Fallen Does Not Return' and Its Applications
A maxim with two applications: contradictory acknowledgment and rejected witness testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'as-saqit la ya'ud' (the fallen does not return) to cases of contradictory acknowledgment and rejected testimony, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A right that has been dropped cannot be revived — once a claim is denied or a witness rejected, the opportunity is permanently lost.

In this lesson, we examine a concise maxim from the Hanafi legal tradition: 'الساقط لا يعود' (The fallen does not return). The passage from al-Tatarkhaniyya presents two concrete applications: a case of contradictory acknowledgment in the book of Iqrar, and a ruling on rejected testimony. Both illustrate how a right or status that has fallen cannot be restored, a principle with significant practical consequences for muftis and judges.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Begin by memorizing the maxim in Arabic (الساقط لا يعود) and understanding its plain meaning: anything that has fallen (a right, status, or circumstance) does not return to its previous state. This is a subsidiary maxim (dabt) governing testimony, acknowledgment, and rights.
The maxim is related to 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك'.
2
Analyze the iqrar case
Read the case from al-Tatarkhaniyya: a person first says 'I have no right against you' (negating any claim), then later acknowledges a debt of a thousand dirhams in the presence of witnesses. The first statement drops the right permanently; the second is void. Apply the maxim: the fallen (the right to claim) does not return.
The witnesses heard both statements, so the contradiction is clear.
3
Analyze the witness rejection case
The author derived a branch: if a judge rejects a competent witness's testimony due to fasiq (immorality) or tuhma (suspicion), that witness cannot be accepted again in the same incident. The rejection drops the witness's acceptability permanently for that case.
This is an explicit application of the same maxim to testimony law.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and scope
Both rulings are from authoritative fatwa literature (al-Tatarkhaniyya) and are considered operative (mufta bihi). The maxim applies broadly where a right or status has been definitively negated and cannot be revived by later actions.
No exception (istithna) is mentioned in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التاتارخانية من كتاب الإقرار : لو قال لا حق لي عليك فاشهد لي عليك درهم ، فقال نعم لا حق لك عليَّ ثم أشهد أن له عليه ألف والشهود يسمعون ذلك كله. فهذا باطل ولا يلزمه شيء ولا يسع الشهود أن يشهدوا عليه (انتهى). وفرَّعت على قولهم الساقط لا يعود قولهم إذا حكم القاضي برد شهادة الشاهد مع وجود الأهلية لفسق أو لتهمة فإنه لا يقبل بعد ذلك في تلك الحادثة.
In al-Tatarkhaniyya from the Book of Acknowledgment: If someone says, 'I have no right against you, so witness for me a dirham against you,' and the other says, 'Yes, you have no right against me,' then later acknowledges that he owes him a thousand while the witnesses hear all of that — this is void, nothing is binding upon him, and it is not permissible for the witnesses to testify against him. (End). And I derived (as a branch) upon their statement 'the fallen does not return' their statement: If a judge rejects a witness's testimony despite his competence due to immorality or suspicion, then he is not accepted thereafter in that incident.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage presents two layers: first, a specific case from al-Tatarkhaniyya about a contradictory acknowledgment that is void because the first denial negates the later claim — the 'right' that fell cannot return. Second, the author applies the same maxim 'الساقط لا يعود' to a rule of evidence: once a witness's testimony is rejected even if he was qualified, the rejection stands permanently for that case. This is a qawida (legal maxim) with a practical furu in testimony law.

Key Terms
الساقط (as-sāqiṭ): That which has fallen or been dropped, i.e., a right or status that has been extinguished or negated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the witnesses did not hear the first statement.
B) Because the first statement negated any right, and the fallen cannot return.
C) Because the acknowledgment was for a different amount.
D) Because the witnesses were not qualified.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'الساقط لا يعود' prevents revival of any right that has been definitively negated, whether by prior denial or judicial rejection.

The Sleeping Person is Like the Awake: A Dabt Applied Across Fiqh
A legal maxim expanded with 25 specific rulings across fiqh chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'an-nā'im ka al-mustayqiẓ' to at least five furu' cases and identify when exceptions or ikhtilaf arise.

Core Idea
The sleeping person is legally equivalent to the awake for liability and obligation, but not for conscious intent.

This passage from al-Walwaliji's Fatawa compiles 25 specific rulings where a sleeping person is treated identically to an awake person. The maxim 'النائم كالمستيقظ' serves as a dabt (restrictive sub-rule) that allows a mufti to quickly analogize across chapters of fiqh. Understanding these cases strengthens your ability to apply qawaid in fatwa and to recognize legitimate ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its usul classification
Identify that this is a dabt (sughra) – a restrictive sub-maxim that limits a broader rule. The maxim is not universal; it applies only in these 25 cases and similar ones by analogy.
The rank is sughra because it is limited to specific issues, not a universal qa'ida kubra.
2
Map the furu' by fiqh chapter
Group the 25 cases into chapters: Sawm (1-3), Hajj (4-7), damages (8-10), khalwa (11-13), rada' (14), tayammum (15), salat (16-19), ayman (20), talaq (21-22), musahara (23-24), janaba (25). This shows the maxim's breadth.
Some cases may fit multiple chapters; use the dominant theme.
3
Analyse one representative case per chapter
For each chapter, take one case and explain why the maxim applies. For example, case 1: rain in a sleeping fasting person's mouth breaks the fast – because eating/drinking invalidates fast regardless of awareness.
The operative cause (illa) is the physical occurrence of the act, not intention.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf and exceptions
Case 22 (Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad) shows disagreement on whether the sleeping husband's passive reception of a kiss makes him a revocator. Also note case 19 where opinions vary on sajda al-tilawa. These indicate limits of the maxim.
The mufta bihi in case 22 is Abu Yusuf's view (precautionary).
5
Apply the maxim to a novel case
Given a new scenario (e.g., a sleeping person's child knocks over a lamp causing damage), determine if the maxim applies. Held: the sleeping parent is liable (qi'yas on case 8).
Exception: if the act requires conscious statement or contract, maxim does not apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن النائم كالمستيقظ في بعض المسائل : قال الولوالجي في آخر فتاواه : النائم كالمستيقظ في خمس وعشرين مسألة : الأولى : إذا نام الصائم على قفاه وفوه مفتوح فقطر قطرة من ماء المطر في فيه فسد صومه، وكذا وقطر أحد قطرة من الماء في فيه وبلغ ذلك جوفه. الثانية : إذا جامعها زوجها وهي نائمة يفسد صومها. الثالثة : لو كانت محرمة فجامعها زوجها وهي نائمة فعليها الكفارة. الرابعة : المحرم إذا نام فجاء رجل فحلق رأسه وجب الجزاء عليه. الخامسة : المحرم إذا نام فانقلب على صيد فقتله وجب عليه الجزاء. السادسة : إذا نام المحرم على بعير ودخل في عرفات فقد أدرك الحج. السابعة : الصيد المرمى إليه بالسهم إذا وقع عند نائم من تلك الرمية فمات يكون حرامًا كما إذا وقع عند يقظان وهو قادر على ذكاته. الثامنة : إذا انقلب النائم على متاع وكسره وجب الضمان. التاسعة : الأب إذا نام تحت جدار فوقع الابن عليه من سطح وهو نائم فمات الابن يحرم عن الميراث على قول البعض، وهو الصحيح. العاشرة : مَن رفع النائم ووضعه تحت جدار فسقط عليه الجدار ومات لا يلزمه الضمان . الحادية عشرة : رجل خلا بامرأته وثمة أجنبي نائم لا تصح الخلوة. الثانية عشرة : رجل نام في بيت فجاءت امرأته ومكثت عنده ساعة صحت الخلوة . الثالثة عشرة : لو كانت المرأة نائمة في بيت ودخل عليها زوجها ومكث عندها ساعة صحت الخلوة . الرابعة عشرة : امرأة نامت فجاء رضيع فارتضع من ثديها تثبت حرمة الرضاع. الخامسة عشرة : المتيمم إذا مرَّت دابته على ماء يمكن استعماله وهو عليها نائم انتقض تيممه . السادسة عشرة : المصلي إذا نام وتكلم في حالة النوم تفسد صلاته . السابعة عشرة : المصلي إذا نام وقرأ في حالة قيامه تعتبر تلك القراءة. الثامنة عشرة : إذا تلا آية السجدة في نومه فسمعها رجل تلزمه السجدة، كما لو سمع من اليقظان . التاسعة عشرة : إذا استيقظ هذا النائم فأخبره رجل بذلك، كان شمس يفتي بأنه لا تجب عليه سجدة التلاوة، وتجب في بعض الأقوال. وعلى هذا لو قرأ رجل عند نائم فانتبه فأخبر فهو على هذا. العشرون : رجل حلف ألا يكلم فلانا فجاء الحالف إلى المحلوف عليه وهو نائم وقال له قم فلم يستيقظ النائم . قال بعضهم لا يحنث والأصح أنه يحنث . الحادية والعشرون : رجل طلق امرأته طلاقا رجعيّا فجاء الرجل ومسها بشهوة نائمة، صار مراجعا. الثانية والعشرون : لو كان الزوج نائما فجاءت المرأة وقبلته بشهوة يصير مراجعا عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله خلافا لمحمد رحمه الله . الثالثة والعشرون : الرجل إذا نام وجاءت امرأة وأدخلت فرجها في فرجه وهي نائمة وعلم بفعلها تثبت حرمة المصاهرة. الرابعة والعشرون : إذا جاءت امرأة إلى نائم وقبلته بشهوة واتفقا على أن ذلك كان بشهوة تثبت حرمة المصاهرة. الخامسة والعشرون : المصلي إذا نام في صلاته واحتلم يجب الغسل ولا يمكنه البناء. وكذلك إذا بقي نائمًا يوما وليلة أو يومين وليلتين صارت الصلاة دينا في ذمته . (انتهى).
Statement that the sleeping person is like the awake in some issues: al-Walwaliji said at the end of his Fatawa: The sleeping person is like the awake in twenty-five issues: First: If a fasting person sleeps on his back with his mouth open and a drop of rainwater falls into his mouth, his fast is broken; likewise if someone drops a drop of water into his mouth and it reaches his stomach. Second: If her husband has intercourse with her while she is sleeping, her fast is broken. Third: If she is in ihram and her husband has intercourse with her while she is sleeping, she must pay the kaffarah. Fourth: If a muhrim sleeps and a man comes and shaves his head, the expiation (jaza) is obligatory upon him. Fifth: If a muhrim sleeps and turns over onto game and kills it, the expiation is obligatory upon him. Sixth: If a muhrim sleeps on a camel and enters Arafat, he has attained the Hajj. Seventh: If game shot with an arrow falls near a sleeping person and dies, it is forbidden just as if it fell near an awake person who is able to slaughter it. Eighth: If a sleeping person turns over onto goods and breaks them, he is liable for compensation. Ninth: If a father sleeps under a wall and his son falls upon him from a roof while the father is sleeping, and the son dies, the father is deprived of inheritance according to some, and that is correct. Tenth: Whoever lifts a sleeping person and places him under a wall, and the wall falls on him and he dies, no compensation is owed. Eleventh: If a man is alone with his wife while there is a sleeping stranger present, the seclusion is not valid. Twelfth: If a man sleeps in a house and his wife comes and stays with him for an hour, the seclusion is valid. Thirteenth: If a woman is sleeping in a house and her husband enters and stays with her for an hour, the seclusion is valid. Fourteenth: If a woman sleeps and an infant comes and suckles from her breast, the prohibition of fosterage is established. Fifteenth: If a person performing tayammum passes by water that he could use while he is asleep on his animal, his tayammum is nullified. Sixteenth: If a praying person sleeps and speaks during sleep, his prayer is invalidated. Seventeenth: If a praying person sleeps and recites while standing, that recitation is considered. Eighteenth: If he recites a verse of prostration in his sleep and a man hears it, prostration is obligatory upon him, just as if he heard it from an awake person. Nineteenth: If this sleeping person wakes up and a man informs him of that, Shams gave a fatwa that the prostration of recitation is not obligatory upon him, though it is obligatory in some opinions. Likewise if a man recites near a sleeping person and he wakes up and is informed, it is upon this. Twentieth: If a man swears that he will not speak to so-and-so, and the one who swore comes to the one sworn about while he is sleeping and says 'Get up' and the sleeper does not wake up — some say he does not break his oath, but the correct view is that he does break it. Twenty-first: If a man divorces his wife with a revocable divorce, and then comes and touches her with desire while she is sleeping, he becomes a revocator. Twenty-second: If the husband is sleeping and the woman comes and kisses him with desire, he becomes a revocator according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), contrary to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). Twenty-third: If a man sleeps and a woman comes and inserts her vagina onto his male organ while she is sleeping and he knows of her action, the prohibition of in-law relationship is established. Twenty-fourth: If a woman comes to a sleeping man and kisses him with desire and both agree that it was with desire, the prohibition of in-law relationship is established. Twenty-fifth: If a praying person sleeps during his prayer and has a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory and he cannot resume prayer (build upon it). Similarly, if he remains asleep for a day and night or two days and two nights, the prayer becomes a debt upon him. (End).
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a collection of twenty-five specific cases where a sleeping person is given the same legal ruling as an awake person, compiled by al-Walwaliji. The maxim 'النائم كالمستيقظ' is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) applied across multiple fiqh chapters including fasting, hajj, sales, damages, seclusion, tayammum, prayer, oaths, divorce, and marriage prohibitions. The list demonstrates that sleep does not negate legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada) in these areas. Note the ikhtilaf in case 22 between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf holds that a sleeping husband becomes a revocator when kissed with desire, while Muhammad disagrees. Also case 19 shows variation in opinion regarding prostration of recitation. The final case about prayer and wet dream illustrates that sleep can lead to obligations (ghusl) and can transform a missed prayer into a debt.

Key Terms
النائم (an-nā'im): A person in a state of sleep, legally considered to have diminished but not absent capacity in certain rulings.
المستيقظ (al-mustayqiẓ): An awake person with full legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada).
الخلوة (al-khalwa): Seclusion between a husband and wife in a place where they can be alone without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must perform ghusl and cannot resume (build upon) his prayer.

Key Takeaway
The sleeping person is legally equivalent to the awake in specific rulings (liability, obligation, prohibition), but exceptions exist for matters requiring conscious intent.
