Rulings on the Ambiguous Hermaphrodite and Other Legal Disabilities
Concise rulings on legal disabilities and intersex status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida for the khuntha mushkil to derive rulings in worship, family law, and criminal law, and distinguish the ma'tuh from the insane.

Core Idea
The ambiguous hermaphrodite is given intermediate rulings between male and female, always taking the precautionary option.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir collects the Hanafi rulings for three special categories: the ma'tuh (dim-witted), the majnoon (insane), and the khuntha mushkil (ambiguous hermaphrodite). The ma'tuh is treated like a discerning child, while the insane are briefly referred to usul works. The bulk of the text details how the khuntha's ambiguous gender affects every aspect of life—prayer, inheritance, marriage, burial, theft penalties, and more. These furuat are governed by a consistent underlying qawida that a mufti must apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and list the three types of persons: ma'tuh, majnoon, khuntha mushkil. For each, note the key ruling or reference.
The ma'tuh has an ikhtilaf; the insane are not detailed here.
2
Analyze the ma'tuh ikhtilaf
The passage records three opinions: like a discerning child (preferred Hanafi), like the insane, or like a mature adult. Understand the thamarah: acts are valid but not obligatory.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate scholarly difference.
3
Extract the qawida for the khuntha
From the many rulings for the khuntha, infer the pattern: where male and female rulings differ, the khuntha is treated in the most precautionary manner (e.g., stands behind men, repeats prayer if in women's row). State the qawida.
The qawida can be phrased as 'Al-khuntha al-mushkil yu'ta ahkaman mutawassitah ma'a al-ahwat'.
4
Apply the qawida to new cases
Use the qawida to derive rulings for scenarios not directly mentioned, such as zakat or fasting obligations.
The precautionary principle means defaulting to the more restrictive rule.
5
Identify the fatwa hierarchy
Note that the khuntha rulings are taken from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah. This gives them strong authority for fatwa.
Later Hanafi works rely on this transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام المعتوه
أحكامه أحكام الصبي العاقل فتصح العبادات منه ولا تجب. وقيل هو كالمجنون، وقيل هو كالبالغ العاقل، وقد ذكرناه في النواقص من شرح الكنز .
أحكام المجنون
ذكرها الأصوليون في بحث العوارض فلينظرها من رامها .
بيان أن الاعتبار للمعنى أو اللفظ :
ذكرناه في كتاب البيوع من النوع الثاني .
أحكام الخنثى المشكل
ذكر النسفي في الكنز حقيقته، وذكر من أحكامه وقوفه في الصف وحكم ميراثه وختانه . وذكر مولانا محمد رحمه الله أحكامه في الأصل من كتاب المفقود، وأنا أذكر ما ذكره هناك باختصار .
يُيَمَّم إذا مات ويُسجّى قبره ولا يدفنه إلا محرم ويكفن كفن المرأة ولا يلبس حريرا ولا حليًّا في حياته، وإذا قبله رجل بشهوة حرم عليه أصوله وفروعه. فإن زوجه أبوه رجلاً فوصل إليه جاز، وإلا فلا علم لي بذلك، أو امرأة فبلغ فوصل إليها جاز وإلا أُجُل كالعِنّين، ويلبس لباس المرأة في الإحرام ولا يصلي إلا بقناع ويقوم أمام النساء خلف الرجال، وإن وقف في صف النساء أعادها وإن وقف في صف الرجال لا يُعيدها ويُعيدها من عن يمينيه ويساره وخلفه محاذيا له، ويوضع في الجنازة خلف الرجال والمرأة خلفه، ويُجعَل خلف الرجل في القبر لو دفنا لضرورة حاجز بينهما من الصعيد ولا حدّ على قاذفه ولا عليه بقذفه بمنزلة المجبوب؛ وتقطع يده للسرقة ويقطع سارق ماله ويقعد في صلاته كالمرأة ولا قصاص على قاطع يده ولو عمدًا ولو كان القاطع امرأة، ولا تقطع يده إذا قطع يد غيره عمدا، أو على عاقلته أرشها ولا يخلو به رجل ولا امرأة ولا يخلو برجل ولا امرأة، ولا يسافر ثلاثة أيام إلا بمحرم.
وإذا أوصى رجل لما في بطن امرأة بألف إن كان غلاما وبخمسمائة إن كان أُنثى، فولدت خنثى مشكلاً فالوصية موقوفة في الخمسمائة الزائدة إلى أن يستبين أمره،
Rulings of the Imbecile (Ma'tuh): His rulings are the rulings of a discerning child: acts of worship are valid from him but not obligatory. And it is said he is like the insane, and it is said he is like a mature discerning person. We have mentioned it in al-Nawaqis from Sharh al-Kanz.
Rulings of the Insane (Majnoon): The Usuliyyun have mentioned them in the discussion of 'Awarid (impediments). Let whoever seeks them look there.
Explanation that consideration is for meaning or wording: We have mentioned it in the Book of Sales of the second type.
Rulings of the Ambiguous Hermaphrodite (Khuntha Mushkil): Al-Nasafi mentioned its reality in al-Kanz, and mentioned among its rulings: its standing in the row, the ruling of its inheritance and circumcision. And our master Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned its rulings in al-Asl from the Book of the Missing Person. I will mention what he mentioned there in brief.
He is given tayammum when he dies, and his grave is leveled, and only a mahram buries him. He is shrouded like a woman's shroud. He does not wear silk or jewelry in his lifetime. If a man kisses him with desire, his ascendants and descendants become forbidden (for that man). If his father marries him to a man and he reaches (the husband) it is permissible; otherwise, I have no knowledge of that. Or (if he is married) to a woman, and he reaches puberty and reaches her, it is permissible; otherwise he is given a term like an impotent man. He wears women's clothing in ihram and does not pray except with a headcover, and he stands in front of women behind the men. If he stands in the women's row, he repeats the prayer; if he stands in the men's row, he does not repeat it. And people on his right, left, and behind him align with him. He is placed in the funeral prayer behind the men, with the woman behind him. He is placed behind the man in the grave if buried for necessity, with a barrier of earth between them. There is no hadd penalty for his slanderer, and no hadd on him for slandering; he is like a eunuch. His hand is cut off for theft, and the hand of the thief who steals his property is cut off. He sits in prayer like a woman. There is no qisas for the one who cuts off his hand, even intentionally, even if the cutter is a woman. His hand is not cut off if he cuts off another's hand intentionally; rather, the diyah is on his 'aqila. No man or woman may be alone with him, nor may he be alone with a man or woman. He may not travel three days except with a mahram.
And if a man bequeaths to what is in a woman's womb one thousand if it is a boy and five hundred if it is a girl, and she gives birth to an ambiguous hermaphrodite, then the bequest is suspended regarding the extra five hundred until its matter becomes clear.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents a collection of rulings on special persons: the imbecile (ma'tuh), the insane (majnoon), and the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil). It begins with the ma'tuh, noting a difference of opinion: some treat him like a discerning child (acts valid but not obligatory), others like the insane (completely incapable), and others like a mature person. The author refers to his earlier work for details. The insane are briefly referenced to usul works. Then a note on whether rulings consider literal meaning or intent, referred to elsewhere. The main portion is on the khuntha mushkil, taken from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl. The rulings cover: death rites (tayammum, shroud like woman, only mahram buries), prohibition on silk/jewelry, how kissing with desire creates marital prohibitions, marriage possibilities (to man or woman with conditions), dress and prayer posture (wears women's ihram, prays with headcover, stands behind men, repeats prayer if in women's row), funeral placement (behind men, woman behind him), burial with barrier, no hadd for slander, theft punishment (hand cut), sitting like woman in prayer, no qisas for injury to his hand, diyah on 'aqila for his intentional injury, no khalwa with him, travel restrictions. Finally, a case of bequest to a pregnant woman where the child is khuntha: extra amount suspended until clarity. These rulings illustrate how ambiguous gender affects legal treatment across many areas.

Key Terms
المعتوه (al-ma'tuh): A person with diminished intellect but not completely insane, similar to a discerning child.
الخنثى المشكل (al-khuntha al-mushkil): A person with ambiguous genitalia whose sex cannot be determined, requiring special rulings.
الأحوط (al-ahwat): The precautionary option, preferred in case of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a khuntha mushkil stands in the women's row during prayer?
A) The prayer is valid and does not need repetition.
B) He must repeat the prayer.
C) His prayer is invalid and must be made up after puberty.
D) He should lead the women's row.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a comprehensive framework for the khuntha mushkil, governed by the qawida of taking intermediate and precautionary rulings, which muftis must apply consistently.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
12 min
The Legal Principle for the Ambiguous Hermaphrodite (Khuntha Mushkil)
Legal rulings (furuat) applying the qawida for khuntha mushkil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default rule for the khuntha mushkil and identify the seven exceptions where the default female treatment is not applied.

Core Idea
The khuntha mushkil is treated as a female in all rulings, except in seven specific matters where ambiguity prevents application.

The khuntha mushkil is an individual whose gender cannot be determined conclusively. The Hanafi jurists have derived a comprehensive principle governing all rulings related to such a person: he/she is to be treated as a female in every aspect, except for a few cases where the ambiguity of gender demands a departure from this default. In this lesson, we will examine the qawida and its applications (furuat) as presented in Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Default Rule
Read the concluding summary: 'وحاصله أنه كالأنثى في جميع الأحكام' – The khuntha is like a female in all rulings. Understand that this is the default presumption.
The default removes doubt in the absence of certainty.
2
List the Exceptional Cases
The text then lists exceptions: 'إلا في مسائل' – seven specific matters where this rule is not applied. Identify each exception and the reason behind it.
These exceptions arise where the ambiguity of gender logically prevents applying the female ruling.
3
Analyse the Legal Reasoning Behind Each Exception
For each exception, consider why the default is suspended. For example, he does not wear silk because he might be male; no hadd for qadhf because the victim's chastity is uncertain; etc.
The underlying principle is caution (ihtiyat) when gender is unknown.
4
Understand the Internal Exceptions (Istithna'at)
The text mentions cases where the khuntha is included if both male and female conditions are stated together (e.g., master says 'every male and every female slave'). Recognize how these istithna'at operate.
These are not contradictions but logical necessities: the khuntha must be one gender.
5
Apply the Qawida to Practical Furuat
Using the passages on divorce, inheritance, testimony, and criminal law, see how the default rule and its exceptions are applied consistently across different chapters of fiqh.
The qawida serves as a unifying principle for all khuntha rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال لامرأته إن كان أول ولد تلدينه غلامًا فأنت طالق أو قال كذلك لأمته فأنت حرة، فولدت خنثى مشكلاً لم تطلق ولم تعتق . ولا سهم له مع المقاتلة وإنما يرضخ له ولا يقتل لو أسيرًا أو مرتدا بعد الإسلام، ولا خراج على رأسه لو كان ذميا، ولا يدخل تحت قول المولى كل عبد لي حرّ أو كل أمة لي حرة إلا إذا قالهما فيعتق، ولو قال الزوج إن ملكت عبدا فأنت طالق فاشترى خنثى لم تطلق وكذلك لو قال إن ملكت أمة، ولو قالهما معا طلقت، ولو قال المشكل أنا ذكر أو أنثى لم يقبل قوله، وإذا قتل خطأ وجبت دية المرأة ويوقف الباقي إلى التبيين، وكذا فيما دون النفس، ويصح إعتاقه عن الكفارة، ولو تزوج مشكل مثله لم يجز حتى يتبين فلا يتوارثان بالموت ولو شهد شهود أنه ذكر وشهود أنه أنثى فإن كان يطلب ميرانا قضيت بشهادة من شهد أنه غلام وأبطلت الأخرى، وإن كان رجل يدعي أنه امرأته قضيت بشهادة من شهد أنه أُنثى وأبطلت الأخرى؛ فإن كانت امرأة تدعي أنه زوجها أوقفت الأمر إلى أن يستبين فإن لم يطلب الخنثى شيئًا ولا يطلب منه شيء لا تقبل واحدة منهما حتى يستبين . وأما ميراثه والميراث منه؛ فقال فإن مات أبوه فله ميراث أُنثى منه، وتمامه فيه . وحاصله أنه كالأنثى في جميع الأحكام إلا في مسائل؛ لا يلبس حريرا ولا ذهبًا ولا فضة، ولا يتزوج من رجل، ولا يقف في صف النساء، ولا حد بقذفه، ولا يخلو بامرأة ولا يقع عتق وطلاق علقا على ولادتها أُنثى به، ولا يدخل تحت قوله كل أمة .
And if a man said to his wife, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are divorced,' or similarly said to his slave girl, 'You are free,' and she gave birth to a hermaphrodite of ambiguous gender, she is not divorced and she is not freed. And he has no share with the fighters, but is given a gratuity (рудх). And he is not killed if captured or an apostate after Islam. And there is no poll tax (kharaj) on his head if he is a dhimmi. And he does not fall under the master's statement 'Every male slave of mine is free' or 'Every female slave of mine is free' unless he says both, then he is freed. And if a husband said, 'If I own a male slave, you are divorced,' and he bought a hermaphrodite, she is not divorced, and similarly if he said 'a female slave' [and bought a hermaphrodite], and if he said both together, she is divorced. And if the ambiguous one says, 'I am male' or 'I am female,' his word is not accepted. And if he kills accidentally, the blood money (diya) of a woman is obligatory, and the remainder is suspended until clarification; similarly for injuries less than life. And his manumission for expiation is valid. And if an ambiguous person marries another like him, it is not permissible until clarity; thus they do not inherit from each other upon death. And if some witnesses testify that he is male and others that he is female, then if he is claiming an inheritance, judgment is given on the testimony that he is a boy and the other is invalidated; and if a man claims that she is his wife, judgment is given on the testimony that she is female and the other is invalidated; but if a woman claims that he is her husband, the matter is suspended until it becomes clear. And if the hermaphrodite claims nothing and nothing is claimed from him, neither testimony is accepted until clarity. As for his inheritance and inheritance from him: if his father dies, he inherits as a female from him, and its completion is in it. The summary is that he is like a female in all rulings except in matters: he does not wear silk, gold, or silver; he does not marry a man; he does not stand in the women's row; there is no prescribed punishment (hadd) for slandering him; he is not alone with a woman; and emancipation and divorce conditional on her giving birth to a female do not take effect; and he does not fall under the statement 'every female slave'.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a set of legal rulings (furuat) concerning the khuntha mushkil (an individual with ambiguous genitalia whose gender cannot be determined conclusively). The overall principle (qawida) derived is that the khuntha mushkil is treated as a female in all rulings except for a few specific exceptions. The rulings cover various chapters: divorce, slavery, inheritance, testimony, criminal law, marriage, and ritual matters. Key points: conditional divorces or emancipations based on the child's gender do not take effect when the child is a khuntha mushkil because the condition is not fulfilled. The khuntha does not receive a share in the spoils of war but a gratuity. He is not executed if captured as an apostate (since apostasy requires certainty of gender? Actually, the ruling is specific). He is exempt from jizya if a dhimmi. In the context of freeing slaves, if the master says 'every male slave is free' or 'every female slave is free,' the khuntha is not included unless the master says both terms, in which case he is freed because one of them must apply. Similarly, if a husband suspends divorce on owning a male or female slave, buying a khuntha does not trigger divorce; only if both conditions are stated does divorce occur because the khuntha must be either male or female. The statement of the khuntha about his own gender is not accepted because of potential self-interest. In accidental homicide, the full diya of a woman is due, with the remainder of the full male diya suspended until the gender is known. Manumission for expiation (e.g., kaffara) is valid because it entirely removes ownership. Marriage of two khunthas is not valid until each is identified as male/female; hence no inheritance between them. In conflicting testimony about the khuntha's gender, if he claims inheritance, the testimony that he is male is preferred because it gives him a share; if a man claims he is his wife, testimony for female is accepted; if a woman claims he is her husband, the matter is suspended; if no one claims, both testimonies are rejected. Inheritance: from his father, he takes a female share. The concluding summary lists exceptions: he cannot wear silk, gold, or silver (which are forbidden to males); he cannot marry a man (since he might be male); he does not stand in women's row (he stands with men or separately); no hadd for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) against him because of ambiguity; he cannot be alone with a non-mahram woman; conditional emancipations/divorces on giving birth to a female do not apply to him; and he is not included in the master's blanket freeing of female slaves.

Key Terms
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): An individual with both male and female genitalia or ambiguous genitals whose gender cannot be determined conclusively.
رضخ (radikh): A gratuity given to those who participate in battle but do not receive a full share of spoils, such as women, children, and the khuntha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the seven exceptions to the default female treatment for the khuntha mushkil?
A) He does not wear silk, gold, or silver.
B) He does not inherit from his father as a male.
C) He does not stand in the women's prayer row.
D) He does not receive the hadd punishment for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawida for the khuntha mushkil is a default of female treatment across all fiqh chapters, with exactly seven exceptions named in the text.

Ahkam al-Untha: Legal Differences Between Men and Women
Enumeration of legal differences between men and women across fiqh chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and categorize at least 10 rulings specific to women from the Hanafi school across chapters such as prayer, Hajj, testimony, and criminal law.

Core Idea
Women are legally distinct in worship, attire, testimony, and criminal liability to preserve modesty and reduce hardship.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir compiles the key differences between men and women in Hanafi fiqh. Rather than a single ruling, it presents a set of rulings (ahkam al-untha) that span nearly every chapter. Understanding these differences is essential for a mufti to apply the correct ruling when the gender of the party matters.

Guided Path
1
Scan and list topics
Quickly read the passage and note all fiqh chapters mentioned: purification, prayer, fasting, Hajj, testimony, criminal law, inheritance, marriage, etc.
This helps organize a large set of rulings.
2
Group by ibadat and muamalat
Separate rulings into worship (ibadat) and social/legal matters (muamalat). Within ibadat, further divide into prayer, Hajj, fasting, etc.
Women's worship often has modifications to reduce hardship.
3
Identify the specific ruling and underlying reason
For each grouping, extract the exact ruling (e.g., 'she claps instead of saying subhanallah') and infer the reason: usually modesty or minimizing burden.
Hanafi fiqh explicitly states these differences.
4
Note differences of opinion (ikhtilaf)
The passage mentions several differences (e.g., voice as 'awra, bathhouse). Identify the relied-upon opinion (al-mu'tamad) and the weaker view.
These are marked by phrases like 'على المعتمد' or 'وقيل'.
5
Formulate the underlying principle
Try to derive a principle: 'Women are given concessions in ibadat to accommodate their nature, and in legal matters their participation is restricted to protect their modesty.'
This principle helps apply rulings consistently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الأنثى تخالف الرجل في أن السنة في عانتها النتف ولا يسن ختانها وإنما هو مكرمة، ويسن حلق لحيتها لو نبتت وتمنع من حلق رأسها ومنيها لا يطهر بالفرك على قول وتزيد في أسباب البلوغ بالحيض والحمل ويُكره أذانها ،وإقامتها، وبدنها كله عورة إلا وجهها وكفيها وقدميها على المعتمد، وذراعيها على المرجوح، وصوتها عورة في قول، ويُكره لها دخول الحمام في قول، وقيل يُكره إلا أن تكون مريضة أو نفساء، والمعتمد لا كراهة مطلقا، ولا ترفع يديها حذاء أذنيها ولا تجهر بقراءتها وتضم في ركوعها وسجودها ولا تفرج أصابعها في الركوع، وإذا نابها شيء في صلاتها صفقت ولا تسبح ، وتُكرَه جماعتهنَّ، ويقف الإمام وسطهنَّ ولا تصلح إمامًا للرجال، ويُكره حضورها الجماعة، وصلاتها في بيتها أفضل وتضع يمينها على شمالها تحت ثديها وتضع يدها في التشهد على ركبتيها وتتورّك، ولا جمعة عليها ولكن تنعقد بها، ولا عيد ولا تكبير تشريق ولا تسافر إلا بزوج أو محرم ولا يجب عليها الحج إلا بأحدهما، ولا تلبي جهرًا ولا تنزع المخيط ولا تكشف رأسها ولا تسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين، ولا تحلق وإنما تقصر ولا ترمل والتباعد في طوافها عن البيت أفضل، ولا تخطب مطلقا، وتقف في حاشية الموقف لا عند الصحرات، وتكون قاعدة وهو راكب، وتلبس في إحرامها الخُفَّين وتترك طواف الصدر لعذر الحيض، وتؤخر طواف الزيارة لعذر الحيض، وتُكَفَّن في خمسة أثواب ولا تؤم في الجنازة ولو فعلت سقط الفرض بصلاتها، ولا تحمل الجنازة وإن كان الميت أنثى، ويندب لها نحو القبة في التابوت، ولا سهم لها وإنما يرضخ لها إن قاتلت ولا تقتل المرتدة والمشركة ولا تُقبل شهادتها في الحدود والقصاص، وتعتكف في بيتها ويُباح لها خضب يديها ورجليها بخلاف الرجل إلا لضرورة. والتضحية بالذكر أفضل منها وهي على النصف من الرجل في الإرث والشهادة والدّية نفسًا أو بعضا، ونفقة القريب، ولا ينبغي أن تولى القضاء، وإن صح منها في غير الحدود والقصاص، وبضعها مقابل بالمهر دون الرجل، وتجبر الأمة على النكاح دون العبد في رواية والمعتمد عدم الفرق بينهما في الجبر، وتُخَيَّر الأمة إذا عتقت بخلاف العبد ولو كان زوجها حرًا، ولبنها محرم في الرضاع دونه . وتُقَدَّم على الرجال في الحضانة والنفقة على الولد الصغير وفي النفر من مزدلفة إلى منى وفي الانصراف من الصلاة، وتؤخر في جماعة الرجال والموقف وفي اجتماع الجنازة عند الإمام ؛ فتعجل عند القبلة والرجل عند الإمام وكذا في اللحد . وتجب الدية بقطع ثديها أو حلمته بخلافه من الرجل فإن فيه الحكومة، ولا قصاص بقطع طرفها بخلافه، ولا مساومة عليها ولا تدخل مع العاقلة؛ فلا شيء عليها من الدّية لو قتلت خطأ بخلاف الرجل فإن القاتل كأحدهم. ويُحفّر لها في الرجم إن ثبت زناها بالبينة وتُجلَد جالسة والرجل قائما ولا تنفى سياسة، ويُنفى هو عاما بعد الجلد سياسة ولا حدا ولا تُكَلَّف الحضور للدعوى إذا كانت مخدّرة ولا لليمين بل يحضر إليها القاضي أو يبعث إليها نائبه يحلفها بحضرة شاهدين، ويقبل توكيلها بلا رضاء الخصم إذا كانت مُخَدَّرة اتفاقا ولا تبتدأ الشابة بسلام وتعزية ولا تجاب، ولا تُشمت، وتحرم الخلوة بالأجنبية ويُكرَه الكلام معها .
Rulings of the female: She differs from the man in that the sunna for her pubic area is plucking, and her circumcision is not sunna but only an honorific act. It is sunna for her to shave her beard if it grows, and she is prevented from shaving her head. Her seminal fluid is not purified by rubbing according to one opinion. She has additional causes of puberty: menstruation and pregnancy. Her adhan and iqama are disliked. Her entire body is 'awra except her face, hands, and feet according to the relied-upon opinion, and her forearms according to the weaker opinion. Her voice is 'awra according to one opinion. It is disliked for her to enter the bathhouse according to one opinion, and it is said to be disliked unless she is ill or postpartum; the relied-upon opinion is no dislike at all. She does not raise her hands to her ears (in takbir), she does not recite aloud, she brings her limbs together in ruku' and sujud, she does not spread her fingers in ruku', and if something occurs to her in prayer she claps rather than saying 'subhanallah'. Congregational prayer for women is disliked. The imam stands in the middle of their row. She is not fit to lead men in prayer. Her attendance at congregation is disliked, and her prayer at home is better. She places her right hand on her left under her chest, she places her hands on her knees in tashahhud, and she sits mutawarrikan. Jumu'ah is not obligatory on her, but it is valid if she attends. There is no Eid prayer or takbir tashriq for her. She may not travel except with a husband or mahram, and Hajj is not obligatory on her except with one of them. She does not raise her voice in talbiyah, she does not remove sewn garments, she does not uncover her head, she does not run between the two green pillars, she does not shave her head but only shortens, she does not raml, and keeping distance from the Ka'bah in tawaf is better for her. She does not deliver khutbah at all. She stands at the edge of the standing place, not near the open spaces. She sits while he rides (in Hajj). She wears khuffs in ihram. She omits tawaf al-sadr due to menstruation. She delays tawaf al-ziyarah due to menstruation. She is shrouded in five garments. She does not lead the funeral prayer; if she does, the obligation is fulfilled. She does not carry the bier even if the deceased is female. It is recommended for her to have something like a dome on the coffin. She has no share (of spoils) but is given a gratuity if she fights. The apostate and polytheist woman is not killed. Her testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas. She performs i'tikaf in her home. It is permissible for her to dye her hands and feet with henna, unlike men except for necessity. Sacrificing a male animal is better than a female. She is half of the man in inheritance, testimony, blood money (full and partial), and maintenance of relatives. She should not be appointed to the judiciary, although her judgment is valid except in hudud and qisas. Her pudendum is exchanged for mahr, unlike the man. The female slave is compelled to marry, unlike the male slave in one narration, but the relied-upon opinion is that there is no difference between them in compulsion. The female slave is given choice upon emancipation, unlike the male slave even if her husband is free. Her milk is a cause of prohibition in breastfeeding, unlike his. She is given precedence over men in custody, maintenance of young children, in moving from Muzdalifah to Mina, and in leaving from prayer. She is delayed in men's congregation, at the standing place (in Hajj), and in the funeral gathering with the imam; so she is placed near the qibla and the man near the imam, similarly in the niche. The full blood money is due for cutting off her breast or nipple, unlike a man for which there is government assessment (hukuma). There is no qisas for cutting off her limb, unlike him. She is not subject to bargaining (in sales? unclear) and she is not included with the 'aqila; thus she is not liable for any blood money if she kills accidentally, unlike the man, for whom the killer is like one of them. For stoning, a pit is dug for her if her adultery is proven by evidence, and she is flogged sitting while the man is standing. She is not exiled as a policy, while he is exiled for a year after flogging as a policy, not as a hadd. She is not required to attend court if she is a woman of seclusion (mukhaddara), nor for taking an oath; rather, the judge goes to her or sends his deputy to administer the oath in the presence of two witnesses. Her appointment of an attorney is accepted without the consent of the opponent if she is mukhaddara, by agreement. A young woman is not initiated with greeting or condolence, nor is she responded to. She is not made to sneeze (i.e., said 'yarhamukallah' if she sneezes? Actually, she is not prompted to say 'alhamdulillah'? The text says 'la tushammat' meaning she is not told 'yarhamukallah' if she sneezes). Khalwa with a non-mahram woman is forbidden, and speaking with her is disliked.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive list of rulings (ahkam) specific to females, organized as a set of differences (khilaf) between men and women. It covers almost all chapters of fiqh: purification, prayer, fasting, Hajj, zakat, marriage, divorce, criminal law, testimony, inheritance, and more. The overall principle is that women are on half of men in certain quantitative matters (inheritance, testimony, diya), and in many acts of worship they have modified or reduced obligations to accommodate their natural dispositions and to protect modesty. Key rulings include: For purification, pubic hair removal is by plucking (sunnah for women), circumcision is not sunna but a noble act. Their entire body is 'awra except face, hands, and feet. In prayer, they pray differently: they do not raise hands to ears, they bring limbs together, they clap instead of saying 'subhanallah' to alert the imam. They are discouraged from congregational prayer; home prayer is better. No adhan, iqama, or raising voice. No Jumu'ah obligation but it counts if performed. In Hajj, they do not run or uncover head; they shorten hair instead of shaving; they delay tawaf if menstruating; they wear khuffs; they stand at the edge of Muzdalifah. They are not required to fight or give spoils shares; they receive gratuity if they do. They are not executed for apostasy or disbelief? Actually, the text says 'the apostate and polytheist woman is not killed' (implying she is imprisoned?). Their testimony is rejected in hudud and qisas. In inheritance, they get half of a man's share. In criminal law, the diya for a woman is half that of a man; cutting her breast incurs full diya while a man's breast only incurs government assessment (hukuma). No qisas for limb amputation. She is not part of the 'aqila (blood money paying group). In family law, she has priority in custody and maintenance of children. She can be compelled to marry if a slave? The relied-upon opinion says no difference between male and female slaves in compulsion. Female slave gets choice upon emancipation. Her milk causes fosterage prohibition. In judicial procedure, she is excused from attending court if she is mukhaddara (veiled woman of status); the judge goes to her. Her appointment of an attorney is accepted without opponent's consent. In social interactions, a young woman is not greeted first, not condoled, not responded to? Actually the text says 'la tujab' meaning she is not answered? This might mean it is disliked to initiate greeting or respond? The precise meaning needs careful interpretation. Overall, the rulings aim to protect women's modesty and reduce hardships.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer and before non-mahram. For women, the entire body except face, hands, and feet according to the relied-upon Hanafi opinion.
مخدّرة (mukhaddara): A woman of status who stays in seclusion, not going out uncovered. Such women are exempted from attending court in person for lawsuits or oaths.
رضخ (radikh): A gratuity given to participants in battle who are not eligible for a full share, such as women, children, and slaves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about women's 'awrah in prayer?
A) Women must cover their entire body, including face and hands.
B) Women's 'awrah is the entire body except face, hands, and feet.
C) Women's 'awrah is the same as men's from navel to knees.
D) Women's 'awrah includes voice and hair only.

Key Takeaway
Women have distinct legal rulings in Hanafi fiqh across all chapters, primarily to preserve modesty and reduce hardship, and these rulings are mufta bihi with few exceptions.

Hanafi Rulings on Women: A Comprehensive Parsing Exercise
Comprehensive list of women-specific Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse the comprehensive list of Hanafi rulings on women into thematic categories and identify the hukm level for each specific ruling.

Core Idea
Women's rulings in Hanafi fiqh are systematic: they follow principles of exemption, protection, and equivalence.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir compiles a wide range of Hanafi rulings specifically concerning women. These span acts of worship, criminal law, marriage, inheritance, testimony, and legal procedure. As a mufti or advanced student, parsing such a register is essential for applying the correct ruling in each context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
For each phrase, determine if it pertains to 'ibadat (prayer, Hajj, fasting), mu'amalat (marriage, inheritance), jinayat (diya, qisas), or procedural law (testimony, agency). This helps organize the information.
E.g., 'ولا جمعة عليها' belongs to 'ibadat (obligation).
2
Extract the hukm level from the phrasing
Look for keywords indicating obligation (يجب), prohibition (يحرم), permission (يباح), etc. Also note phrases like 'لا يجب' indicating non-obligation or 'أفضل' indicating preference.
E.g., 'صلاتها في بيتها أفضل' indicates mustahabb.
3
Note conditions and exemptions specific to women
Identify elements that modify general rules due to the female gender, such as requirement of a mahram for travel or exemption from public duties.
E.g., 'ولا يجب عليها الحج إلا بأحدهما' makes Hajj conditional on a mahram.
4
Identify differences from general rules
Contrast the women-specific ruling with the general ruling for men where applicable, e.g., in tashahhud posture, funeral prayer leadership, or qisas.
E.g., 'لا قصاص بقطع طرفها بخلافه' shows gender differentiation.
5
Recognize rulings based on the woman's state
Some rulings depend on the woman's condition, like being a mukhadara (secluded) or a slave. Identify these context-specific rules.
E.g., 'إذا كانت مخدرة' exempts her from attending court.

حضورها الجماعة، وصلاتها في بيتها أفضل وتضع يمينها على شمالها تحت ثديها وتضع يدها في التشهد على ركبتيها وتتورّك، ولا جمعة عليها ولكن تنعقد بها، ولا عيد ولا تكبير تشريق ولا تسافر إلا بزوج أو محرم ولا الموقف لا عند الصحرات، وتكون قاعدة وهو راكب، وتلبس في إحرامها الخفين وتترك طواف الصدر لعذر الحيض، وتؤخر طواف الزيارة لعذر الحيض، وتكفن في خمسة أثواب ولا تؤم في الجنازة ولو فعلت سقط الفرض بصلاتها، ولا كأحدهم. ويحفر لها في الرجم إن ثبت زناها بالبينة وتجلد جالسة والرجل قائما ولا تنفى سياسة، وينفى هو عاما بعد الجلد سياسة لا حدا ولا تكلف الحضور للدعوى إذا كانت مخدرة ولا لليمين بل يحضر إليها القاضي أو يبعث إليها نائبه يحلفها بحضرة شاهدين، ويقبل توكيلها بلا رضاء الخصم إذا كانت مخدرة اتفاقا ولا تبتدأ الشابة بسلام وتعزية ولا تجاب، ولا تشمت، وتحرم الخلوة بالأجنبية ويكره الكلام معها. واختلفوا في جواز كونها نبية واختار في المسايرة جواز كونها نبية لا رسولة، لأن الرسالة مبنية على الاشتهار ومبنى حالهن على الستر بخلاف النبوة والتمام فيها، ولا تدخل النساء في الغرامات السلطانية كما في الولوالجية من القسمة.
Her attendance in congregation, and her prayer in her house is better, and she places her right hand over her left under her chest, and she places her hand in tashahhud on her knees, and she sits mutawarrikan. There is no Friday prayer obligatory upon her, but it is valid with her presence. There is no Eid prayer or Takbir al-Tashriq. She does not travel except with a husband or mahram, and Hajj is not obligatory upon her except with one of them. She does not recite talbiyah loudly, does not remove stitched garments, does not uncover her head, does not run between the two green milestones, does not shave but rather trims, does not walk briskly (ramal), and staying far from the Kaaba during tawaf is better for her. She does not deliver sermons absolutely. She stands at the edge of the standing place, not at the rocks. She sits while the man rides. She wears khuffs in her ihram, and leaves the farewell tawaf due to menstruation, and delays the visit tawaf due to menstruation. She is shrouded in five garments. She does not lead the funeral prayer; if she does, the obligation is fulfilled by her prayer. She does not carry the bier, even if the deceased is female. It is recommended for her to have something like a dome in the coffin. She has no share (of booty), but is given a discretionary grant if she fights. The apostate and polytheist woman is not killed. Her testimony in hadd and qisas cases is not accepted. She performs i'tikaf in her house. Dyeing her hands and feet is permissible for her, unlike men except for necessity. Sacrificing a male is better than her. She receives half of a man in inheritance, testimony, and blood money for soul or limb, and maintenance of relatives. She should not be appointed to judgeship, though it is valid from her in other than hadd and qisas. Her private parts are exchanged for dower, unlike a man. The slave woman is forced into marriage, but not the slave in one narration, though the relied-upon position is no difference between them in compulsion. The slave woman has option upon emancipation, unlike the slave, even if her husband is free. Her milk prohibits in breastfeeding, unlike his. She is given precedence over men in custody, maintenance of the young child, departing from Muzdalifah to Mina, and leaving the prayer. She is delayed in the congregation of men, the standing place, and in the funeral gathering at the imam; so she hastens at the qiblah and the man at the imam, and likewise in the niche. Diya is obligatory for cutting off her breast or nipple, unlike a man where there is government (equitable compensation). No qisas for cutting off her limb, unlike a man. There is no bargaining over her, and she does not enter the 'aqilah; so nothing of diya is upon her if she kills by mistake, unlike the man where the killer is like one of them. A pit is dug for her in stoning if her adultery is proven by evidence, and she is flogged sitting while the man stands, and she is not exiled for policy, while he is exiled for a year after flogging as policy, not as a hadd. She is not required to attend the claim if she is a secluded woman, nor for oath, but the judge comes to her or sends his deputy to have her swear in the presence of two witnesses. Her agency is accepted without the opponent's consent if she is secluded, unanimously. The young woman is not initiated with greeting or condolence, nor responded to, nor sneezed for. Seclusion with a non-mahram is prohibited, and speaking with her is disliked. They differed about the permissibility of her being a prophet, and al-Masayara chose the permissibility of her being a prophet but not a messenger, because messengership is based on publicity while their condition is based on concealment, unlike prophethood; and the completion therein. And women are not included in the sultanate penalties, as in al-Walwaljiyya from the division.

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive compilation of Hanafi rulings specific to women. It covers a wide range of topics. The passage begins with prayer rules: congregational prayer is not obligatory for women, and praying at home is superior. It details a woman's posture in prayer (placing hands under the chest, sitting mutawarrikan in tashahhud). For Eid and Friday prayer, no obligation on women, but they can be present? Actually, Jumu'ah is not obligatory on her, but if she attends, it's valid and fulfills the obligation. Eid and Takbir al-Tashriq are not for women. Travel requires a husband or mahram, and Hajj becomes obligatory only if she has one. In ihram, she does not raise voice in talbiyah, keeps stitched garments on, does not uncover head, does not run between Safa and Marwa, but rather trims hair. After tawaf, she avoids ramal and keeps distance. She does not deliver sermons. At Arafat, she stands at the outskirts. When a man rides, she sits. In funeral rites, she is shrouded in five garments, does not lead the prayer, and does not carry the bier. In jihad, she receives only a discretionary grant (radkh), not a share of booty. Apostate and polytheist women are not killed. Her testimony is not accepted in hadd or qisas cases. For i'tikaf, she does it at home. Dyeing hands and feet with henna is permissible, unlike men. Sacrificing a male animal is better than a female. In inheritance, testimony, and blood money, she gets half the share of a man. She should not be a judge. Her private parts are compensated by dower in marriage. Regarding forced marriage (jabr), there is a narration that a slave woman is forced but not a slave, but the relied-upon view is that there is no difference. An emacipated slave woman has choice. Her milk establishes fosterage prohibition. She is given precedence over men in custody and maintenance of children, and in departing from Muzdalifah to Mina. In congregational prayer, she stands behind men. In funeral prayer, she stands near the qiblah while the man is near the imam. Diya for cutting off her breast includes the full diya for a woman (half of man's), while for a man it is government (equitable compensation). Qisas is not applied for her limbs, while for a man it is. She is not included with the 'aqilah for blood money if she kills mistakenly. In stoning for adultery, a pit is dug for her. Flogging is done while sitting, while the man stands. She is not exiled, but the man is exiled for a year. For legal proceedings, a secluded woman (mukhadara) does not attend court; the judge comes to her or sends a deputy. Her agency is accepted without the opponent's consent. Young women should not be initiated with greeting, condolence, or sneeze response. Seclusion with a non-mahram is prohibited, and conversation with her is disliked. Finally, there is a dispute about women being prophets; the preferred view in al-Masayara is that she can be a prophet but not a messenger, due to the nature of concealment. Also, women are not subject to sultanate penalties, as mentioned in al-Walwaljiyya.

Key Terms
مخدرة (mukhadara): A woman who stays in her home and does not appear in public
رضخ (radkh): A discretionary grant given to those who participate in jihad but are not entitled to a fixed share
حكومة (hukuma): Equitable compensation assessed by experts for injury to a body part not covered by fixed diya
الميلين الأخضرين (al-milayn al-akhdarayn): Two green milestones between the hills of Safa and Marwa in Mecca

This passage systematically outlines Hanafi exemptions and modifications for women across all major areas of fiqh, revealing a coherent principle: women are protected and excused from public duties to preserve their dignity and security.

Rulings on the Dhimmī in Hanafi Fiqh
A list of distinct legal rules for a protected non-Muslim subject

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general principle governing the dhimmī's legal status and list at least five specific exceptions regarding worship, property, and social interactions.

Core Idea
The dhimmī shares Muslim rulings in all except worship, some crimes, and social distinction – yet their statements are accepted in transactions.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir collects the key legal rules for the dhimmī, a non-Muslim under Islamic protection. Understanding these rules is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas involving dhimmīs in areas of contracts, criminal liability, and communal coexistence. The rulings balance inclusion in civil matters with differentiation in religious and social spheres.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The passage opens with the default rule: the dhimmī has the same ruling as Muslims in everything. Note that exceptions follow, so the burden of proof is on the exception.
This is a key hermeneutic: the default is equality, and exceptions are explicit.
2
Categorize the Exceptions
Group the exceptions into themes: acts of worship (ibadat), property and contracts (muamalat), criminal penalties (hudud and ta'zir), social distinctions (garb, greeting), and procedural rules (testimony).
Each category has its own hikmah (legal rationale).
3
Analyze the Dispute on Testimony
Note the disagreement between al-Zayla'i and the author of al-Kanz regarding acceptance of the dhimmī's statement on halal and haram. Understand the resolution: acceptance is limited to transactional contexts.
This is a mufti-level dispute (ikhtilaf) between later authorities.
4
Extract the Social Distinction Rules
List the specific dress, riding, and housing restrictions. Recognize that the mufta bihi position uses a single mark, but the stricter view requires all.
These rules change with time and place (urf) – a key consideration for fatwa.
5
Summarize the Hadd Application
The passage concludes with a principle: all hudud apply except the hadd for wine. This is an exception to the default equality.
The hadd for zina is flogging, not stoning, because a dhimmī is not subject to ihsan.

أحكام الذمّي
له حكمه حكم المسلمين؛ إلا أنه لا يؤمر بالعبادات ولا تصح منه ولا يصح تيممه، ويصح وضوؤه وغسله فلو أسلم جازت صلاته به. ولا يأثم على ترك العبادات على قول، ويأثم على ترك اعتقادها إجماعا ولا يمنع من دخول المسجد جنبا بخلاف المسلم ولا يتوقف جواز دخوله على إذن مسلم عندنا، ولو كان المسجد الحرام. ولا يصح نذره ولا سهم من الغنيمة. ويرضخ له إن قاتل أو دل على الطريق، ولا يحد بشرب الخمر ولا تراق عليه بل ترد عليه إذا غصبت منه. ويضمن متلفها له إلا أن يظهر بيعها بين المسلمين فلا ضمان في إراقتها أو يكون المتلف إماما يرى ذلك بخلاف إتلاف خمر المسلم فإنه لا يوجب الضمان ولو كان المتلف ذميا، وينبغي أن يكون إظهاره شربها كإظهاره بيعها ولم أره الآن، ولا يمنع من لبس الحرير والذهب ولا يعترض لهم لو تناكحوا فاسدا أو تبايعوا كذلك ثم أسلموا. وفي الكنز: ويقبل قول الكافر في الحل والحرمة. وتعقبه الزيلعي بأنه سهو ولا يقبل قوله فيهما وجوابه أنه يقبل فيهما ضمن المعاملات لا مقصودا وهو مراده، كما أفصح به في الكافي. ويأخذ الذمي بالتميز عنا في المركب والملبس فيركبون بالأكف ولا يلبسون الطيالسة والأردية ولا ثياب أهل العلم والشرف وتجعل على دورهم علامة، ولا يحدثون بيعة ولا كنيسة في مصر. واختلفت الرواية في سكناهم بين المسلمين في المصر، والمعتمد الجواز في محلة خاصة واختلف المشايخ رحمهم الله هل يلزم تمييزهم بجميع العلامات أو تكفي واحدة والمعتمد أنهم لا يركبون مطلقا ولا يلبسون العمائم. وإن ركب الحمار لضرورة نزل في المجامع ويضيق عليه في المرور، ولا يرجم إنما يجلد. والحاصل أنه تقام الحدود كلها عليه إلا حد شرب الخمر، ولا يبدأ الذمي بسلام إلا لحاجة ولا يزاد في الجواب على وعليك وتكره مصافحته، ويحرم تعظيمه، ويكره للمسلم أن يؤجر نفسه من كافر لعصر العنب. وفي الملتقط: كل شيء امتنع منه المسلم امتنع منه الذمي إلا الخمر والخنزير. ولا تكره عبادة جاره
Rulings of the Dhimmī. His ruling is the same as that of Muslims, except that he is not commanded to perform acts of worship, nor are they valid from him, and his tayammum is not valid. His ablution and bath are valid, so if he accepts Islam, his prayer is valid with it. He does not sin by abandoning acts of worship according to one opinion, but he sins by abandoning belief in them by consensus. He is not prevented from entering the mosque in a state of major impurity, unlike a Muslim, and permissibility of his entry does not depend on a Muslim's permission according to us, even if it is the Sacred Mosque. His vow is not valid, nor is his share of booty. He is given a discretionary grant if he fights or guides the way. He is not subjected to the hadd punishment for drinking wine, and it is not poured away over his objection, but rather it is returned to him if taken from him by force. The one who destroys it is liable to compensate him, unless its sale among Muslims becomes apparent, in which case there is no liability for pouring it away, or if the destroyer is an imam who holds that view. Unlike destroying a Muslim's wine, which does not incur liability even if the destroyer is a dhimmī. And it should be that his openly drinking it is like his openly selling it, but I have not seen it now. He is not prevented from wearing silk and gold, and they are not objected to if they marry or trade invalidly and then accept Islam. In al-Kanz: 'The word of a disbeliever is accepted regarding what is permissible and forbidden.' Al-Zayla'i followed it up saying it is a mistake, and his statement is not accepted in either. The answer is that it is accepted in both within transactions, not as a primary intent, and that is what is meant, as clarified in al-Kafi. The dhimmī is made distinct from us in riding and dress: they ride on packsaddles, do not wear tailasans, cloaks, or clothes of scholars and nobility, and a mark is placed on their houses. They do not establish churches or synagogues in the city. There is a difference of narration concerning their residence among Muslims in the city; the relied-upon position is permissibility in a specific quarter. The scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) differed as to whether all distinguishing marks are necessary or one suffices; the relied-upon position is that they do not ride at all and do not wear turbans. If they ride a donkey out of necessity, they dismount in crowded places and squeeze through in passage. They are not stoned but rather flogged. The summary: all hudud punishments are carried out on him except the hadd for drinking wine. The dhimmī is not started with greeting except for need, and the response is no more than 'and upon you'. Shaking hands with him is disliked, respecting him is forbidden, and it is disliked for a Muslim to hire himself to a disbeliever for pressing grapes. In al-Multaqat: 'Everything a Muslim is prohibited from, the dhimmī is also prohibited from, except wine and pig.' Worship of his neighbor is not disliked.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents a collection of Hanafi rulings specific to the dhimmī, a non-Muslim living under Islamic protection. The opening principle: the dhimmī shares the same rulings as Muslims in everything except what is explicitly excluded. The first exception is that acts of worship (prayer, fasting, etc.) are not commanded upon him, and if he performs them they are not valid. However, his purification (wudu, ghusl) is valid, so if he embraces Islam, his prayer performed with that purification is valid. He does not sin for abandoning worship according to one opinion, but he does sin for abandoning belief (kufr) by consensus. He may enter the mosque even in janabah, unlike a Muslim, and does not need permission even for Masjid al-Haram. His nadhr (vow) is invalid. He receives no share of ghanimah but may get a discretionary grant if he fights or guides. The hadd for wine is not applied to him, and his wine is protected property; if taken by force, it must be returned. If someone destroys it, they must compensate him unless the wine was openly sold among Muslims, in which case there is no guarantee. An imam who considers wine property may also destroy without liability. Openly drinking wine is likened to openly selling it in terms of removing protection. The dhimmī may wear silk and gold. Invalid marriages and sales among them are left alone, and if they later accept Islam, those contracts are not revisited. A dispute is mentioned from al-Kanz: the statement of a disbeliever is accepted regarding halal and haram. Al-Zayla'i criticized this, but the response clarifies that it is accepted within transactions, not as a primary testimony. The dhimmī must be distinguished in riding and dress: they ride on packsaddles (not saddles), do not wear tailasans (a type of cloak), cloaks, or clothing of scholars and nobles. They must place a mark on their homes. They cannot build new churches or synagogues in cities founded by Muslims. Their residence among Muslims is permissible, but preferably in a separate quarter. There is a dispute whether all distinguishing marks are necessary; the relied-upon view is that they must not ride at all and not wear turbans. If a dhimmī rides a donkey out of necessity, he must dismount in crowds. For zina, the dhimmī is flogged, not stoned. The conclusion: all hudud are applied to the dhimmī except the hadd for wine. Social interactions: do not initiate greeting, reply minimally, avoid handshake, do not show respect, and it is disliked for a Muslim to work for a dhimmī in grape-pressing. Finally, al-Multaqat states that everything prohibited for a Muslim is also prohibited for a dhimmī except wine and pork. Worshipping his neighbor (i.e., the dhimmī's worship) is not disliked.

Key Terms
ذمّي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim who lives permanently under Muslim rule with a pact of protection
رضخ (radkh): A discretionary grant from booty given to non-combatants such as dhimmis, women, and children
طيلسة (taylasan): A type of cloak or shawl worn by scholars and nobles
بِيعة (bi'a): A church building for Christian worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is a dhimmī's wine considered protected property such that destruction incurs compensation?
A) Always, because wine is his property
B) Only if he has not openly sold it among Muslims
C) Never, because wine is inherently impure
D) Only if he is a Muslim

Key Takeaway
The dhimmī is a legal subject with rights and duties distinct from Muslims, balancing protection and differentiation in a framework that respects their status while upholding Islamic norms.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

The Hanafi Qawida of Mahram: Definition and General Rulings
Definition and general rules of mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida defining mahram, identify which relationships are mahram, and apply the general rulings of looking, privacy, and travel with mahrams, including exceptions for breastfeeding.

Core Idea
A mahram is one permanently prohibited in marriage due to lineage, marriage, or breastfeeding, even from zina, and this status permits looking, privacy, and travel except for some breastfeeding cases.

The Hanafi school defines mahram with a precise qawida that covers not only permitted marriages but also rights of looking, privacy, and travel. This lesson unpacks that definition and its immediate applications, noting where breastfeeding mahrams differ from those by lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of mahram
Read the opening sentence: 'A mahram is one whose marriage is perpetually prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if through unlawful intercourse.' Note the three causes and the inclusion of zina.
The phrase 'even if through unlawful intercourse' is a distinctive Hanafi position.
2
Distinguish the three types
Classify relationships as nasab (lineage), musahara (affinity), or rada' (breastfeeding). The text gives examples: paternal uncles' children are excluded (not mahram); sister of the wife, her aunt, mother of one's adulterous partner are included.
Remember: cousins are not mahram; in-laws from zina are.
3
Apply the definition to sample cases
Test cases: maternal uncle's daughter (not mahram), father's wife's sister (in-law? careful: sister of wife is mahram as long as wife is alive). Also the mother of one's adulterous partner becomes mahram.
The text explicitly says 'mother of the one with whom one committed adultery' is a mahram.
4
State the general rulings of mahram status
List: marriage is haram, looking is permissible, privacy (khalwa) is permissible, and travel is permissible (e.g., she can travel with a mahram).
These are the default rulings for all mahrams.
5
Note the exception for breastfeeding mahrams
The text says: 'except the mahram from breastfeeding, for privacy with her is disliked, and likewise with a young in-law.' So for rada' mahrams, privacy is makruh, not haram.
Also, the husband shares these rights with mahrams, but trustworthy women do not replace a mahram for travel.

أحكام المحارم
نكاحه على التأبيد بنسب أو مصاهرة أو رضاع ولو
المحرم عندنا من حرم : بوطء حرام ; فخرج بالأول ولد العمومة والخؤولة وبالثاني أخت الزوجة وعمتها أو خالتها، وشمل أم المزني بها وبنتها وآباء الزاني وابنه.
وأحكامه تحريم النكاح وجواز النظر والخلوة والمسافرة إلا المحرم من الرضاع، فإن الخلوة بها مكروهة وكذا بالصهرة الشابة وحرمة النكاح على التأبيد لا مشاركة للمحرم فيها ; فإن الملاعنة تحلّ إذا أكذب نفسه أو خرج عن أهلية الشهادة، والمجوسية تحلّ بالإسلام أو بتهودها أو تنصرها، والمطلقة ثلاثا بدخول الثاني وانقضاء عدتها ومنكوحة الغير بطلاقها وانقضاء عدتها ومعتدة الغير بانقضاء عدتها . وكذا لا مشاركة للمحرم في جواز النظر والخلوة والسفر وأما عبدها فكالأجنبي على المعتمد لكن الزوج يشارك المحرم في هذه الثلاثة والنساء الثقات لا يقمن مقام الزوج والمحرم في السفر .

في عشر مسائل ذكرناها في شرح الكنز ; فإن فرَّق صح البيع. ومنها أن المحرمية مانعة من الرجوع في الهبة.
وتختص الأصول والفروع من بين سائر المحارم بأحكام منها أنها لا يقطع أحدهما بسرقة مال الآخر ومنها لا يقضي ولا يشهد أحدهما للآخر. ومنها تحريم موطوءة كلِّ منهما على الآخر ولو بزنا. ومنها تحريم منكوحة كل منهما على الآخر بمجرد العقد. ومنها لا يدخلون في الوصية للأقارب.
وتختص الأصول بأحكام منها لا يجوز له قتل أصله الحربي إلا دفعا عن نفسه، وإن خاف رجوعه ضيّق عليه وألجأه ليقتله غيره، وله قتل فرعه الحربي كمحرمه. ومنها لا يقتل الأصل بفرعه ويقتل الفرع بأصله. ومنها لا يحدّ الأصل بقذف فرعه ويحدّ الفرع بقذف أصله ومنها لا تجوز مسافرة الفرع إلا بإذن أصله دون عكسه ومنها لو ادعى الأصل ولد جارية ابنه ثبت نسبه . والجدّ أب الأب كالأب عند عدمه ولو حكمًا لعدم الأهلية بخلاف الفرع إذا ادعى ولد جارية أصله لم يصح إلا بتصديق الأصل ومنها لا يجوز الجهاد إلا بإذنهم بخلاف الأصول لا يتوقف جهادهم على إذن الفروع ومنها لا تجوز المسافرة إلا بإذنهم إن كان الطريق مخوفا، وإلا فإن لم يكن ملتحيا فكذلك وإلا فلا. ومنها إذا دعاه أحد أبويه في الصلاة وجبت إجابته إلا أن يكون عالما بكونه فيها .

واختص الأب والجد بأحكام : منها ولاية المال; فلا ولاية للأم في مال الصغير إلا الحفظ وشراء ما لا بد منه للصغير. ومنها تولّي طرفي العقد; فلو باع الأب ماله من ابنه أو اشترى وليس فيه غبن فاحش انعقد بكلام واحد ومنها عدم خيار البلوغ في تزويج الأب والجد فقط وأما ولاية الإنكاح فلا تختص بهما فيثبت لكل ولي سواء كان عصبة أو من ذوي الأرحام وكذا الصلاة في الجنازة لا تختص بهما. وفي الملتقط من النكاح : لو ضرب المعلم الولد بإذن الأب فهلك لم يغرم إلا أن يضرب ضربا لا
٢٨٦
Rulings on Mahrams: [A mahram is] one whose marriage is perpetually prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if [the sexual act] is unlawful. So the mahram according to us is one who is prohibited [from marriage] due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if through unlawful intercourse. Thus by the first [type] is excluded children of paternal uncles and aunts and maternal uncles and aunts; by the second [type] is included the sister of the wife, and her paternal aunt or maternal aunt; and it includes the mother of the one with whom one committed adultery, and her daughter, and the father of the adulterer and his son. And its rulings are: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel – except the mahram from breastfeeding, for privacy with her is disliked, and likewise with a young in-law; and permanent prohibition of marriage – no participation [in the prohibition] for the mahram in it; for the woman who is the subject of li'an becomes permissible if he retracts his accusation or becomes disqualified from testimony; and the Magian woman becomes permissible by Islam, or by her becoming a Jewess or Christian; and the thrice-divorced woman [becomes permissible] by the second husband's consummation and completion of her idda; and the wife of another [becomes permissible] by divorce and completion of her idda; and the woman in idda of another [becomes permissible] by completion of her idda. Similarly, there is no participation for the mahram in the permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel. As for her slave, he is like a stranger in the relied-upon view, but the husband shares with the mahram in these three, and trustworthy women do not take the place of the husband and mahram in travel. And the mahram by lineage is specified with rulings, among them: his freeing of his relative if he owns him, and this is not specific to ancestors and descendants; among them: the obligation of maintenance of the needy incapable relative by his wealthy relative, so he must be a mahram from the direction of kinship; so the cousin and the brother from breastfeeding are not freed, nor is his maintenance obligatory; and the mahram washes his female relative; among them: it is not permissible to separate a minor from his mahram by sale or gift except in ten cases which we mentioned in Sharh al-Kanz; if he separates, the sale is valid. Among them: the mahram relationship prevents returning a gift. And the ancestors and descendants are specified among other mahrams with rulings, among them: one of them is not cut off for stealing the property of the other; among them: one does not judge nor testify for the other; among them: the prohibition of each other's concubine even by adultery; among them: the prohibition of each other's wife merely by the contract; among them: they are not included in the will for relatives. And the ancestors are specified with rulings, among them: it is not permissible for him to kill his ancestor if he is a combatant except in self-defense; if he fears his return, he may restrict him and compel him so that someone else kills him; and he may kill his descendant if a combatant, like his mahram. Among them: the ancestor is not killed for the descendant, but the descendant is killed for the ancestor. Among them: the ancestor is not hadd-punished for slandering his descendant, but the descendant is hadd-punished for slandering his ancestor. Among them: the descendant may not travel except with the permission of his ancestor, without the reverse. Among them: if the ancestor claims a child of his son's slave-girl, his lineage is established. And the grandfather, the father's father, is like the father when he is absent, even if by legal consideration due to lack of capacity – contrary to the descendant if he claims a child of his ancestor's slave-girl, it is not valid except with the ancestor's confirmation. Among them: jihad is not permissible except with their permission, contrary to ancestors – their jihad does not depend on the permission of descendants. Among them: travel is not permissible except with their permission if the road is dangerous; otherwise, if he is not bearded [i.e., a minor], then likewise; otherwise no. Among them: if one of his parents calls him during prayer, it is obligatory to respond unless he knows that he is in it. And I have not seen the ruling for grandparents. It is appropriate to analogize. Among them: it is disliked for him to perform Hajj without the permission of either parent if he needs their service. Among them: the permissibility of the ancestor disciplining his descendant. The apparent view is that it is not exclusive to the father; so the mother, grandparents are likewise. I have not seen that now. Among them: the descendant follows the ancestor in Islam. And we have written the issues of the grandfather and what takes the father's place in it in the art of al-Fawa'id. Among them: they are not imprisoned for the debt of the descendant, and likewise grandparents. And the male ancestors are specified with the obligation of providing sexual satisfaction. And the father and grandfather are specified with rulings: among them: guardianship of wealth; so there is no guardianship for the mother over the minor's wealth except for preservation and purchasing what is necessary for the minor. Among them: contracting both sides of the transaction; so if the father sells his property to his son or buys from him without excessive fraud, it is valid with one utterance. Among them: the absence of option of puberty in the marriage contracted by the father and grandfather only. As for guardianship in marriage, it is not exclusive to them; it is established for every guardian, whether an asaba or a relative. Likewise the prayer over the funeral is not exclusive to them. And in al-Multaqat min al-Nikah: if the teacher strikes the child with the father's permission and he dies, he is not liable unless he strikes a blow that is not [customary].
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive compilation of qawaid (maxims) and their furuat (applications) concerning mahrams. The core definition: a mahram is one whose marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if the sexual act leading to that relationship was unlawful (zina). The text then lists numerous rulings that follow from mahram status: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel—with exceptions for breastfeeding mahrams (privacy is disliked) and young in-laws. It clarifies that temporary prohibitions (like li'an, different religion, triple divorce) are not permanent and thus not mahram. The husband shares some rights (looking, privacy, travel) with mahrams, but trustworthy women do not replace a mahram for travel. The passage then details specific rulings for three categories: (1) all mahrams by lineage, (2) ancestors and descendants specifically, (3) male ancestors only, and (4) father and grandfather only. Each category has unique rules: e.g., freeing of relative, maintenance obligation, prohibition of separating minor from mahram except in ten cases, no cutting of hand for theft between usul/furu, no execution of parent for child but vice versa, no hadd for slander of descendant, travel restrictions, establishment of lineage if ancestor claims, necessity of permission for jihad and travel, obligation to respond to parent's call in prayer, and many more. The author also notes gaps (e.g., grandparents' rulings) and suggests analogical extension. This is a classic example of how a single concept (mahram) branches into dozens of fiqh rulings across different chapters (jinayat, hudud, nikah, hajj, jihad, etc.). The Hanafi school's precise categorization is evident: mahram by breastfeeding does not carry all the same rulings as by lineage (e.g., privacy disliked).

Key Terms
المحرم (al-mahram): One whose marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if through unlawful intercourse.
الصهرة (al-sihra): Woman related by marriage (in-law).
الخلوة (al-khalwa): Privacy between a man and a woman who are not married but are mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qawida, which of the following is NOT a mahram?
A) One's own daughter
B) One's father's sister
C) One's maternal uncle's daughter
D) One's wife's mother

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of mahram includes relationships arising from unlawful intercourse, and the status permits looking, privacy, and travel except for breastfeeding mahrams where privacy is disliked.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications

Rulings Specific to Lineage Mahrams: Maintenance, Freeing, and Separation of Minors
Specific rulings for mahrams by lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings that are specific to mahrams by lineage, including the obligation of maintenance, the rule of freeing a relative when owned, and the prohibition of separating a minor from his mahram by sale or gift.

Core Idea
Lineage mahrams have additional obligations: wealthy relatives must support needy mahrams, owning a mahram relative requires freeing them, and separating a minor from his mahram is prohibited except in ten cases.

Not only does mahram status forbid marriage, but it also creates financial and personal obligations. This lesson focuses on three key rulings that apply specifically to mahrams by lineage: the duty of maintenance, the rule of freeing when owned, and the prohibition of selling a minor away from his mahram.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scope of lineage mahrams
Recall that mahrams by lineage include ascendants (parents, grandparents), descendants (children, grandchildren), and collateral relatives like siblings, uncles/aunts (but not their children). The rulings in this lesson apply to all these, with specifics for different subcategories.
These rulings do not apply to mahrams by marriage or breastfeeding except where noted.
2
Explain the obligation of maintenance (nafaqa)
The text states: 'obligation of maintenance of the needy incapable relative by his wealthy relative, so he must be a mahram from the direction of kinship.' This means a wealthy person must support his needy mahram relative, and this duty is limited to those related by lineage and within the mahram network.
Cousins are not included because they are not mahram. Breastfeeding brothers are also not included.
3
Describe the rule of freeing when owning a relative
If a person comes to own his mahram relative (e.g., inherits a sibling who is a slave), he must free that relative. This is specific to mahram by lineage, not to every relative.
This applies to all lineage mahrams, not just ancestors/descendants.
4
Analyze the prohibition of separating a minor from his mahram
The text says: 'it is not permissible to separate a minor from his mahram by sale or gift except in ten cases.' If such a sale occurs, the sale is valid (the property transfers) but the separation is sinful.
The author refers to Sharh al-Kanz for the ten exceptions.

أحكام المحارم
نكاحه على التأبيد بنسب أو مصاهرة أو رضاع ولو
المحرم عندنا من حرم : بوطء حرام ; فخرج بالأول ولد العمومة والخؤولة وبالثاني أخت الزوجة وعمتها أو خالتها، وشمل أم المزني بها وبنتها وآباء الزاني وابنه.
وأحكامه تحريم النكاح وجواز النظر والخلوة والمسافرة إلا المحرم من الرضاع، فإن الخلوة بها مكروهة وكذا بالصهرة الشابة وحرمة النكاح على التأبيد لا مشاركة للمحرم فيها ; فإن الملاعنة تحلّ إذا أكذب نفسه أو خرج عن أهلية الشهادة، والمجوسية تحلّ بالإسلام أو بتهودها أو تنصرها، والمطلقة ثلاثا بدخول الثاني وانقضاء عدتها ومنكوحة الغير بطلاقها وانقضاء عدتها ومعتدة الغير بانقضاء عدتها . وكذا لا مشاركة للمحرم في جواز النظر والخلوة والسفر وأما عبدها فكالأجنبي على المعتمد لكن الزوج يشارك المحرم في هذه الثلاثة والنساء الثقات لا يقمن مقام الزوج والمحرم في السفر .
،
واختص المحرم النسبي بأحكام منها عتقه على قريبه لو ملكه، ولا يختص بالأصل والفرع ومنها وجوب نفقة الفقير العاجز على قريبه الغني فلا بد من كونه رحما محرمًا من جهة القرابة ; فابن العم والأخ من الرضاع لا يعتق ولا تجب نفقته، ويغسل المحرم قريبته ومنها أنه لا يجوز التفريق بين صغير ومحرم ببيع أو هبة إلا
٢٨٥

في عشر مسائل ذكرناها في شرح الكنز ; فإن فرَّق صح البيع. ومنها أن المحرمية مانعة من الرجوع في الهبة.
وتختص الأصول والفروع من بين سائر المحارم بأحكام منها أنها لا يقطع أحدهما بسرقة مال الآخر ومنها لا يقضي ولا يشهد أحدهما للآخر. ومنها تحريم موطوءة كلِّ منهما على الآخر ولو بزنا. ومنها تحريم منكوحة كل منهما على الآخر بمجرد العقد. ومنها لا يدخلون في الوصية للأقارب.
وتختص الأصول بأحكام منها لا يجوز له قتل أصله الحربي إلا دفعا عن نفسه، وإن خاف رجوعه ضيّق عليه وألجأه ليقتله غيره، وله قتل فرعه الحربي كمحرمه. ومنها لا يقتل الأصل بفرعه ويقتل الفرع بأصله. ومنها لا يحدّ الأصل بقذف فرعه ويحدّ الفرع بقذف أصله ومنها لا تجوز مسافرة الفرع إلا بإذن أصله دون عكسه ومنها لو ادعى الأصل ولد جارية ابنه ثبت نسبه . والجدّ أب الأب كالأب عند عدمه ولو حكمًا لعدم الأهلية بخلاف الفرع إذا ادعى ولد جارية أصله لم يصح إلا بتصديق الأصل ومنها لا يجوز الجهاد إلا بإذنهم بخلاف الأصول لا يتوقف جهادهم على إذن الفروع ومنها لا تجوز المسافرة إلا بإذنهم إن كان الطريق مخوفا، وإلا فإن لم يكن ملتحيا فكذلك وإلا فلا. ومنها إذا دعاه أحد أبويه في الصلاة وجبت إجابته إلا أن يكون عالما بكونه فيها .
