·
ولم أرَ حكم الأجداد والجدات. وينبغي الإلحاق ومنها كراهة حجه بدون إذن من كرهه من أبويه إن احتاج إلى خدمته ومنها جواز تأديب الأصل فرعه. والظاهر عدم الاختصاص بالأب ; فالأم والأجداد والجدات كذلك. ولم أره الآن. ومنها تبعية الفرع للأصل في الإسلام وكتبنا مسائل الجدّ وما يقوم مقام الأب فيه في فن الفوائد. ومنها لا يحبسون بدين الفرع والأجداد والجدات كذلك.
واختص الأصول الذكور بوجوب الإعفاف.
واختص الأب والجد بأحكام : منها ولاية المال; فلا ولاية للأم في مال الصغير إلا الحفظ وشراء ما لا بد منه للصغير. ومنها تولّي طرفي العقد; فلو باع الأب ماله من ابنه أو اشترى وليس فيه غبن فاحش انعقد بكلام واحد ومنها عدم خيار البلوغ في تزويج الأب والجد فقط وأما ولاية الإنكاح فلا تختص بهما فيثبت لكل ولي سواء كان عصبة أو من ذوي الأرحام وكذا الصلاة في الجنازة لا تختص بهما. وفي الملتقط من النكاح : لو ضرب المعلم الولد بإذن الأب فهلك لم يغرم إلا أن يضرب ضربا لا
٢٨٦
Rulings on Mahrams: [A mahram is] one whose marriage is perpetually prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if [the sexual act] is unlawful. So the mahram according to us is one who is prohibited [from marriage] due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if through unlawful intercourse. Thus by the first [type] is excluded children of paternal uncles and aunts and maternal uncles and aunts; by the second [type] is included the sister of the wife, and her paternal aunt or maternal aunt; and it includes the mother of the one with whom one committed adultery, and her daughter, and the father of the adulterer and his son. And its rulings are: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel – except the mahram from breastfeeding, for privacy with her is disliked, and likewise with a young in-law; and permanent prohibition of marriage – no participation [in the prohibition] for the mahram in it; for the woman who is the subject of li'an becomes permissible if he retracts his accusation or becomes disqualified from testimony; and the Magian woman becomes permissible by Islam, or by her becoming a Jewess or Christian; and the thrice-divorced woman [becomes permissible] by the second husband's consummation and completion of her idda; and the wife of another [becomes permissible] by divorce and completion of her idda; and the woman in idda of another [becomes permissible] by completion of her idda. Similarly, there is no participation for the mahram in the permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel. As for her slave, he is like a stranger in the relied-upon view, but the husband shares with the mahram in these three, and trustworthy women do not take the place of the husband and mahram in travel. And the mahram by lineage is specified with rulings, among them: his freeing of his relative if he owns him, and this is not specific to ancestors and descendants; among them: the obligation of maintenance of the needy incapable relative by his wealthy relative, so he must be a mahram from the direction of kinship; so the cousin and the brother from breastfeeding are not freed, nor is his maintenance obligatory; and the mahram washes his female relative; among them: it is not permissible to separate a minor from his mahram by sale or gift except in ten cases which we mentioned in Sharh al-Kanz; if he separates, the sale is valid. Among them: the mahram relationship prevents returning a gift. And the ancestors and descendants are specified among other mahrams with rulings, among them: one of them is not cut off for stealing the property of the other; among them: one does not judge nor testify for the other; among them: the prohibition of each other's concubine even by adultery; among them: the prohibition of each other's wife merely by the contract; among them: they are not included in the will for relatives. And the ancestors are specified with rulings, among them: it is not permissible for him to kill his ancestor if he is a combatant except in self-defense; if he fears his return, he may restrict him and compel him so that someone else kills him; and he may kill his descendant if a combatant, like his mahram. Among them: the ancestor is not killed for the descendant, but the descendant is killed for the ancestor. Among them: the ancestor is not hadd-punished for slandering his descendant, but the descendant is hadd-punished for slandering his ancestor. Among them: the descendant may not travel except with the permission of his ancestor, without the reverse. Among them: if the ancestor claims a child of his son's slave-girl, his lineage is established. And the grandfather, the father's father, is like the father when he is absent, even if by legal consideration due to lack of capacity – contrary to the descendant if he claims a child of his ancestor's slave-girl, it is not valid except with the ancestor's confirmation. Among them: jihad is not permissible except with their permission, contrary to ancestors – their jihad does not depend on the permission of descendants. Among them: travel is not permissible except with their permission if the road is dangerous; otherwise, if he is not bearded [i.e., a minor], then likewise; otherwise no. Among them: if one of his parents calls him during prayer, it is obligatory to respond unless he knows that he is in it. And I have not seen the ruling for grandparents. It is appropriate to analogize. Among them: it is disliked for him to perform Hajj without the permission of either parent if he needs their service. Among them: the permissibility of the ancestor disciplining his descendant. The apparent view is that it is not exclusive to the father; so the mother, grandparents are likewise. I have not seen that now. Among them: the descendant follows the ancestor in Islam. And we have written the issues of the grandfather and what takes the father's place in it in the art of al-Fawa'id. Among them: they are not imprisoned for the debt of the descendant, and likewise grandparents. And the male ancestors are specified with the obligation of providing sexual satisfaction. And the father and grandfather are specified with rulings: among them: guardianship of wealth; so there is no guardianship for the mother over the minor's wealth except for preservation and purchasing what is necessary for the minor. Among them: contracting both sides of the transaction; so if the father sells his property to his son or buys from him without excessive fraud, it is valid with one utterance. Among them: the absence of option of puberty in the marriage contracted by the father and grandfather only. As for guardianship in marriage, it is not exclusive to them; it is established for every guardian, whether an asaba or a relative. Likewise the prayer over the funeral is not exclusive to them. And in al-Multaqat min al-Nikah: if the teacher strikes the child with the father's permission and he dies, he is not liable unless he strikes a blow that is not [customary].
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive compilation of qawaid (maxims) and their furuat (applications) concerning mahrams. The core definition: a mahram is one whose marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if the sexual act leading to that relationship was unlawful (zina). The text then lists numerous rulings that follow from mahram status: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel—with exceptions for breastfeeding mahrams (privacy is disliked) and young in-laws. It clarifies that temporary prohibitions (like li'an, different religion, triple divorce) are not permanent and thus not mahram. The husband shares some rights (looking, privacy, travel) with mahrams, but trustworthy women do not replace a mahram for travel. The passage then details specific rulings for three categories: (1) all mahrams by lineage, (2) ancestors and descendants specifically, (3) male ancestors only, and (4) father and grandfather only. Each category has unique rules: e.g., freeing of relative, maintenance obligation, prohibition of separating minor from mahram except in ten cases, no cutting of hand for theft between usul/furu, no execution of parent for child but vice versa, no hadd for slander of descendant, travel restrictions, establishment of lineage if ancestor claims, necessity of permission for jihad and travel, obligation to respond to parent's call in prayer, and many more. The author also notes gaps (e.g., grandparents' rulings) and suggests analogical extension. This is a classic example of how a single concept (mahram) branches into dozens of fiqh rulings across different chapters (jinayat, hudud, nikah, hajj, jihad, etc.). The Hanafi school's precise categorization is evident: mahram by breastfeeding does not carry all the same rulings as by lineage (e.g., privacy disliked).

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqa): Maintenance; financial support including food, clothing, and shelter.
العتق (al-itq): Freeing a slave; here, required if one owns a mahram relative.
التفريق (al-tafriq): Separating a minor from his mahram by selling or gifting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true regarding the sale of a minor from his mahram?
A) The sale is absolutely invalid
B) The sale is valid but sinful unless an exception applies
C) The sale is valid only with the mahram's consent
D) The sale is allowed only for male minors

Key Takeaway
Lineage mahrams have special rights and obligations: maintenance, freeing upon ownership, and the prohibition of separating minors, with exceptions limited to ten cases.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
advanced
10 min
Rulings Specific to Ancestors and Descendants (Usul and Furu)
Rulings specific to ancestors and descendants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the unique rulings that apply only between ancestors (usul) and descendants (furu) among mahrams, such as no hand-cutting for theft, no testimony and judgment, travel and jihad permission, and rules for killing combatants.

Core Idea
Between ancestors and descendants, special criminal, financial, and travel rules apply that do not apply to other mahrams, emphasizing the unique bond of direct lineage.

Direct lineage (usul and furu) holds a special place in Hanafi fiqh, with rulings that go beyond general mahram status. This lesson covers the distinctive rules that apply only between a person and their parents, children, and grandparents, including provisions in criminal law, testimony, travel, jihad, and lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope: ancestors (usul) include parents, grandparents; descendants (furu) include children, grandchildren.
The text specifies 'ancestors and descendants from among other mahrams.' These rulings apply only to the direct line, not to siblings, aunts, uncles, etc.
Grandparents are included by analogy when absent.
2
List the criminal and judicial rulings
Among them: no hand-cutting for theft between usul/furu; no testimony or judgment for each other; ancestor not executed for killing descendant but descendant executed for killing ancestor; no hadd for slander of descendant but descendant gets hadd for slandering ancestor.
This shows a hierarchy of protection favoring the ancestor.
3
Explain travel and jihad rules
A descendant may not travel or perform jihad without the permission of his ancestor (if the road is dangerous or if he is a minor). An ancestor does not need the descendant's permission for travel or jihad.
These rules apply to both parents, not just father.
4
Discuss lineage and inheritance implications
If an ancestor claims a child of his descendant's slave-girl, the lineage is established. The reverse (descendant claiming) requires confirmation by the ancestor. Also, the descendant is not imprisoned for the ancestor's debt, and vice versa? Actually text says 'they are not imprisoned for the debt of the descendant' – meaning ancestors are not jailed for descendant's debt.
This protects the ancestor from liability.

Rulings on Mahrams: [A mahram is] one whose marriage is perpetually prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if [the sexual act] is unlawful. So the mahram according to us is one who is prohibited [from marriage] due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if through unlawful intercourse. Thus by the first [type] is excluded children of paternal uncles and aunts and maternal uncles and aunts; by the second [type] is included the sister of the wife, and her paternal aunt or maternal aunt; and it includes the mother of the one with whom one committed adultery, and her daughter, and the father of the adulterer and his son. And its rulings are: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel – except the mahram from breastfeeding, for privacy with her is disliked, and likewise with a young in-law; and permanent prohibition of marriage – no participation [in the prohibition] for the mahram in it; for the woman who is the subject of li'an becomes permissible if he retracts his accusation or becomes disqualified from testimony; and the Magian woman becomes permissible by Islam, or by her becoming a Jewess or Christian; and the thrice-divorced woman [becomes permissible] by the second husband's consummation and completion of her idda; and the wife of another [becomes permissible] by divorce and completion of her idda; and the woman in idda of another [becomes permissible] by completion of her idda. Similarly, there is no participation for the mahram in the permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel. As for her slave, he is like a stranger in the relied-upon view, but the husband shares with the mahram in these three, and trustworthy women do not take the place of the husband and mahram in travel. And the mahram by lineage is specified with rulings, among them: his freeing of his relative if he owns him, and this is not specific to ancestors and descendants; among them: the obligation of maintenance of the needy incapable relative by his wealthy relative, so he must be a mahram from the direction of kinship; so the cousin and the brother from breastfeeding are not freed, nor is his maintenance obligatory; and the mahram washes his female relative; among them: it is not permissible to separate a minor from his mahram by sale or gift except in ten cases which we mentioned in Sharh al-Kanz; if he separates, the sale is valid. Among them: the mahram relationship prevents returning a gift. And the ancestors and descendants are specified among other mahrams with rulings, among them: one of them is not cut off for stealing the property of the other; among them: one does not judge nor testify for the other; among them: the prohibition of each other's concubine even by adultery; among them: the prohibition of each other's wife merely by the contract; among them: they are not included in the will for relatives. And the ancestors are specified with rulings, among them: it is not permissible for him to kill his ancestor if he is a combatant except in self-defense; if he fears his return, he may restrict him and compel him so that someone else kills him; and he may kill his descendant if a combatant, like his mahram. Among them: the ancestor is not killed for the descendant, but the descendant is killed for the ancestor. Among them: the ancestor is not hadd-punished for slandering his descendant, but the descendant is hadd-punished for slandering his ancestor. Among them: the descendant may not travel except with the permission of his ancestor, without the reverse. Among them: if the ancestor claims a child of his son's slave-girl, his lineage is established. And the grandfather, the father's father, is like the father when he is absent, even if by legal consideration due to lack of capacity – contrary to the descendant if he claims a child of his ancestor's slave-girl, it is not valid except with the ancestor's confirmation. Among them: jihad is not permissible except with their permission, contrary to ancestors – their jihad does not depend on the permission of descendants. Among them: travel is not permissible except with their permission if the road is dangerous; otherwise, if he is not bearded [i.e., a minor], then likewise; otherwise no. Among them: if one of his parents calls him during prayer, it is obligatory to respond unless he knows that he is in it. And I have not seen the ruling for grandparents. It is appropriate to analogize. Among them: it is disliked for him to perform Hajj without the permission of either parent if he needs their service. Among them: the permissibility of the ancestor disciplining his descendant. The apparent view is that it is not exclusive to the father; so the mother, grandparents are likewise. I have not seen that now. Among them: the descendant follows the ancestor in Islam. And we have written the issues of the grandfather and what takes the father's place in it in the art of al-Fawa'id. Among them: they are not imprisoned for the debt of the descendant, and likewise grandparents. And the male ancestors are specified with the obligation of providing sexual satisfaction. And the father and grandfather are specified with rulings: among them: guardianship of wealth; so there is no guardianship for the mother over the minor's wealth except for preservation and purchasing what is necessary for the minor. Among them: contracting both sides of the transaction; so if the father sells his property to his son or buys from him without excessive fraud, it is valid with one utterance. Among them: the absence of option of puberty in the marriage contracted by the father and grandfather only. As for guardianship in marriage, it is not exclusive to them; it is established for every guardian, whether an asaba or a relative. Likewise the prayer over the funeral is not exclusive to them. And in al-Multaqat min al-Nikah: if the teacher strikes the child with the father's permission and he dies, he is not liable unless he strikes a blow that is not [customary].
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive compilation of qawaid (maxims) and their furuat (applications) concerning mahrams. The core definition: a mahram is one whose marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if the sexual act leading to that relationship was unlawful (zina). The text then lists numerous rulings that follow from mahram status: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel—with exceptions for breastfeeding mahrams (privacy is disliked) and young in-laws. It clarifies that temporary prohibitions (like li'an, different religion, triple divorce) are not permanent and thus not mahram. The husband shares some rights (looking, privacy, travel) with mahrams, but trustworthy women do not replace a mahram for travel. The passage then details specific rulings for three categories: (1) all mahrams by lineage, (2) ancestors and descendants specifically, (3) male ancestors only, and (4) father and grandfather only. Each category has unique rules: e.g., freeing of relative, maintenance obligation, prohibition of separating minor from mahram except in ten cases, no cutting of hand for theft between usul/furu, no execution of parent for child but vice versa, no hadd for slander of descendant, travel restrictions, establishment of lineage if ancestor claims, necessity of permission for jihad and travel, obligation to respond to parent's call in prayer, and many more. The author also notes gaps (e.g., grandparents' rulings) and suggests analogical extension. This is a classic example of how a single concept (mahram) branches into dozens of fiqh rulings across different chapters (jinayat, hudud, nikah, hajj, jihad, etc.). The Hanafi school's precise categorization is evident: mahram by breastfeeding does not carry all the same rulings as by lineage (e.g., privacy disliked).

Key Terms
الأصول (al-usul): Ancestors: parents, grandparents, and above.
الفروع (al-furu): Descendants: children, grandchildren, and below.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retributive justice; here, the rule that an ancestor is not killed for a descendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a descendant slanders his ancestor, what is the ruling?
A) Both are subject to hadd punishment
B) The ancestor is punished but not the descendant
C) The descendant is punished with hadd, but the ancestor is not
D) Neither is punished

Key Takeaway
Ancestors and descendants have a unique legal relationship with special rules in criminal, travel, jihad, and lineage matters that favor the ancestor's authority.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

Rulings Specific to Father and Grandfather: Guardianship and Marriage
Rulings specific to father and grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinct rulings that apply only to the father and grandfather, including financial guardianship over minors, the ability to contract both sides of a sale with one utterance, the absence of the option of puberty in marriage, and the obligation of i'faf for male ancestors.

Core Idea
The father and grandfather hold special financial and marital authority, including the exclusive right to marry off minors without option of puberty and the ability to execute a sale with one utterance, while the mother has only limited guardianship.

The Hanafi school grants the father and grandfather unique powers that other mahrams do not possess. This lesson explores their exclusive role in financial guardianship, marriage contracting, and the obligation to provide for the sexual needs of their descendants (i'faf).

Guided Path
1
Understand the exclusive powers of father and grandfather
The text specifies rulings that apply only to the father and the grandfather (who takes his place in his absence). These include guardianship of wealth (wilayat al-mal), the ability to contract both sides of a sale, and the absence of khiyar al-bulugh in marriage.
The mother does not have these powers; she only preserves and buys necessities.
2
Explain the financial guardianship
The father (and grandfather) have full guardianship over the minor's property. The mother's role is limited to preservation and purchasing what is necessary. She cannot sell or manage the property broadly.
This applies to both movable and immovable property.
3
Describe the rule of contracting both sides of a transaction
If the father sells his property to his son, or buys from his son, with one utterance (e.g., 'I sell you this for X' and acceptance is implied), the contract is valid as long as there is no gross fraud (ghaban fahish). This allows the father to act as both seller and buyer simultaneously.
This is not allowed for other guardians.
4
Explain the absence of option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh)
When a father or grandfather marries off a minor (whether son or daughter), the minor upon reaching puberty does not have the option to annul the marriage (khiyar al-bulugh). This is exclusive to the father and grandfather; other guardians' marriage contracts do have this option.
This is based on the father's superior judgment.
5
Discuss the obligation of i'faf (providing sexual satisfaction)
The male ancestors (father, grandfather, etc.) are obligated to provide for the sexual needs of their male descendants by enabling them to marry (e.g., paying for the wedding expenses). This is a distinct obligation (i'faf).
This is only for male ancestors, not female.

المحرم عندنا من حرم : بوطء حرام ; فخرج بالأول ولد العمومة والخؤولة وبالثاني أخت الزوجة وعمتها أو خالتها، وشمل أم المزني بها وبنتها وآباء الزاني وابنه.

Rulings on Mahrams: [A mahram is] one whose marriage is perpetually prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if [the sexual act] is unlawful. So the mahram according to us is one who is prohibited [from marriage] due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if through unlawful intercourse. Thus by the first [type] is excluded children of paternal uncles and aunts and maternal uncles and aunts; by the second [type] is included the sister of the wife, and her paternal aunt or maternal aunt; and it includes the mother of the one with whom one committed adultery, and her daughter, and the father of the adulterer and his son. And its rulings are: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel – except the mahram from breastfeeding, for privacy with her is disliked, and likewise with a young in-law; and permanent prohibition of marriage – no participation [in the prohibition] for the mahram in it; for the woman who is the subject of li'an becomes permissible if he retracts his accusation or becomes disqualified from testimony; and the Magian woman becomes permissible by Islam, or by her becoming a Jewess or Christian; and the thrice-divorced woman [becomes permissible] by the second husband's consummation and completion of her idda; and the wife of another [becomes permissible] by divorce and completion of her idda; and the woman in idda of another [becomes permissible] by completion of her idda. Similarly, there is no participation for the mahram in the permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel. As for her slave, he is like a stranger in the relied-upon view, but the husband shares with the mahram in these three, and trustworthy women do not take the place of the husband and mahram in travel. And the mahram by lineage is specified with rulings, among them: his freeing of his relative if he owns him, and this is not specific to ancestors and descendants; among them: the obligation of maintenance of the needy incapable relative by his wealthy relative, so he must be a mahram from the direction of kinship; so the cousin and the brother from breastfeeding are not freed, nor is his maintenance obligatory; and the mahram washes his female relative; among them: it is not permissible to separate a minor from his mahram by sale or gift except in ten cases which we mentioned in Sharh al-Kanz; if he separates, the sale is valid. Among them: the mahram relationship prevents returning a gift. And the ancestors and descendants are specified among other mahrams with rulings, among them: one of them is not cut off for stealing the property of the other; among them: one does not judge nor testify for the other; among them: the prohibition of each other's concubine even by adultery; among them: the prohibition of each other's wife merely by the contract; among them: they are not included in the will for relatives. And the ancestors are specified with rulings, among them: it is not permissible for him to kill his ancestor if he is a combatant except in self-defense; if he fears his return, he may restrict him and compel him so that someone else kills him; and he may kill his descendant if a combatant, like his mahram. Among them: the ancestor is not killed for the descendant, but the descendant is killed for the ancestor. Among them: the ancestor is not hadd-punished for slandering his descendant, but the descendant is hadd-punished for slandering his ancestor. Among them: the descendant may not travel except with the permission of his ancestor, without the reverse. Among them: if the ancestor claims a child of his son's slave-girl, his lineage is established. And the grandfather, the father's father, is like the father when he is absent, even if by legal consideration due to lack of capacity – contrary to the descendant if he claims a child of his ancestor's slave-girl, it is not valid except with the ancestor's confirmation. Among them: jihad is not permissible except with their permission, contrary to ancestors – their jihad does not depend on the permission of descendants. Among them: travel is not permissible except with their permission if the road is dangerous; otherwise, if he is not bearded [i.e., a minor], then likewise; otherwise no. Among them: if one of his parents calls him during prayer, it is obligatory to respond unless he knows that he is in it. And I have not seen the ruling for grandparents. It is appropriate to analogize. Among them: it is disliked for him to perform Hajj without the permission of either parent if he needs their service. Among them: the permissibility of the ancestor disciplining his descendant. The apparent view is that it is not exclusive to the father; so the mother, grandparents are likewise. I have not seen that now. Among them: the descendant follows the ancestor in Islam. And we have written the issues of the grandfather and what takes the father's place in it in the art of al-Fawa'id. Among them: they are not imprisoned for the debt of the descendant, and likewise grandparents. And the male ancestors are specified with the obligation of providing sexual satisfaction. And the father and grandfather are specified with rulings: among them: guardianship of wealth; so there is no guardianship for the mother over the minor's wealth except for preservation and purchasing what is necessary for the minor. Among them: contracting both sides of the transaction; so if the father sells his property to his son or buys from him without excessive fraud, it is valid with one utterance. Among them: the absence of option of puberty in the marriage contracted by the father and grandfather only. As for guardianship in marriage, it is not exclusive to them; it is established for every guardian, whether an asaba or a relative. Likewise the prayer over the funeral is not exclusive to them. And in al-Multaqat min al-Nikah: if the teacher strikes the child with the father's permission and he dies, he is not liable unless he strikes a blow that is not [customary].

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive compilation of qawaid (maxims) and their furuat (applications) concerning mahrams. The core definition: a mahram is one whose marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, marriage relationship, or breastfeeding, even if the sexual act leading to that relationship was unlawful (zina). The text then lists numerous rulings that follow from mahram status: prohibition of marriage, permissibility of looking, privacy, and travel—with exceptions for breastfeeding mahrams (privacy is disliked) and young in-laws. It clarifies that temporary prohibitions (like li'an, different religion, triple divorce) are not permanent and thus not mahram. The husband shares some rights (looking, privacy, travel) with mahrams, but trustworthy women do not replace a mahram for travel. The passage then details specific rulings for three categories: (1) all mahrams by lineage, (2) ancestors and descendants specifically, (3) male ancestors only, and (4) father and grandfather only. Each category has unique rules: e.g., freeing of relative, maintenance obligation, prohibition of separating minor from mahram except in ten cases, no cutting of hand for theft between usul/furu, no execution of parent for child but vice versa, no hadd for slander of descendant, travel restrictions, establishment of lineage if ancestor claims, necessity of permission for jihad and travel, obligation to respond to parent's call in prayer, and many more. The author also notes gaps (e.g., grandparents' rulings) and suggests analogical extension. This is a classic example of how a single concept (mahram) branches into dozens of fiqh rulings across different chapters (jinayat, hudud, nikah, hajj, jihad, etc.). The Hanafi school's precise categorization is evident: mahram by breastfeeding does not carry all the same rulings as by lineage (e.g., privacy disliked).

Key Terms
الإعفاف (al-i'faf): Obligation of male ancestors to provide for the sexual needs of their descendants (by enabling marriage).
خيار البلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): Option of puberty: the right of a minor who was married off by a guardian other than the father/grandfather to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fahish): Gross fraud or excessive overpricing/underpricing in a transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Father and grandfather have unique financial and marital authority, including full guardianship of wealth, the ability to contract with one utterance, and marriages without option of puberty, while male ancestors are obligated to provide for the marriage needs of their descendants.

The Grandfather is Like the Father: The Qawida and Its Exceptions
Defining the maxim and its exception clause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim that the grandfather is like the father in his absence, list the twelve exceptions, and distinguish between the correct (sahih) and invalid (fasid) grandfather.

Core Idea
The grandfather stands in the father's place except in twelve specific cases.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a critical Hanafi legal maxim: the paternal grandfather (al-jadd al-sahih) is treated like the father when the father is absent, but only in all rulings except for twelve particular exceptions. These exceptions are detailed in the inheritance section and involve distinctions between a 'true' grandfather and an 'invalid' one. Understanding this maxim is essential for applying inheritance and guardianship rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Identify the Arabic text of the qawida and its plain English meaning.
Memorize the Arabic: 'الجد كالأب عند فقده إلا في اثنتي عشرة مسألة'.
2
Define the term 'grandfather'
Recognize that it refers specifically to the paternal grandfather (father's father) and distinguish between al-jadd al-sahih (no female intervening) and al-jadd al-fasid (female intervening).
Only the sahih grandfather is covered by the maxim.
3
Note the exceptions
The text mentions twelve exceptions. While not listed here, they are documented in the fara'id chapters. Understand that these limit the maxim's application.
The exceptions are well-known in Hanafi fara'id.
4
Apply the maxim to the furu' example
The first sentence of the passage gives a furu': hitting a child with the mother's permission. If death occurs, the grandfather pays blood money, just like the father would.
This shows the maxim's scope beyond inheritance.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference between sahih and fasid grandfather affects inheritance shares and guardianship rights.
This distinction is critical for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يضرب مثله، ولو ضرب بإذن الأم غرم الدّية إذا هلك. والجد كالأب عند فقده إلا في اثنتي عشرة مسألة ذكرناها في الفوائد من كتاب الفرائض وذكرنا ما خالف فيه الجد الصحيح الفاسد .
He is hit like him, and if he hits with the mother's permission, he pays the blood money if the person dies. And the grandfather is like the father in his absence except in twelve matters which we mentioned in the benefits from the book of inheritance, and we mentioned what the correct grandfather disagreed with the invalid one.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage defines a general rule in Hanafi fiqh regarding hitting as a disciplinary measure. The text states that a person who is authorized to discipline a child (like a grandfather) is treated like the father in terms of liability: if he hits with the mother's permission, he must pay blood money if the child dies. It then introduces a key principle: the grandfather takes the place of the father when the father is absent, except for twelve specific exceptions that are detailed in the section on inheritance (fara'id). These exceptions are well-known among Hanafi jurists and involve differences between the 'true' grandfather (who is a paternal grandfather without an intervening female) and the 'invalid' grandfather (who has an intervening female).

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): The grandfather, specifically the paternal grandfather (father's father) in the context of inheritance and guardianship.
الجد الصحيح (al-jadd al-sahih): The 'correct' grandfather: a paternal grandfather with no female intervening in the lineage to the deceased (e.g., father's father).
الجد الفاسد (al-jadd al-fasid): The 'invalid' grandfather: a grandfather with a female intervening (e.g., mother's father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ten
B) Twelve
C) Fourteen
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The grandfather (paternal, sahih) is treated as the father under Hanafi law unless one of twelve specific exceptions applies.

Rulings Triggered by Disappearance of the Glans (Ghaybat al-Hashafa)
Comprehensive list of legal consequences of sexual intercourse in Hanafi fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify all legal consequences that arise from ghaybat al-hashafa and apply the Hanafi qawida that a single cause triggers multiple rulings across different fiqh chapters.

Core Idea
Disappearance of the glans triggers over 40 rulings across all fiqh chapters—a single cause with vast effects.

In Hanafi fiqh, the legal criterion for sexual intercourse (wat') that causes major impurity is the disappearance of the glans (ghaybat al-hashafa), not ejaculation. This single act triggers a cascade of legal consequences spanning acts of worship, family law, financial obligations, and criminal penalties. The passage before us enumerates these rulings systematically, providing a comprehensive reference for muftis. This lesson will help you internalize these rulings as a unified set stemming from one legal cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognize that ghaybat al-hashafa is the sole sabab for all listed rulings. Note that ejaculation is not required.
The cause is full insertion of the glans; partial insertion has no legal effect.
2
Categorize the rulings by fiqh chapter
Group rulings into: Ibadat (ghusl, prayer, fasting, hajj, etc.), Family Law (mahr, divorce, idda, mahram), Criminal Law (hadd, ta'zir), and Miscellaneous (removal from office, rejection of testimony).
This helps in memorization and ensures no ruling is overlooked.
3
Memorize using the list structure
The list is cumulative; start with the most immediate (ghusl) and work through each prohibition and obligation. Use mnemonic devices based on cause and effect.
For example: ghusl because janaba requires purification; prohibition of prayer because janaba prevents it.
4
Apply each ruling in context
For each ruling, ask: How does ghaybat al-hashafa specifically trigger it? Understand the link between the cause and the ruling.
E.g., obligation of mahr al-mithl because intercourse with shubha is akin to valid marriage.
5
Use as a fatwa reference
When issuing a fatwa involving wat', check this list to ensure no consequence is missed. The list serves as a quick reference.
This is especially important in complex cases involving multiple areas of fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام غيبوبة الحشفة يترتب عليها أحكام وجوب الغسل وتحريم الصلاة والسجود والخطبة والطواف وقراءة القرآن وحمل المصحف ومسه وكتابته ودخول المسجد وكراهة الأكل والشرب قبل الغسل ووجوب نزع الخُفْ. والكفَّارة وجوبًا أو ندبًا في أول الحيض بدينار وفي آخره بنصف دينار. وفساد الصوم ووجوب قضائة والتعزير والكفارة وعدم انعقاده إذا طلع الفجر مخالطًا وقطع التتابع المشروط فيه وفي الاعتكاف وفساد الاعتكاف، والحج قبل الوقوف والعمرة قبل طواف الأكثر، ووجوب المضي في فاسدهما وقضائهما، ووجوب الدم وبطلان خيار الشرط لمَن له وسقوط الرد بعيب إذا فعله المشتري بعد الاطلاع عليه مطلقا وقبله إن كانت بكرًا أو نقصها الوطء. ووجوب مهر المثل بالوطء بشبهة أو بنكاح فاسد وثبوت الرجعة به، وبيع العبد في مهرها إذا نكح بإذن سيده، وتحريم الربيبة وتحريم أصل الموطوءة وفرعها عليه، وتحريم أصله وفرعه عليها وحلّها للزوج الأول ولسيدها الذي طلقها ثلاثا قبل ملكها، وتحريم وطء أختها إذا كانت أمة وزوال العنة وإبطال خيار العتيقة وإبطال خيار البلوغ إذا كانت بكرا، وكمال المسمَّى، ووجوب مهر المثل للمفوضة وإسقاط حبسها نفسها لاستيفاء مهر معجل من مهرها على قولهما، ووقوع الطلاق المعتق به، وثبوت السنة والبدعة في طلاقها وكونه تعيينا في الطلاق المبهم وثبوت الفيء في الإيلاء، ووجوب كفَّارة اليمين لو كان بالله تعالى ووجوب العدة ومنع تزويجها قبل الاستبراء على قول محمد رحمه الله المفتى به ووجوب النفقة والسكنى للمطلقة بعده، ووجوب الحد لو كان زنا أو لواطة على قولهما وذبح البهيمة المفعول بها ثم حرقها، ووجوب التعزير إن كان في ميتة أو مشتركة أو موصى بمنفعتها أو محرم مملوكة له أو لواطة بزوجته، وثبوت الإحصان وثبوت النسب ووقوع العتق المعلّق به، واستحقاق العزل عن القضاء والولاية والوصاية وردّ الشهادة لو كان زنّا والله أعلم.
Rulings of the disappearance of the glans: there follow from it rulings: obligation of ghusl, prohibition of prayer, prostration, sermon, circumambulation, reading Quran, carrying the mushaf, touching it, writing it, entering the mosque, dislike of eating and drinking before ghusl, obligation of removing the khuff. And expiation (obligatory or recommended) at the beginning of menstruation with a dinar and at the end with half a dinar. And invalidation of fasting, obligation of making it up, ta'zir, expiation, and non-validity if dawn breaks while in state of junub, and breaking of the required continuity in fasting and i'tikaf, and invalidation of i'tikaf, and hajj before standing at Arafat, and umrah before the majority of tawaf, and obligation to continue in the invalid ones and make them up, and obligation of dam, and nullification of option of condition for the one who has it, and dropping of the right to return due to defect if the buyer does it after seeing it absolutely, and before if she was a virgin or the intercourse lessened her. And obligation of mahr al-mithl by intercourse with shubha or invalid marriage, and establishment of raj'ah by it, and sale of the slave for her mahr if she married with her master's permission, and prohibition of the stepdaughter (rabiba) and prohibition of the mother of the woman and her daughter upon him, and prohibition of his origin and branch upon her, and her permissibility for the first husband and for her master who divorced her thrice before she was owned, and prohibition of intercourse with her sister if she is a slave, and removal of impotence, and nullification of the option of the freed slave woman, and nullification of the option of puberty if she was a virgin, and completion of the named mahr, and obligation of mahr al-mithl for the woman with unspecified mahr (mufawwada), and dropping of her right to detain herself to receive immediate mahr from her mahr according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and occurrence of divorce suspended upon it, and establishment of the sunna and bid'a in her divorce, and it being a specification in ambiguous divorce, and establishment of fay' in ila', and obligation of expiation of oath if it was by Allah, and obligation of idda, and prohibition of marrying her before istibra' according to the fatwa of Muhammad, and obligation of maintenance and housing for the divorced woman after it, and obligation of hadd if it was zina or liwat according to them, and slaughtering the animal used for bestiality then burning it, and obligation of ta'zir if it was with a dead animal, or a shared one, or one whose benefit was bequeathed, or a mahram owned by him, or liwat with his wife, and establishment of ihsan, and establishment of lineage, and occurrence of suspended manumission upon it, and entitlement to removal from judgeship, governance, and guardianship, and rejection of testimony if it was zina. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an exhaustive enumeration of the legal effects (ahkam) that result from the disappearance of the glans (ghaybat al-hashafa), which is the Hanafi legal criterion for sexual intercourse (wat') that triggers major impurity (janaba) and numerous other rulings. The rulings are listed in a cumulative manner, covering acts of worship (ibadat) like ghusl, prohibition of prayer, fasting, hajj, and umrah; financial obligations like mahr, hadd, and kaffara; family law like mahram relationships, idda, and divorce; and social consequences like removal from public office. The passage serves as a comprehensive reference for scholars issuing fatwas, ensuring no consequence is overlooked. It reflects the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from a single cause (sabab) and applying them across all chapters of fiqh.

Key Terms
الحشفة (al-hashafa): The glans of the penis; its disappearance is the legal criterion for sexual intercourse causing janaba
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse defined by disappearance of the glans

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A single cause (ghaybat al-hashafa) triggers a multitude of rulings across all chapters of fiqh; muftis must master this list to issue comprehensive fatwas.

The General Rule: Anal Intercourse is Like Vaginal — with Exceptions
A qawida establishing the analogous status of anal intercourse with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule regarding anal intercourse and identify the specific exceptions where it differs from vaginal intercourse.

Core Idea
Anal intercourse is like vaginal for most rulings, but with specific exceptions where it is treated differently.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir lays down a crucial qawida: that anal intercourse is analogous to vaginal intercourse for most legal rulings, but then lists several exceptions where it diverges. Understanding this principle allows the mufti to apply consistent rulings across related cases.

Guided Path
1
State the General Qawida
The passage begins with the rule: anal intercourse is like vaginal intercourse for legal rulings. This establishes a default analogy.
2
Identify the Shared Rulings
List the rulings where anal intercourse is treated identically to vaginal: ghusl, prohibition (i.e., it is haram), invalidation of fasting, hajj, and i'tikaf, and establishment of raj'a.
These apply by agreement or according to the relied-upon view.
3
List the Exceptions
The passage then enumerates matters where anal intercourse differs: no musahara, no execution for first offense, no ihsan, no tahlil, no fay' for mawla, does not remove impotence, does not remove virginity, and is absolutely haram (unlike vaginal which is halal in marriage). Also in marriage: no mahr and no idda without khalwa.
Exceptions are prefaced with 'لا' or 'إلا'.
4
Understand the Rationale
The exceptions stem from the fact that anal intercourse is not the natural means of reproduction, so it does not create certain legal consequences like musahara or ihsan. The act itself is haram, but its effects are limited.
The qawida functions as a general rule with specific carve-outs.
5
Apply to Fatwa
When issuing a fatwa, the mufti must first apply the general analogy, then check if the case falls under any exception. For example, in a case of anal intercourse during fasting, the fast is invalidated (general rule), but no mahr is due after divorce if no khalwa occurred (exception).
The text explicitly marks some positions as 'على المفتى به'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة : الوطء في الدبر كالوطء في القبل فيجب به الغسل ويحرم به بالوطء في القبل ويفسد الصوم به اتفاقا واختلفوا في وجوب الكفَّارة؛ والأصح وجوبها، ويفسد الحج به قبل الوقوف على قولهما واختلفت الرواية على قوله؛ والأصح فساده به كما في فتح القدير. ويفسد به الاعتكاف وتثبت به الرجعة على المفتى به كما في التبيين إلا في مسائل : لا تثبت به حرمة المصاهرة، ولا يجب به عند الإمام إلا إذا تكرر فيقتل على المفتى به، ولا يثبت به الإحصان ولا التحليل للزوج الأول ولا فيء للمولى، ولا يخرج به عن العنة، ولا تخرج به عن كونها بكرا فيكتفي بسكوتها، ولا يحلّ بحال والوطء في القبل حلال في الزوجة والأمة عند عدم مانع وينبغي أن يسقط به خيار الشرط والعيب لقولهم بسقوطه بالتقبيل والمس بشهوة؛ فهذا أولاً للدلالة على الرضا وفي جامع الفصولين جامعها في دبرها بنكاح فاسد لا يجب المهر والعدة. (انتهى). فعلى هذا الوطء في الدبر لا المهر في النكاح الصحيح ولا تجب به العدة لو طلقها بعده من غير خلوة.
The third benefit: Anal intercourse is like vaginal intercourse; ghusl becomes obligatory by it, and it prohibits by vaginal intercourse, and it invalidates fasting by it by agreement, and they differed on the obligation of kaffara; the most correct is its obligation. And it invalidates hajj before standing according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the narration differed according to him (Abu Hanifa); the most correct is its invalidation by it as in Fath al-Qadir. And it invalidates i'tikaf, and raj'ah is established by it according to the fatwa as in al-Tabyin, except in matters: the prohibition of in-law relationship (musahara) is not established by it, nor is execution required according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) except if it is repeated, then he is killed according to the fatwa. And ihsan is not established by it, nor tahlil for the first husband, nor fay' for the mawla (husband in ila'), and it does not remove impotence, and she does not cease to be a virgin by it, so her silence suffices, and it is never permissible, while vaginal intercourse is permissible with wife and slave-girl when no obstacle exists. And it is fitting that the option of condition and defect be nullified by it, based on their ruling that they are nullified by kissing and touching with desire; this is foremost as an indication of consent. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: 'If he has intercourse with her in her anus in an invalid marriage, mahr and idda are not obligatory.' (End). Thus on this basis, anal intercourse in a valid marriage does not require mahr, nor does idda become obligatory if he divorces her after it without a valid seclusion (khalwa).
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a crucial benefit that clarifies the legal status of anal intercourse (wat' al-dubr) in Hanafi fiqh. The general rule is that it is like vaginal intercourse for most purposes: it requires ghusl, invalidates fasting, hajj, and i'tikaf, and establishes raj'a (right to take back during idda after revocable divorce). However, there are several exceptions where it differs: it does not establish the prohibition of musahara (in-law relationships), does not allow execution on the first occurrence (only on repetition), does not establish ihsan (for stoning in zina), does not make a woman permissible for the first husband via tahlil, does not fulfill a husband's fay' in ila' (vow of abstinence), does not remove the husband's impotence, does not remove a woman's virginity (so she can remain silent as consent in a marriage), and it is absolutely haram (unlike vaginal which is halal). Additionally, it does not obligate mahr in a valid marriage (since mahr is for vaginal intercourse) nor idda after divorce without valid seclusion. The passage also notes that anal intercourse likely nullifies the option of condition and defect because it indicates consent, analogous to kissing with desire.

Key Terms
الوطء في الدبر (al-wat' fi al-dubr): Anal intercourse, defined by insertion of the glans into the anus
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmat al-musahara): Prohibition of marriage between in-laws, e.g., mother-in-law, daughter-in-law
الإحصان (al-ihsan): Legal status of being married and having consummated, required for stoning penalty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Obligation of ghusl
B) Invalidation of fasting
C) Establishment of ihsan for stoning
D) Invalidation of i'tikaf

Key Takeaway
Anal intercourse is generally like vaginal for most legal purposes, but with specific exceptions that a mufti must know.

The Four Exceptions: Intercourse in Invalid Marriage vs. Valid
Four exceptions to the similarity rule for intercourse in invalid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four exceptions where an invalid marriage differs from a valid one regarding intercourse, and apply each rule to a concrete scenario.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, intercourse in a fasid marriage is generally like sahih, but four crucial exceptions affect mahr, haram, tahlil, and ihsan.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a concise qa'ida (legal maxim) with four specific exceptions. As a mufti, you must know when an invalid marriage triggers the same effects as a valid one, and when it does not. These distinctions impact dower, marital prohibitions, and even hudud punishments. Understanding these nuances is essential for accurate fatwa in marriage-related cases.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the baseline ruling: intercourse in an invalid marriage is like intercourse in a valid marriage in most effects (e.g., ghusl, 'idda, nasab). This is the foundation.
The general rule is the default; memorize it first.
2
List the four exceptions
Memorize the four matters where the rule does not apply: (1) mahr becomes mahr al-mithl, (2) prohibition (hurma) arises, (3) tahlil not valid, (4) ihsan not established.
Use the Arabic mnemonic: مهر الحرمة حل إحصان.
3
Explain the legal basis of each exception
For each exception, understand why the ruling differs. For example, mahr al-mithl is used because the specified mahr is not binding due to the invalid contract; the woman still deserves compensation. The prohibition (hurma) is immediate because the marriage is defective. Tahlil requires a valid marriage. Ihsan requires a valid marriage for its full effect.
Connect each exception to the underlying principle of the invalidity.
4
Apply the exceptions to a scenario
Given a hypothetical case (e.g., a woman married without witnesses, then intercourse occurs), determine which exceptions apply and what the ruling is.
Practice translating knowledge into case resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة : الوطء بنكاح فاسد كالوطء بنكاح صحيح إلا في مسائل : ١ - وجوب مهل المثل ولا يزاد على المسمى وفي الصحيح يجب المسمى . ٢ - الحرمة . ٣- عدم الحِلّ للأول . ٤ - عدم الإحصان به .
The fourth benefit: Intercourse in an invalid marriage is like intercourse in a valid marriage except in matters: 1) Obligation of mahr al-mithl and it is not increased beyond the named amount, while in valid marriage the named amount is obligatory. 2) The prohibition (of marriage to relatives). 3) Non-permissibility for the first husband (tahlil). 4) Non-establishment of ihsan by it.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This benefit succinctly compares intercourse in an invalid marriage (nikah fasid) to that in a valid marriage. In Hanafi fiqh, the general rule is that they are similar, meaning that most rulings (like obligation of ghusl, idda, etc.) apply equally. However, there are four exceptions: 1) The mahr (dower) is mahr al-mithl (mahr of the woman's peers) rather than the specified amount, but the specified amount cannot be exceeded if it is less; in valid marriage the specified amount is binding. 2) Prohibition (haram) for the couple is more immediate as the marriage is invalid. 3) The woman does not become permissible for the first husband after triple divorce through tahlil (since the marriage was invalid). 4) Ihsan (being married and then committing zina leading to stoning) is not established because the marriage was invalid. This is a precise distillation from classical Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage contract that is defective in its conditions or pillars but meets the basic requirements of a contract, e.g., without witnesses
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equivalent dower of a woman of similar status, not the specified amount
الإحصان (al-ihsan): The state of being in a valid marriage, which affects the penalty for zina (stoning if muhsan)
التحليل (al-tahlil): The intervening marriage that makes a woman permissible for her first husband after three divorces

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four exceptions where an invalid marriage differs from a valid one?
A) Obligation of mahr al-mithl
B) Establishment of ihsan
C) Immediate prohibition (hurma)
D) Tahlil not valid

Key Takeaway
Intercourse in a fasid marriage generally mirrors a valid marriage, but four precise exceptions regarding mahr, hurma, tahlil, and ihsan must be remembered for correct fatwa.

The Maxim: Milk al-Yamin Rulings Mirror Marriage, with Two Exceptions
A maxim comparing milk al-yamin to nikah with furuat and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim governing intercourse with a slave-girl (milk al-yamin), enumerate the four analogous rulings, and identify the two exceptions (tahlil and ihsan).

Core Idea
Milk al-yamin creates most marriage-like prohibitions, but not tahlil or ihsan.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a concise legal maxim: intercourse with a slave-girl is analogous to marriage in establishing mahram relationships, istibra', and the prohibition of combining sisters. However, two key differences exist – tahlil and ihsan. Understanding this maxim is crucial for applying the correct rulings in cases of milk al-yamin, especially when comparing to nikah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
Recognize that the passage states a general rule: 'Intercourse by right hand possession has the same rulings as intercourse by marriage.' This is the qawida.
2
List the furuat (analogous rulings)
Extract the four specific rulings that are analogous to marriage: (1) the slave-girl becomes prohibited to the man's ascendants and descendants; (2) her ascendants and descendants become prohibited to him; (3) istibra' is obligatory; (4) combining her sister with her (in intercourse) is prohibited.
These are the applications of the qawida.
3
Identify the exceptions (istithna'at)
Note the two rulings where the analogy does NOT hold: tahlil (making a divorced woman permissible for her first husband) and ihsan (the state that triggers stoning for zina) are not established by milk al-yamin.
These exceptions are due to the nature of milk al-yamin as ownership, not a marriage contract.
4
Understand the rationale
Tahlil requires a valid marriage contract (nikah), which milk al-yamin is not. Similarly, ihsan (the full legal capacity for stoning) requires a valid marriage contract; a slave-girl does not create a full marriage bond.
The exceptions are rooted in the contractual difference between nikah and milk.
5
Apply the maxim to a new case
Given a scenario (e.g., can a man marry the sister of his slave-girl?), use the analogy: since combining sisters is prohibited in marriage, it is also prohibited here. For exceptions, test if the ruling involves tahlil or ihsan.
Practice makes this maxim a powerful tool for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة : للوطء بملك اليمين أحكام كأحكام الوطء بنكاح؛ فيوجب تحريمها على أصوله وفروعه، وتحريم أُصولها وفروعها عليه، ووجوب الاستبراء، وحرمة ضمّ أختها إليها. ويخالف الوطء بالنكاح في مسائل : لا يثبت به التحليل ولا الإحصان.
The fifth benefit: Intercourse by right hand possession (milk al-yamin) has rulings like the rulings of intercourse by marriage: it obligates her prohibition upon his ascendants and descendants, and the prohibition of her ascendants and descendants upon him, and the obligation of istibra' (waiting period after purchase), and the prohibition of combining her sister with her. And it differs from intercourse by marriage in matters: tahlil (making permissible for first husband) is not established by it, nor ihsan (for stoning).
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This benefit outlines the legal effects of intercourse with a female slave owned by the man (milk al-yamin, right hand possession). In Hanafi fiqh, such intercourse is largely analogous to intercourse in marriage regarding the establishment of mahram relationships: the slave becomes permanently prohibited to the man's father and sons (usul and furu'), and her mother and daughter become prohibited to him (just as with a wife). Istibra' (a waiting period to ensure the woman is not pregnant from a previous owner) is obligatory. Also, he cannot have intercourse with her sister simultaneously (like with two wives). However, two important differences are that: 1) Tahlil (making a divorced woman permissible for her first husband) is not achieved because that requires a valid marriage, not mere possession. 2) Ihsan (the state that makes a married person liable for stoning for zina) is not established, because a slave-girl does not create ihsan for the man in the way a wife does. This is a precise statement from Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ملك اليمين (milk al-yamin): Right hand possession, referring to a female slave owned by a man, with whom intercourse is permissible
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): A waiting period (usually one menstrual cycle) imposed on a newly purchased slave-girl to ensure she is not pregnant

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT established by intercourse with a slave-girl according to this passage?
A) Prohibition of her mother upon him
B) Obligation of istibra'
C) Tahlil for a previous husband
D) Prohibition of combining her sister with her

Key Takeaway
Intercourse with a slave-girl (milk al-yamin) mirrors marriage in establishing mahram and istibra', but not in tahlil or ihsan.

The Barrier Penetration Maxim in Hanafi Law
Listing legal effects and a rule about barrier penetration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim on barrier penetration to classify acts across fiqh chapters and identify when the condition of heat transfer is met.

Core Idea
A thin barrier does not change the ruling of intercourse as long as heat is felt.

In this passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, the author first lists several legal effects that become established through proven intercourse: ihsan, lineage, suspended emancipation, and disqualification from certain offices. Then he presents a general rule: a physical barrier does not affect the ruling of penetration provided that heat can be felt on the other side. This rule is taken from the chapter on tahlil (analysis of consequences) and applies to all chapters of fiqh. Understanding this maxim is essential for any mufti who needs to determine when the full effects of intercourse are triggered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed legal effects
Read the first part of the passage and note down the effects that become established when intercourse is proven: ihsan (status), lineage, emancipation suspended on intercourse, and removal from judiciary/guardianship/executorship/rejection of testimony if the intercourse was zina.
These effects span various chapters of fiqh, showing the wide scope of the rule.
2
Parse the qawida wording
Examine the Arabic 'لا فرق في الإيلاج بين أن يكون بحائل أو لا؛ لكن بشرط أن تصل الحرارة معه'. Break it down: 'lā farq' means no difference; 'bi-ḥā’il' means with a barrier; 'lākin bi-sharṭ' means but on condition; 'taṣil al-ḥarārah' means the heat reaches.
Pay attention to the restrictive clause introduced by 'lākin'.
3
Understand the condition of heat
The condition 'taṣil al-ḥarārah' (heat reaches) is crucial. The barrier must be thin enough that the sensation of heat transfers through it. If the barrier is thick or heat is not felt, the ruling of penetration does not apply.
This condition appears to be unique to the Hanafi madhhab.
4
Apply the qawida to other chapters
The passage states 'fatajrī fī sā’ir al-abwāb' (so it applies in all chapters). This means the rule is not limited to tahlil but governs any fiqh context where the occurrence of intercourse matters: ghusl, zina, talaq, ihsan, etc.
Think of a case in the chapter of ghusl: if a barrier is present but heat is felt, ghusl becomes obligatory.
5
Note the authority and mufta bihi status
The qawida comes from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, a later work of qawaid by Ibn Nujaym. It is part of the fatawa mutakhkhirin tradition. The mufta bihi position is that the rule applies with the heat condition.
The authority level is strong, as it is a general principle accepted by later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثبوت الإحصان وثبوت النسب ووقوع العتق المعلّق به، واستحقاق العزل عن القضاء والولاية والوصاية وردّ الشهادة لو كان زنّا والله أعلم. فوائد الأولى : لا فرق في الإيلاج بين أن يكون بحائل أو لا؛ لكن بشرط أن تصل الحرارة معه. هكذا ذكروه في التحليل؛ فتجري في سائر الأبواب.
And proof of ihsan, proof of lineage, occurrence of suspended emancipation, entitlement to removal from judiciary, guardianship, executorship, and rejection of testimony if it was for fornication, and Allah knows best. Benefits: First: There is no difference in penetration whether there is a barrier or not; but on condition that the heat reaches with it. Thus they mentioned it in the section on tahlil; so it applies in all chapters.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage opens with a list of legal effects that become established through proven intercourse: ihsan (status that requires stoning for zina), lineage, emancipation if suspended on intercourse, disqualification from holding certain offices, and rejection of testimony if the intercourse was zina. Following this, the first ‘benefit’ (fā’idah) presents a general legal rule: in determining the occurrence of intercourse, a physical barrier does not prevent the ruling as long as heat can be felt on the other side. This rule is cited from the chapter on tahlil (the analysis of legal consequences) and is applicable across all chapters of fiqh. The condition of heat transfer ensures that the barrier is thin enough that the sensation passes through.

Key Terms
الإيلاج (al-īlāj): The act of inserting the glans into the vulva or anus; legally, the minimum that triggers full rulings of intercourse.
الحائل (al-ḥā’il): A physical barrier between the male and female organs during intercourse, such as cloth or thin skin.
الحرارة (al-ḥarārah): The sensation of heat that must be felt for the barrier to be considered negligible in the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for penetration with a barrier to be legally equivalent to direct penetration?
A) The barrier must be made of cloth.
B) The heat must be felt on the other side.
C) The barrier must be removed immediately after.
D) The barrier must not exceed the thickness of a fingertip.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, barrier penetration with heat transfer is legally equivalent to direct penetration across all fiqh chapters.

What Rulings Are Established for the Glans Are Established for Its Amputated Equivalent
A universal rule about the legal effects of amputation of the glans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'ma thabata lil-hashafah...' to determine the legal status of a partially amputated glans in various fiqh rulings.

Core Idea
If the equivalent of the glans remains, its rulings remain; if not, none remain.

This lesson examines a precise legal maxim from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. The glans (ḥashafah) is the benchmark for rulings dependent on penetration in Hanafi fiqh. When amputation occurs, the key question is whether enough tissue remains to be considered equivalent. The maxim provides a clear criterion: rulings follow the glans as long as its size equivalent is present. This rule is essential for muftis dealing with physical anomalies and their legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Universal Rule
Extract the qawida from the Arabic: 'ما ثبت للحشفة من الأحكام ثبت لمقطوعها إن بقي منه قدرها'. This is the universal positive statement: rulings of the glans apply to the amputated part if the equivalent size remains.
The qawida is stated as a universal (kulliya), but the author notes he has not seen it explicitly transmitted.
2
Identify the Exception
Find the negative condition: 'وإن لم يبق منه قدرها لم يتعلق به شيء من الأحكام'. If less than the equivalent remains, no rulings attach at all.
This is the exception (istithnā') that defines the boundary of the qawida.
3
Understand the Rulings Affected
List the fiqh rulings that depend on the glans: (1) ghusl becoming obligatory after full penetration, (2) hadd (fixed punishment) for zinā requiring penetration, (3) expiration of iddah through intercourse, etc. All these apply if the equivalent of the glans remains.
Hanafi fiqh defines full penetration as disappearance of the glans; amputation changes the measure.
4
Apply to Fictitious Cases
Consider two scenarios: (a) a man loses the glans entirely but the remaining part is the same length as the original glans — the rulings still apply. (b) the remaining part is clearly shorter — then no rulings of penetration attach.
The assessment is based on size, not shape.
5
Note the Epistemological Note
The author says 'ويحتاج إلى نقل لكونها كلية ولم أره' — this rule is a universal but he has not seen a transmitted source. This alerts the mufti that the rule may be based on logical extension (qiyās) rather than direct naql.
In fatwa, such a rule is still operative as it is derived from the known fiqh principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية : ما ثبت للحشفة من الأحكام ثبت لمقطوعها إن بقي منه قدرها، وإن لم يبق منه قدرها لم يتعلق به شيء من الأحكام ويحتاج إلى نقل لكونها كلية ولم أره.
Second: Whatever rulings are established for the glans are established for its amputated part if the equivalent of it remains, but if the equivalent of it does not remain, no ruling attaches to it, and it needs transmission because it is a universal [rule] and I have not seen it.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This second benefit discusses the legal status of the glans (ḥashafah) when it is partially or fully amputated. In Hanafi fiqh, the glans is the defining measure for rulings that depend on penetration (e.g., ghusl, hadd, etc.). If only part is left, but it is at least the size of the original glans, then the same rulings apply. However, if less than that remains, the man is considered no longer capable of legal penetration; thus none of the rulings dependent on the glans apply. The author notes that this is a universal rule, but he has not seen it transmitted explicitly.

Key Terms
الحشفة (al-ḥashafah): The glans of the penis; the part whose entire disappearance defines legal penetration.
مقطوعها (maqṭūʿuhā): The amputated part of the glans.
قدرها (qadruhā): Its equivalent in size; the original measure of the glans.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida, what is the condition for the rulings of the glans to apply to the amputated part?
A) The amputated part must be exactly the same shape as the glans.
B) The amputated part must be at least the equivalent size of the original glans.
C) The amputated part must include the tip of the glans.
D) The amputated part must be fully functional.

Key Takeaway
The rulings of the glans survive partial amputation as long as the remaining part is equivalent in size to the original glans; otherwise, no rulings attach.

Intercourse Rulings Ignore Emission
A maxim stating that emission is not a condition for rulings tied to intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal maxim regarding intercourse and apply it to furuat in tahara and hudud.

Core Idea
Emission is irrelevant for rulings triggered by intercourse; penetration alone suffices.

This short yet powerful maxim eliminates emission as a condition for all legal effects tied to intercourse. Understanding this principle clarifies many Hanafi rulings across different chapters of fiqh, from ghusl to hadd punishments.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim verbatim
Memorise the Arabic text: كل حكم تعلق بالوطء لا يعتبر فيه الإنزال لكونه تبعا. Understand that it means: any ruling connected to intercourse does not require emission because emission is subsidiary.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim from Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.
2
Identify the scope
Note that this maxim applies to all rulings whose sabab (cause) is the act of intercourse itself. This includes ghusl, hadd for zina, iddah, ihsan, etc.
It does not apply to rulings whose cause is emission (e.g., ghusl from wet dream).
3
Apply to the given furuat
Work through the two examples provided: (1) Ghusl becomes obligatory by penetration even without emission. (2) Hadd for zina is established by penetration alone.
Both follow directly from the maxim's general statement.
4
Explain the rationale
Emission is considered subsidiary (tabi) because the primary legal cause is the act of intercourse (wat') defined as penetration of the glans. Emission may or may not occur, but the ruling is fixed once penetration occurs.
This aligns with the Hanafi definition of intercourse as contact of the two circumcised parts (iltiqa al-khitanan).
5
Confirm no exceptions
The maxim has no listed istithna'at (exceptions) in this text. However, remember that this maxim only covers rulings tied to intercourse itself; other rulings tied to emission (e.g., ghusl from ihtilam) are governed by a different maxim.
Be careful not to over-apply this maxim outside its scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادسة كل حكم تعلق بالوطء لا يعتبر فيه الإنزال لكونه تبعا .
Sixth: Every ruling that is related to intercourse does not consider emission because it is subsidiary.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This short principle is a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh: any legal effect that is linked to the act of intercourse (such as ghusl, hadd, iddah, ihsan, etc.) is triggered by penetration alone, regardless of whether ejaculation occurs. Emission is considered a subsidiary matter; the primary cause is insertion of the glans. This is consistent with the definition of intercourse in the school.

Key Terms
الإنزال (al-inzāl): Ejaculation; release of semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this principle, when does ghusl become obligatory?
A) Only after ejaculation
B) Only after penetration with emission
C) After penetration even without emission
D) Only when both partners are willingly

Key Takeaway
Emission is not a factor in any ruling that is triggered by the act of intercourse; penetration alone is sufficient.
