The Qawida: Intercourse Outside Ownership Requires Mahr or Hadd – Exceptions
Exceptions to a general qawida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qawida, list its seven exceptions from the text, and explain the legal rationale for each.

Core Idea
Every intercourse outside milk al-yamin triggers mahr or hadd, but seven exceptions exist where neither applies.

This passage presents the seventh and eighth benefits from a series of legal rules. The seventh benefit enumerates exceptions to the general principle that any intercourse outside slave ownership results in either mahr (if under a valid or defective contract) or hadd (if it constitutes zina). The eighth benefit extends the analysis to a case where a mortgagor permits the mortgagee to have intercourse with a mortgaged slave-girl. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for issuing correct fatwas on cases of irregular unions and shubha.

Guided Path
1
State the main qawida
Identify the general rule: 'لا يخلو الوطء بغير ملك اليمين عن مهر أو حدّ' – every intercourse outside slave ownership is not free from mahr or hadd.
This is the point of departure; the rest of the passage lists exceptions.
2
List the seven exceptions from the seventh benefit
Go through each numbered case: 1) Dhimmi woman married without mahr, then both convert, believing no mahr due. 2) A minor boy marries. 3) A non-muhsana woman marries without wali and willingly has intercourse with a slave. 4) A slave has shubha intercourse with his mistress. 5) Intercourse with a harbi woman. 6) Beneficiary of waqf with endowed slave-girl. 7) Seller with slave-girl before delivery.
The author notes he has not seen transmission for cases 5-7.
3
Analyze the legal basis for each exception
For each, consider why mahr and hadd are waived – conversion, minority, lack of muhsana status, shubha, or enemy status.
Shubha often negates hadd and sometimes mahr.
4
Note the eighth benefit and its implications
The case of mortgagee with permission: the author says no mahr is due, but he has not seen it transmitted, indicating it may be based on analogy.
This reinforces that the qawida is not absolute and requires careful ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : لا يخلو الوطء بغير ملك اليمين عن مهر أو حدّ إلا في مسائل : ١ - الذميَّة إذا نكحت بغير مهر مثلاً ثم أسلما وكانوا يدينون أن لا يجب مهر . ٢ - نكح صبي ٣ - زوج أمته من عبده فالأصح أن لا غير محصنة نكحت بغير ولي ووطئها طائعة؛ فلا حد ولا مهر. ٤ - وطء العبد سيدته بشبهة فلا مهر كذلك . ٥ - لو وطء حربية فلا مهر لها، ولم أره الآن. ٦ - الموقوف عليه إذا وطء الموقوفة ينبغي أن لا مهر، ولم أره الآن. ٧ - البائع لو وطء الجارية قبل التسليم إلى المشتري وهي في حفظي منقولة الثامنة : أذِنَ الراهن للمرتهن في الوطء فوطىء ظانًا الحلّ ينبغي ألأ مهر. ولم أره الآن. التاسعة : الذي يحرم على الرجل وطء زوجته مع بقاء النكاح الحيض والنفاس : والصوم الواجب وضيق وقت الصلاة والاعتكاف والإحرام والإيلاء والظهار قبل التكفير وعدة وطء الشبهة، وإذا صارت مفضاة اختلط قبلها ودبرها فإنه لا يحلّ له إتيانها حتى يتحقق وقوعه في قبلها، وفيما إذا كانت لا تحتمله لصغر أو مرض أو سمنه، وعند امتناعها لقبض معجّل مهرها لم يحل ،كرها وفي بعض كتب الشافعية أنه يحرم وطء من وجب عليها قصاص وليس بها حبل ظاهر لئلا يحدث حمل يمنع من استيفاء ما وجب عليها . العاشرة : إذا حرم الوطء حرمت دواعيه ؛ إلا في الحيض والنفاس والصوم لمَن أمن فتحرم في الاعتكاف والإحرام مطلقا والظهار والاستبراء. الحادية عشرة : إذا اختلف الزوجان في الوطء فالقول لنا فيه إلا في مسائل : مع يمينه إلا إن كانت ادَّعى العنين الإصابة وأنكرت وقلن ثيب، فالقول له بكرا ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون قبل التأجيل أو بعده. ٢ - المولى إذا ادعى الوصول إليها قبل مضي المدة قبل قوله بيمينه لا بعد مضيها .
Seventh: No intercourse is free of mahr or hadd except in cases: 1 - A dhimmī woman who married without mahr, then both became Muslim, and they believed that no mahr is due. 2 - A boy (saghīr) married... (continued with more cases). Eighth: If a mortgagor permitted the mortgagee to have intercourse, and he had intercourse thinking it was permissible, it seems no mahr is due. Ninth: That which is prohibited for a man to have intercourse with his wife while marriage remains: menstruation, postpartum bleeding, obligatory fast, narrow time of prayer, i'tikaf, ihram, ila', zihar before expiation, iddah of shubha intercourse, and if she becomes mufdāh (fistula?) vagina and anus become mixed... Tenth: If intercourse is prohibited, its preliminaries are also prohibited except in menstruation, postpartum, and fast for those who are safe. Eleventh: If the spouses differ about intercourse, the word is with the one who [affirms] except in cases: [details].
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is dense and covers the remaining فوائد from seventh to eleventh. The seventh benefit lists exceptions to the rule that every intercourse outside of ownership results in either mahr (if under a valid or fasid marriage) or hadd (if zina). The eighth benefit discusses a case where a mortgagor permits the mortgagee to have intercourse with the mortgaged slave-girl. The ninth benefit enumerates prohibitions of intercourse with one's wife while the marriage is intact, including menstruation, fasting, i'tikaf, etc. The tenth benefit extends the prohibition to preliminaries, with exceptions. The eleventh benefit discusses whose testimony is accepted when spouses dispute whether intercourse occurred. The passage ends abruptly in the middle of a phrase about the master (mawlā) claiming access. The OCR seems to have merged these فوائد into one block; I will separate them.

Key Terms
الوطء بشبهة (al-waṭ’ bi-shubhah): Intercourse under a mistaken belief of legality, e.g., mistaking a woman for one's slave.
ملك اليمين (milk al-yamīn): Ownership of a slave (concubine).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the seventh benefit, which of the following is an exception to the rule that intercourse outside milk al-yamin requires mahr or hadd?
A) A free woman married without mahr and then both convert
B) A man's intercourse with a slave-girl he owns
C) Intercourse in a valid marriage
D) Intercourse with a woman who is menstruating

Key Takeaway
The qawida that intercourse outside milk al-yamin always triggers mahr or hadd has several exceptions, particularly where shubha or special status (like dhimmī or minor) negates the penalty.

Prohibitions of Intercourse within Marriage
Enumeration of prohibitions within marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the prohibitions of intercourse with one's wife while marriage is intact, and distinguish between those that also forbid preliminaries and those that do not.

Core Idea
Many states prohibit marital intercourse; some also prohibit its preliminaries, while others allow preliminaries to avoid temptation.

This passage, comprising the ninth and tenth benefits, details the situations in which a husband is prohibited from having intercourse with his wife despite the continuation of the marriage contract. It also clarifies when the prohibition extends to acts leading up to intercourse (دوافع الوطء) and when it does not. Understanding these nuances is essential for issuing correct fatwas regarding marital relations.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibitions from the ninth benefit
Identify each prohibition: menstruation, postpartum bleeding, obligatory fast, narrow time of prayer, i'tikaf, ihram, ila', zihar before expiation, 'iddah of shubha intercourse, and cases of fistula/obstruction.
Some are natural states, others are religious acts.
2
Note the additional prohibitions from Shafi'i sources
The author mentions that some Shafi'i books add prohibition when the wife is subject to qisas (retaliation) and not pregnant, to avoid preventing the qisas by pregnancy.
This is not part of the Hanafi position but shows cross-madhhab awareness.
3
Apply the tenth benefit: distinction of preliminaries
The rule: if intercourse is prohibited, its preliminaries are also prohibited, except in menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and fast (for those who are safe from temptation). In i'tikaf, ihram, zihar, and istibra', preliminaries are also absolutely prohibited.
The exception is based on necessity to avoid greater harm (temptation).

Source Text

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā’): An oath by a husband to abstain from intercourse with his wife for a period of at least four months.
الظهار (al-ẓihār): A pre-Islamic form of divorce by which a husband declares his wife to be like his mother's back; intercourse is prohibited until expiation.
الاستبراء (al-istibrā’): A waiting period to verify that a female slave is not pregnant before allowing intercourse with a new owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Menstruation
B) Fast
C) I'tikaf
D) Postpartum bleeding

Key Takeaway
Marital intercourse is prohibited in numerous states; the prohibition of preliminaries is absolute in some cases (i'tikaf, ihram, zihar, istibra') but not others (menstruation, postpartum, fast).

Disputes About Intercourse: Whose Word is Accepted?
Rules for resolving disputes about intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the spouse affirming intercourse is believed except in specific exceptions, and identify those exceptions.

Core Idea
In disputes over whether intercourse occurred, the word is with the one who affirms it, except when the husband claims impotence or the mawlā claims access after the period.

This passage, the eleventh benefit, addresses procedural rules when spouses disagree about the occurrence of intercourse. The general rule is that the testimony of the spouse who affirms intercourse is accepted, with a qasam (oath). However, there are exceptions: when the husband is claimed to be impotent, or when a mawlā (master claiming return to a slave-girl) asserts access before the period of abstinence expires. Understanding whose word is given precedence is crucial for resolving disputes regarding iddah, mahr, and custody.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
When spouses differ about whether intercourse occurred, the word is with the one who affirms it (القول له) and he/she takes an oath.
This is the default position.
2
Identify the exceptions listed
Two exceptions: (1) If the wife claims the husband is impotent and he denies impotence but asserts he had intercourse, while she denies it and she is a thayyib (non-virgin), then the word is with him if she is a virgin. (2) If a mawlā claims he had access to his slave-girl before the period of istibra' (waiting period) passes, his word is accepted with oath only before the period ends; after it ends, his word is not accepted.
The text is partially garbled but the gist is clear.
3
Analyze the rationale
In the first exception, the virginity status affects the credibility. In the second, the time frame limits the acceptability of the claim.
These rules avoid contradictory testimonies and preserve legal certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : لا يخلو الوطء بغير ملك اليمين عن مهر أو حدّ إلا في مسائل : ١ - الذميَّة إذا نكحت بغير مهر مثلاً ثم أسلما وكانوا يدينون أن لا يجب مهر . ٢ - نكح صبي ٣ - زوج أمته من عبده فالأصح أن لا غير محصنة نكحت بغير ولي ووطئها طائعة؛ فلا حد ولا مهر. ٤ - وطء العبد سيدته بشبهة فلا مهر كذلك . ٥ - لو وطء حربية فلا مهر لها، ولم أره الآن. ٦ - الموقوف عليه إذا وطء الموقوفة ينبغي أن لا مهر، ولم أره الآن. ٧ - البائع لو وطء الجارية قبل التسليم إلى المشتري وهي في حفظي منقولة الثامنة : أذِنَ الراهن للمرتهن في الوطء فوطىء ظانًا الحلّ ينبغي ألأ مهر. ولم أره الآن. التاسعة : الذي يحرم على الرجل وطء زوجته مع بقاء النكاح الحيض والنفاس : والصوم الواجب وضيق وقت الصلاة والاعتكاف والإحرام والإيلاء والظهار قبل التكفير وعدة وطء الشبهة، وإذا صارت مفضاة اختلط قبلها ودبرها فإنه لا يحلّ له إتيانها حتى يتحقق وقوعه في قبلها، وفيما إذا كانت لا تحتمله لصغر أو مرض أو سمنه، وعند امتناعها لقبض معجّل مهرها لم يحل ،كرها وفي بعض كتب الشافعية أنه يحرم وطء من وجب عليها قصاص وليس بها حبل ظاهر لئلا يحدث حمل يمنع من استيفاء ما وجب عليها . العاشرة : إذا حرم الوطء حرمت دواعيه ؛ إلا في الحيض والنفاس والصوم لمَن أمن فتحرم في الاعتكاف والإحرام مطلقا والظهار والاستبراء. الحادية عشرة : إذا اختلف الزوجان في الوطء فالقول لنا فيه إلا في مسائل : مع يمينه إلا إن كانت ادَّعى العنين الإصابة وأنكرت وقلن ثيب، فالقول له بكرا ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون قبل التأجيل أو بعده. ٢ - المولى إذا ادعى الوصول إليها قبل مضي المدة قبل قوله بيمينه لا بعد مضيها .
Seventh: No intercourse is free of mahr or hadd except in cases: 1 - A dhimmī woman who married without mahr, then both became Muslim, and they believed that no mahr is due. 2 - A boy (saghīr) married... (continued with more cases). Eighth: If a mortgagor permitted the mortgagee to have intercourse, and he had intercourse thinking it was permissible, it seems no mahr is due. Ninth: That which is prohibited for a man to have intercourse with his wife while marriage remains: menstruation, postpartum bleeding, obligatory fast, narrow time of prayer, i'tikaf, ihram, ila', zihar before expiation, iddah of shubha intercourse, and if she becomes mufdāh (fistula?) vagina and anus become mixed... Tenth: If intercourse is prohibited, its preliminaries are also prohibited except in menstruation, postpartum, and fast for those who are safe. Eleventh: If the spouses differ about intercourse, the word is with the one who [affirms] except in cases: [details].
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is dense and covers the remaining فوائد from seventh to eleventh. The seventh benefit lists exceptions to the rule that every intercourse outside of ownership results in either mahr (if under a valid or fasid marriage) or hadd (if zina). The eighth benefit discusses a case where a mortgagor permits the mortgagee to have intercourse with the mortgaged slave-girl. The ninth benefit enumerates prohibitions of intercourse with one's wife while the marriage is intact, including menstruation, fasting, i'tikaf, etc. The tenth benefit extends the prohibition to preliminaries, with exceptions. The eleventh benefit discusses whose testimony is accepted when spouses dispute whether intercourse occurred. The passage ends abruptly in the middle of a phrase about the master (mawlā) claiming access. The OCR seems to have merged these فوائد into one block; I will separate them.

Key Terms
العنين (al-‘anīn): A man who is impotent, unable to have intercourse.
المولى (al-mawlā): Here, the master of a slave-girl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eleventh benefit, in which of the following situations is the general rule (accepting the affirmative spouse's word) NOT applied?
A) Wife denies intercourse, husband affirms
B) Husband claims intercourse, wife denies, and she is a virgin
C) Mawlā claims intercourse with slave-girl after the period
D) Both spouses agree intercourse occurred

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedural rule for spousal disputes about intercourse is that the affirmative party's word is accepted with oath, but exceptions exist for impotence claims (especially with virginity) and for timing of claims by a mawlā.
